# C+ — Plan

A systems language in the same domain as C — close to the metal, no runtime — with the well-known C footguns removed and Rust-level memory safety. LLVM backend.

C+ is **AI-native**: tooling and structured information are first-class from the early phases, not a Phase-9 afterthought. Compiler-as-library, structured diagnostics, deterministic builds, a single canonical formatter, a built-in test runner, and an LSP all land alongside the language itself — so AI agents (and humans using AI tools) get maximum signal from day one. See §5.

---

## 1. Foundational decisions (settled)

### 1.1 C compatibility

**ABI-compatible only.** C+ emits standard object files; the system linker stitches them together with C-compiled objects. C source is never compiled by `cpc`.

The only language-level interop primitive is `extern fn`:

```cp
extern fn printf(fmt: *u8, ...) -> i32;
extern fn malloc(size: usize) -> *u8;
```

Header consumption (libclang-based bindgen) is a **separate future tool** (`cpc-bindgen`), not a language feature. It emits `.cp` files containing `extern fn` declarations that get committed to the consumer's repo. Same shape as Dart `ffigen`, Rust `bindgen`, Swift's clang importer-as-tool. Not on any phase plan; built when hand-writing bindings becomes painful, possibly never.

**Not** source-compatible. Existing `.c` files do not compile.

### 1.2 Other foundations

- **Compiler implementation language: Rust.** Good LLVM crates, modern tooling, already installed.
- **Comptime: out.** No comptime evaluator. `const fn`-style bounded compile-time evaluation, generics via type params + interfaces (monomorphization), and `print` as a compiler intrinsic. Same shape as Rust minus macros. No comptime expansion of language semantics; spec stays small.
- **Ownership tracking: full borrow checker, phased in.** Move semantics in Phase 3, shared borrows + lifetime inference in Phase 5, exclusive borrows + aliasing-XOR-mutability rule + explicit lifetime annotations in Phase 6. Delivers Rust-level memory safety: use-after-free, double-free, data races, iterator invalidation all caught at compile time. **No `&T` / `&mut T` syntax.** Borrowing is expressed by parameter form: `x: T` is a shared borrow, `mut x: T` is an exclusive borrow, `move x: T` transfers ownership; receivers follow the same shape (`self` / `mut self` / `move self`). The borrow checker enforces aliasing-XOR-mutability around the `mut` keyword, not around a reference type. See §2.9 for the full value-passing model and [docs/design/phase3-ownership.md](docs/design/phase3-ownership.md).
- **Release-mode overflow: wrap.** Debug traps, release wraps (Rust/Go-style). Plain `+ - *` are checked in debug, modular in release. `+% -% *%` operators wrap regardless of build mode (documents intent). Division by zero traps in both modes (always).
- **Memory model: C11 + borrow checker.** Atomics are library types `Atomic[T]` with explicit memory-ordering parameters (`Relaxed`, `Acquire`, `Release`, `AcqRel`, `SeqCst`), backed by compiler intrinsics. Data races on non-atomic memory are compile errors via the aliasing-XOR-mutability rule; the C11 "data race is UB" clause is structurally unreachable in safe C+. `unsafe` blocks can construct races, in which case C11 UB applies. Volatile access via `read_volatile` / `write_volatile` functions, not a type qualifier.

---

## 2. Settled design

### 2.1 Types

- Fixed-width integers only: `i8 i16 i32 i64 u8 u16 u32 u64 isize usize`. No `int`, no `long`.
- Floats: `f32`, `f64`.
- Real `bool`. No implicit int conversion.
- Real `enum`. No implicit int conversion.
- Tagged unions / sum types as a distinct construct, with pattern matching and exhaustiveness checking.
- Slices `T[]` are fat pointers (`ptr + len`). Indexing is bounds-checked; raw pointer escape hatch available.
- Strings: length-prefixed UTF-8 `string` type. Separate `cstring` for C interop.
- Pointers non-null by default. Nullable opt-in: `?*T`. Forced narrowing at use site.
- Explicit casts only: `as` or `@cast`. Implicit narrowing forbidden. Mixed signed/unsigned comparison forbidden or warned.

### 2.2 Memory and resources

- Manual memory management. No GC.
- Allocator passed as a parameter wherever allocation happens (Zig pattern).
- `defer` for scope-bound cleanup. Runs on scope exit including early returns.
- Definite assignment required — reading an uninitialized variable is a compile error.

### 2.3 Arithmetic

- `+ - * /` trap on overflow in debug; wrap (modular) in release.
- `+% -% *%` wrap regardless of build mode. Use to document intent and to get predictable wrapping in debug too.
- Division by zero traps in all build modes.

### 2.4 Errors

- **Errors are values, not control flow.** No exceptions, no unwinding, no `try`/`throw`/`catch`.
- Functions that can fail return a tagged union (`enum FileResult { Ok(i32), NotFound, ... }`).
- **No `try` / error-propagation operator, no `!T` magic type.** Even as pure sugar over an implicit early-return-on-error (Zig-style, no runtime cost), it signals "this function has non-value error flow" to binding consumers. The FFI honesty principle (§2.8b) rules it out. Function signatures stay literal — what the source says is what the ABI carries.
- **Pattern-match sugar at the call site is allowed.** `if let` and `guard let` (slice 4A.5) desugar to plain `match` in an early lowering pass; the resulting function signatures, return values, and ABI are identical to what the user would have written with hand-rolled match. This is in a different category from `try`/`!T`: signatures don't lie, no hidden control-flow contract crosses the FFI boundary, and the desugar is locally visible to any reader. See [docs/design/phase4-pattern-let.md](docs/design/phase4-pattern-let.md).
- Pre-Phase-3 plan had `!T` + `try`. Removed in favor of plain tagged unions (slice 3H). The verbosity of chained `match` was addressed in slice 4A.5 by `if let`/`guard let` sugar — *not* by reintroducing error machinery.

### 2.5 Modules

- Real module system. No preprocessor.
- One file = one module. Imports are path strings with mandatory `as` prefix (`import "math.cplus" as math;`). No headers, no `mod` declarations, no filesystem-derived namespace hierarchy.
- Same-file references see everything; cross-file references go through the import prefix (`math::Item`).
- No glob / no narrowing form. One import mechanism.
- Declarations and definitions live together. See [docs/design/phase4-modules.md](docs/design/phase4-modules.md) for the full design.

### 2.6 Standard library

**Out of scope for this plan.** A stdlib is necessary for real programs but is a separate follow-on project, written *in* C+ once the language compiles. This plan covers only the language and its compiler.

The one exception is `println(n: i32)` in Phase 1 — that's a *compiler intrinsic* (the codegen emits a direct `printf` call), not a stdlib function. The eventual proper formatted-print facility will replace it.

### 2.7 Removed from C

- Preprocessor (no `#include`, `#define`, `#ifdef`)
- `gets`, `strcpy`, `sprintf`, other unbounded variants
- Implicit `int`
- K&R syntax
- Trigraphs and digraphs
- Comma operator (the expression-level form `a, b`). The `,` separator in argument lists, struct literals, and `for` headers stays.
- Variable-length arrays (probably)
- Implicit array-to-pointer decay

### 2.8b FFI honesty (locked in)

The principle behind §2.4's "no `try`": **no surface syntax that implies machinery the FFI boundary doesn't actually carry.** C+ is ABI-compatible with C (§1.1); a C+ function appears to a binding consumer (a Dart FFI generator, a Python ctypes wrapper, hand-written C glue) as a function returning some value. That value can be a tagged union — fine, just bits with a tag — but it must not be "a thing that propagates via unwinding" or "a thing the consumer's runtime needs to integrate with."

The lesson from C++: `throw` looks like flow control, but its actual contract requires a working unwinder. Languages binding to C++ can't catch C++ exceptions. The function's true signature doesn't match its source-level appearance, and the mismatch hurts every consumer. C+ rejects that pattern outright — even where the magic would be free at runtime (like Zig's `try`-as-sugar). Source code reads the way the ABI behaves.

This principle gates future syntax additions. Anything that introduces hidden control flow at function call boundaries is out. Anything that's "just a value at the ABI level" is in regardless of surface form (e.g., `?*T` nullable pointers — see §2.1 — map to a plain pointer-that-might-be-null, exactly what C has; the narrowing is sema-only and doesn't cross FFI).

### 2.8c Verbosity exposes hidden rules; sugar exposes structure (locked in)

C+ is optimized for **LLM-as-primary-writer** and human-readable LLM output. The principle has two directions, both grounded in the same goal — locally-complete source — and both apply simultaneously:

- **Verbosity is acceptable when it makes a hidden rule visible.** Explicit `return` over tail expression (§2.8a), explicit `match` arms over `try` (§2.4 + §2.8b), `move`/`mut` markers at every parameter (§2.9), no overloading or operator overloading (§2.8). Every one of these prefers typing more characters to importing an unstated rule, because LLMs (and humans reading LLM output) win when the source carries its own meaning.
- **Sugar is acceptable when it makes structure visible.** Slice 4A.5's `if let` / `guard let` is the canonical example: chained fallible `match` blocks bury the success path under boilerplate and force the reader to mentally diff each arm — verbosity that *hides* the flow rather than exposing a rule. The pattern-binding sugar exposes the flow (`guard let Ok(x) = ... else { return ... };` reads top-to-bottom) and desugars to existing `match` IR with no FFI implication.

Both directions reduce to the same test: **does the syntax help a reader who lacks context understand what the code does?** If yes, prefer it. If no, prefer the alternative regardless of character count.

This principle is recorded so future feature debates don't relitigate it.

### 2.8a Style rules (locked in)

These are syntactic preferences settled after Phase 2. They apply to all C+ code in samples, tests, and future features.

- **Explicit `return` at function-body level.** No implicit tail-expression return — `fn f() -> i32 { 0 }` is rejected (E0333). `fn f() -> i32 { return 0; }` is correct. Block expressions still work in `let` initializers, assignments, and return-expression positions: `let x: i32 = if c { 1 } else { 2 };` is fine; `return if c { 1 } else { 2 };` is fine. Only the function-body-tail is forbidden.
- **Precise function names.** No "abbreviated semantics" where a name lies. `magnitude` means `sqrt(x²+y²)`; the squared form is `magnitude_squared`. Optimize for AI/LLM readability: the name tells the truth.
- **No `&` syntax. Values + `mut` markers.** Method receivers are `self` (read-only) or `mut self` (mutable). Both lower to a `ptr` parameter at the LLVM level; user never writes `&`. The borrow checker (Phase 5/6) will enforce aliasing-XOR-mutability around the `mut` keyword, not lifetime-typed references. Non-receiver parameter mutability (`mut x: T`) is deferred to Phase 3+.
- **`::` for type/namespace, `.` for instance.** Strict separation. `Color::Red`, `Point::new(3, 4)` use `::`. Field access `p.x` and method calls `p.method()` use `.`. Never mix.

### 2.9 Ownership and value passing (locked in)

This section captures the value-passing model in one place so future contributors don't have to reconstruct it from the Phase 3 design notes. See [docs/design/phase3-ownership.md](docs/design/phase3-ownership.md) and [docs/design/phase3-copy-derivation.md](docs/design/phase3-copy-derivation.md) for the full design rationale.

**No `&` syntax.** C+ does not have `&T` or `&mut T` reference types. The `&` token is not part of the language (the bitwise-and operator is unaffected; it only appears between expressions, never in types). Borrowing is expressed by *omitting* a marker on a parameter; the marker space is reserved for the non-default cases (`mut`, `move`). Receivers follow the same convention.

**Three parameter forms:**

| Surface | Semantics on non-`Copy` type | Semantics on `Copy` type |
|---|---|---|
| `x: T` | Shared borrow — function reads only; caller retains ownership; counted as a read by the borrow checker. | Pass-by-value copy; caller's value untouched. |
| `mut x: T` | Exclusive borrow — function may mutate; caller retains ownership; mutations propagate to the caller's place; counted as a write by the borrow checker. | Pass-by-value copy bound to a mutable local; caller's value untouched. |
| `move x: T` | Ownership transfer — caller gives up the value; using it after the call is E0335 (use-after-move). | `move` is silently accepted (E0336 lint will eventually suggest dropping it); the value is bit-copied; the source binding remains valid. |

The same three forms apply to method receivers: `self`, `mut self`, `move self`. `move` and `mut` on the same parameter is a parse error (E0334). Whether `x: T` / `mut x: T` is borrow-flavor or copy-flavor is determined by the `Copy`-ness of the *type*, not by syntax.

**`Copy` is structural.** A type is `Copy` iff every component is. Primitives + plain enums are atomic-`Copy`. Aggregates auto-derive (struct or array is `Copy` iff every field/element is). A struct with a `fn drop(mut self)` is forced non-`Copy`. The borrow checker only tracks non-`Copy` parameters; `Copy` values pass with no aliasing constraints.

**Return values always move.** `fn f() -> T` transfers ownership of the returned `T` to the caller binding. There is no return-side marker — moving is the only thing a return can semantically mean before lifetime annotations exist (Phase 6).

- For non-`Copy` types: the returned value is owned by the caller's binding after `return`. The producer's local that fed the `return` expression is consumed; the producer's frame holds nothing live for that slot. LLVM lowering depends on the ABI (small returns in registers, large aggregates via `sret`), but the C+-level semantics is uniformly "move."
- For `Copy` types: bitwise copy. The distinction is invisible at the source level because the producer's stack frame is gone by the time the caller observes the result. For `Copy` types it is mechanically a copy that fits the move shape.
- `return x;` where `x` is a non-`Copy` local moves `x` out of the local; it cannot then be read by a `defer` or by any later code (which is dead anyway).
- `return EXPR;` where `EXPR` constructs a value (e.g., a struct literal) constructs that value in the return slot and transfers it. Same model.

**Call sites carry no markers.** `f(x)` is the syntax regardless of whether `f` borrows or consumes `x`. The signature tells the story; the borrow checker emits a precise error at the use-after-move site if the caller misuses the value. A future style lint may warn when a `move`-parameter call doesn't write `f(move x)`, but that is opt-in style enforcement, not a language requirement.

**Borrow-checker mapping for Phase 5/6:**
- Phase 5 tracks the *shared* borrow form — `x: T` on non-`Copy` types. Many readers are fine; conflicts with `mut`/`move` of the same place.
- Phase 6 tracks the *exclusive* borrow form — `mut x: T` on non-`Copy` types. At most one at a time; conflicts with everything else.
- Aliasing-XOR-mutability is enforced against the `mut` keyword on parameters, not against a separate reference type system.
- LLVM `noalias` attaches to the underlying pointer parameter for `mut x: T` on non-`Copy` types once Phase 6 lands.

### 2.8d Attributes are declarative-only (locked in at Phase-5 kickoff)

C+ adopts `#[...]` attribute syntax as a *general* extension point for declarative metadata about an item — but **attributes carry no expression-level compile-time computation.** They are read by tools (the test runner, the optimizer hint pipeline, future doc generators) or by codegen as flags; they do not generate code, transform the AST, or run user-written logic at compile time. This is the line that keeps §2.8's anti-decorator / anti-macro / anti-comptime stance intact while admitting that some metadata is real.

The discriminating test: does the attribute's effect *write a function body* or *rewrite the surrounding declaration*? If yes, it's a decorator — out, per §2.8. If the attribute only flips a flag the compiler reads, it's metadata — in.

Examples:
- ✅ `#[test]` — marks a fn for `cpc test` discovery. No code generated; the runner sees a flag. Phase 5.
- ✅ `#[inline]` — hint to the optimizer. Codegen reads the flag and adds the LLVM `inlinehint`. No code generated.
- ✅ `#[repr(C)]` — changes struct layout. Codegen reads the flag and uses the C ABI. No code generated.
- ✅ `#[deprecated("use X instead")]` — diagnostic warning on use. Tool reads the flag.
- ❌ `#[derive(Eq)]` — synthesizes method bodies. That's a decorator; rejected. When Phase 7's interface system lands, `Copy` / `Eq` / `Drop` etc. derive *structurally* (same approach already used for `Copy` in §2.9), not via `#[derive(...)]`.
- ❌ `#[cfg_attr(...)]` — conditional compilation that emits attributes is meta-attribute machinery; rejected.

This decision also resolves the Phase 5 `#[test]` design carry-forward in §11: the syntax is `#[test]`, not `test fn`. Reason for picking attributes over a marker keyword: every future "this item is special" marker (`#[inline]`, `#[repr(C)]`, `#[deprecated]`, FFI calling-convention overrides) is near-certain to land before Phase 11, and burning a keyword per marker is the wrong direction.

Each *new* attribute requires its own design note per §6, and the note must justify why the attribute is declarative-only. The first time someone proposes a transforming attribute, the answer is no — and the principle gets restated here.

### 2.8 Won't add (deliberate non-features)

These are popular in modern languages but are out of scope for C+. AI-friendliness, locality of reasoning, and small spec are the rationale.

- **No function overloading.** A function with a given name has exactly one signature. AI sees `frobnicate(x, y)` and the function is the function — no overload resolution.
- **No operator overloading.** `+ - * /` work only on built-in numeric types. User types use named methods (`v.add(w)`). Smallest language; no surprise dispatch.
- **No `any`-type or dynamic-typing escape hatch.** The type system is load-bearing. AI-written TypeScript is plagued by stale `any`/`as`; C+ refuses to admit the failure mode.
- **No implicit type conversions.** Already covered in §2.1 — explicit `as` casts only.
- **No macros, no decorators, no compile-time AST transformation.** Already covered by no-preprocessor + no-comptime.
- **No glob imports as a default.** Each `use` names what it brings in; project linting can ban glob imports entirely. (Detail in Phase 4 module design.)
- **No inheritance.** Composition + interfaces only. (Detail in Phase 7.)
- **No `try` operator, no `!T` error union type.** Errors are tagged unions; users write `match` at every fallible call site. See §2.4 + §2.8b for rationale (FFI honesty + LLM-as-primary-writer).

---

## 3. Phased implementation

Each phase ends with a working compiler that handles strictly more programs than the previous one. Do not polish earlier phases at the expense of moving forward.

### Phase 0 — Repo and toolchain · 1–2 weeks · ✅ done

- Compiler implementation language: Rust.
- Cargo workspace; later split into `cplus-core` library + `cpc` binary (per §5.1).
- Hand-written LLVM IR ([cpc/src/hello.ll](cpc/src/hello.ll)) that prints `hello, world` via `printf`. Driver writes IR to a temp file and invokes `clang` for assemble+link.
- E2E test harness in place ([cpc/tests/e2e.rs](cpc/tests/e2e.rs)): 4 tests, all passing.

**Exit met:** `cargo test` passes; hand-written IR produces a runnable binary.

### Phase 1 — Tracer bullet · 3–6 weeks · ✅ done

Minimum viable end-to-end pipeline. Grammar fully specified in [docs/design/phase1-grammar.md](docs/design/phase1-grammar.md).

Language subset:
- Function definitions
- `i32` only (plus `bool` for conditions)
- Locals with type inference (`let` / `let mut`)
- Arithmetic on `i32` with overflow trapping in debug, wrap in release; division-by-zero traps in both modes
- `if`/`else` (statement and expression), `while`
- C-style and range-based `for`
- `return`, function calls, short-circuiting `&&` / `||`
- Compiler intrinsic `println(n: i32)` lowered to `printf("%d\n", n)`

Compiler components — all green:
- [x] **Library/binary split** ([cplus-core/](cplus-core/), [cpc/](cpc/)) per §5.1
- [x] Lexer + spans + sample programs ([cplus-core/src/lexer.rs](cplus-core/src/lexer.rs), [docs/examples/](docs/examples/)) — 14 unit tests
- [x] Recursive-descent parser → AST ([cplus-core/src/parser.rs](cplus-core/src/parser.rs), [cplus-core/src/ast.rs](cplus-core/src/ast.rs)) — 13 unit tests
- [x] **Structured diagnostics infrastructure** ([cplus-core/src/diagnostics.rs](cplus-core/src/diagnostics.rs), [docs/design/diagnostics.md](docs/design/diagnostics.md)) — 8 unit tests; `cpc --diagnostics=json|short|human` wired through CLI
- [x] **Name resolution + type checker** ([cplus-core/src/sema.rs](cplus-core/src/sema.rs)) — 14 error codes E0300–E0313, 29 unit tests covering every design-note §7.2 rejection plus happy-path positives
- [x] **AST → LLVM IR codegen** ([cplus-core/src/codegen.rs](cplus-core/src/codegen.rs)) — `alloca`+`mem2reg` strategy; debug-mode overflow trapping via `llvm.{sadd,ssub,smul}.with.overflow.i32` + `llvm.trap`; always-on division-by-zero check; 19 unit tests
- [x] **Driver: `cpc FILE [-o OUT]`** ([cpc/src/main.rs](cpc/src/main.rs)) — full pipeline lex → parse → sema → codegen → temp `.ll` → invoke clang → binary. `cpc --emit-ll FILE` for IR inspection. `cpc --release` / `--debug` (default) selects build mode. 13 e2e tests including all four sample programs running end-to-end, runtime overflow trap verification, runtime div-zero trap verification, and release-mode wrap behavior.

Test count: **102 tests passing** (89 library + 13 e2e), zero warnings.

**Sample programs all run with correct output:**

| Program | Output |
|---|---|
| [factorial.cplus](docs/examples/factorial.cplus) | `3628800` |
| [fibonacci.cplus](docs/examples/fibonacci.cplus) | `6765` |
| [sum_range.cplus](docs/examples/sum_range.cplus) | `5050` |
| [c_for.cplus](docs/examples/c_for.cplus) | `45` |

**Grammar reservations** (no semantics yet, but the syntax must parse, per the lexer): `mut`, `move`, `unsafe`, plus future-keywords (`struct`, `enum`, `trait`, `impl`, `match`, `defer`, `import`, `pub`, `guard`, `break`, `continue`, `loop`, etc.). Reserving now avoids painful migrations later. (`break` / `continue` / `loop` were activated as real statements in slice 4-end alongside `while let`.) Note: `&T` / `&mut T` are **not** reserved — C+ has no reference types; ownership uses parameter-marker syntax (see §2.9).

**LLVM features used in this phase:** `alloca` for every local + `mem2reg` pass to promote to SSA (avoids hand-rolled SSA construction); `add`/`sub`/`mul`/`sdiv`/`srem`/`icmp`/`br`/`ret`/`call`/`xor`/`load`/`store`/`extractvalue`/`unreachable`; `llvm.sadd.with.overflow.i32` / `llvm.ssub.with.overflow.i32` / `llvm.smul.with.overflow.i32` for debug-mode overflow detection; `llvm.trap` for both overflow and divide-by-zero traps; `declare i32 @printf(ptr, ...)` for `println`.

**Deferred (not blocking Phase 2):**
- [ ] **AST/IR JSON dumps**: `cpc parse --json`, `cpc check --json`. AST nodes need `serde::Serialize` derive. No consumer needs them yet; pick up when a tool (LSP, formatter, external analyzer) requires it.

**Exit met:** all four sample programs compile and run end-to-end via `cpc FILE -o OUT`; sema rejects every design-note §7.2 case with a structured diagnostic; runtime overflow traps in debug, wraps in release; runtime division-by-zero traps in both modes; CI green at 102 tests.

### Phase 2 — Aggregates and full primitive types · 4–8 weeks · ✅ done (slice 2E deferred)

Structured as three slices:

#### Slice 1 — Full primitive types + explicit casts · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase2-types.md](docs/design/phase2-types.md).

- All integer types (`i8 i16 i32 i64 u8 u16 u32 u64 isize usize`) and floats (`f32 f64`)
- Per-family operator semantics: signed-int debug-overflow trap; unsigned wrap; float IEEE 754
- Per-type comparison predicates: `slt/sle` signed, `ult/ule` unsigned, `olt/ole` float
- Float `%` rejected (E0316). Float `/` doesn't trap on zero (IEEE inf/nan).
- Negate (`-`) rejected on unsigned types
- Explicit `as` casts: numeric ↔ numeric, `bool → integer` allowed; `* → bool` rejected (E0315)
- Literal type inference from declared type (`let x: u64 = 42` works); strict no-implicit-conversion otherwise
- 3 new sample programs: [mixed_ints.cplus](docs/examples/mixed_ints.cplus) (i64 + casts), [float_arith.cplus](docs/examples/float_arith.cplus) (f64), [unsigned.cplus](docs/examples/unsigned.cplus) (u64 in a `for` loop)
- Test count: **143 total** (127 library + 16 e2e), zero warnings

**LLVM features used:** `add/sub/mul/sdiv/udiv/srem/urem`; `fadd/fsub/fmul/fdiv/fneg`; `icmp slt/sle/sgt/sge/ult/ule/ugt/uge/eq/ne`; `fcmp olt/ole/ogt/oge/oeq/one`; `llvm.{sadd,ssub,smul}.with.overflow.{i8,i16,i32,i64}` for signed checked arithmetic; cast instructions `trunc`/`sext`/`zext`/`fptosi`/`fptoui`/`sitofp`/`uitofp`/`fpext`/`fptrunc`/`bitcast`.

#### Slice 2A — Plain enums + path expressions · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase2-enums.md](docs/design/phase2-enums.md).

- `enum Name { V1, V2, ... }` declarations (no payloads, no discriminators)
- Two-segment path expressions `Name::Variant` (foundation for Phase 4 modules and Phase 3 tagged unions)
- Sema: `Ty::Enum(EnumId)`; declaration-order indexing; cross-enum types are distinct (E0302)
- Equality on enums works; ordering rejected (use `as i32` if you want it)
- Cast `EnumValue as i32` allowed (yields variant index); `int as Enum` rejected (E0315 — needs runtime range check)
- 1 new sample program: [direction.cplus](docs/examples/direction.cplus)
- New error codes: E0317 (unknown variant), E0318 (duplicate variant)
- Test count: **162 total** (145 library + 17 e2e), zero warnings

**LLVM features used:** Each enum lowers to `i32`. `Color::Red` is the constant `i32 0`. Equality is `icmp eq i32`. `as i32` cast is a no-op (already i32).

#### Slice 2B — Structs (no methods) · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase2-structs.md](docs/design/phase2-structs.md).

- `struct Name { f: T, ... }` declarations (including empty `Empty {}`); fields in declaration order
- Struct literal: `Point { x: 1, y: 2 }` — must specify all fields, no extras, no duplicates
- Field read: `p.x` (postfix `.`)
- Field assignment: `p.x = 5` — sema walks the Field chain to find the root mutable Ident; nested writes (`l.to.x = 5`) work
- Struct-literal-vs-block disambiguation: in head of `if`/`while`/`for-in <iter>`, an `Ident` followed by `{` is parsed as the cond/iter and the body block; force literal with parens
- Pass-by-value: structs as fn params and return types (`fn distance(a: Point, b: Point) -> i32`)
- Forward references: a struct field can name a type declared later in the file (two-pass collection)
- 3 new sample programs: [point.cplus](docs/examples/point.cplus), [mutable_struct.cplus](docs/examples/mutable_struct.cplus), [nested.cplus](docs/examples/nested.cplus)
- New error codes: E0319 (duplicate field), E0320 (unknown field on struct), E0321 (missing field in literal), E0322 (extra field in literal), E0323 (field access on non-struct). E0301 covers cross-type-namespace name collisions.
- Test count: **193 total** (173 library + 20 e2e), zero warnings

**LLVM features used:** `%Name = type { ... }` named-struct declarations in the preamble; `getelementptr` for field addressing; struct types as `define`-level params and return types (LLVM handles platform ABI lowering); aggregate `load`/`store` for whole-struct assignment.

#### Slice 2C — Methods on structs (`impl` blocks) · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase2-methods.md](docs/design/phase2-methods.md).

Resolved §11 open question on method syntax in favor of **Rust-style `impl` blocks** (over UFCS / no-methods): the borrow checker (Phase 5/6) needs receivers that express ownership, Phase 7 traits use the same `impl` syntax, and UFCS conflicts with the §2.8 no-overloading rule.

> Historical note: this slice originally landed with three receiver forms `self` / `&self` / `&mut self`. The post-Phase-2 §2.8a style migration removed `&` from the language; the current syntax is `self` / `mut self` (and `move self` since slice 3A). The list below has been updated to the current syntax. The original landing details live in the resolved-log entry at the bottom of §11.

- `impl Type { fn method(...) -> T { ... } }` blocks for inherent methods on structs
- Three receiver forms: `self` (shared borrow), `mut self` (exclusive borrow), `move self` (consumes — added in slice 3A). All three lower to a `ptr` parameter at LLVM level.
- Associated functions (no receiver): called as `Type::method(args)`
- Instance methods: called as `value.method(args)`
- `mut self` requires a writable place at the call site (sema enforces); `self` accepts any expression
- `self` inside method bodies is a special local: receiver kind determines mutability (`mut self` → mutable, `self` → immutable)
- LLVM name mangling: `Type::method` → `@Type.method` (using `.` separator — valid in LLVM, can't appear in C+ identifiers)
- New sample program: [methods.cplus](docs/examples/methods.cplus)
- New error codes: E0324 (no method on type), E0325 (impl on unknown/non-struct), E0326 (duplicate method), E0327 (wrong call form: instance-via-type or assoc-via-instance), E0328 (`mut self` call on non-mut place)
- Test count: **217 total** (196 library + 21 e2e), zero warnings

**LLVM features used:** function-name dot-mangling; `ptr` parameter type for all receivers (no extra alloca for the receiver param — bound directly to the SSA parameter, so `mem2reg` sees a clean pointer); struct types in `define`-level params still handled by aggregate ABI lowering where they appear.

#### Slice 2D — Fixed-size arrays · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase2-arrays.md](docs/design/phase2-arrays.md).

Scope decision: this slice handles **fixed-size arrays only**. Raw pointers `*T` and slices `T[]` interact directly with the Phase-5/6 borrow checker (shared/exclusive borrow tracking, fat-pointer semantics) and are deferred to Phase 3 or 5 where the same machinery is being built anyway.

- `[T; N]` fixed-size array type
- Array literal `[e1, e2, ...]` — element type uniform, length inferred from element count
- Indexing `a[i]` — runtime bounds check via `icmp uge` + `llvm.trap`; `i` must be `usize` (explicit `as usize` cast for `i32` loop counters)
- Indexed assignment `a[i] = v` — extends place-walk to Index chains; root mutability still required
- Pass-by-value as fn params and return types; arrays as struct fields
- **`Ty` refactor**: `Copy` → `Clone` to support `Box<Ty>` in `Ty::Array`. ~50 small `.clone()` insertions across sema and codegen. The right long-term model for generics and slices later.
- 2 new sample programs: [array_sum.cplus](docs/examples/array_sum.cplus), [array_struct.cplus](docs/examples/array_struct.cplus)
- New error codes: E0329 (mixed element types), E0330 (length mismatch), E0331 (indexing non-array), E0332 (empty array literal not supported)
- Test count: **236 total** (212 library + 24 e2e), zero warnings

**LLVM features used:** `[N x T]` array type; `getelementptr` for indexing (two-step: base GEP then element GEP); `icmp uge` + `br` + `call void @llvm.trap()` + `unreachable` for runtime bounds-check; array-as-aggregate parameter and return types.

#### Slice 2E — Slices + raw pointers · deferred to Phase 3 / 5

The original Phase-2 plan bundled raw pointers `*T` and slices `T[]` with arrays. After implementing arrays we realized: both depend on the borrow-tracking machinery that Phase 5/6 brings in. Doing them in Phase 2 means designing the pointer story twice. Deferred to land naturally alongside borrow checking. (Note: C+ never grew `&T` / `&mut T` reference types — borrowing is expressed via parameter form, per §2.9.)

**Phase 2 exit:** ✅ met — sample programs walk arrays of structs ([array_struct.cplus](docs/examples/array_struct.cplus)). Linked lists via raw pointers deferred to Phase 3/5 with the borrow-checker rollout.

### Phase 3 — Core safety + move semantics · 4–8 weeks · ✅ done

Structured as slices 3A–3J plus the bench sanity check. All landed; **the only Phase-3 work deferred is `?*T` and slices, both blocked on raw-pointer / borrow-checker machinery that arrives in Phase 5/6.**

#### Slice 3A — Ownership surface syntax + move tracking · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase3-ownership.md](docs/design/phase3-ownership.md).

- `move` reserved keyword
- Parameter ownership markers: `x: T` (shared, default), `mut x: T` (exclusive / mutable local), `move x: T` (consumes)
- Receiver ownership markers: `self` (Read), `mut self` (Mut), `move self` (Move); `mut move self` / `move mut self` rejected as parse errors
- Sema E0334: `mut` + `move` on same parameter is rejected
- Sema E0335: use of moved value
- Sema E0337: cannot move out of non-binding place (partial moves deferred to Phase 5/6)
- `Ty::is_copy()` — conservative Phase-3 rule: primitives + plain enums are `Copy`; structs and arrays are non-`Copy`. `Copy`-typed `move` params are silently allowed (a future E0336 lint will suggest removal).
- Move tracking is linear within the body (no flow-sensitive merging across branches; Phase 5 work). Only whole-binding moves through a `move` parameter or `move self` call are consumed; expressions used as `move`-args must be plain `Ident`s.
- 1 new sample: [ownership.cplus](docs/examples/ownership.cplus) — exercises all three receiver kinds; outputs `28\n7\n`
- Codegen lowering unchanged: receivers were already pointer-passed since the §2.8a migration, so `move self` works without further codegen work. The §3.1 design-note rule to pointer-pass non-Copy *parameters* is deferred to Phase 6 alongside `noalias` (rationale recorded in design note §7a).
- Test count: **263 total** (236 library + 27 e2e), zero warnings

**Pre-existing codegen limitation surfaced:** array literals like `[0u8, 0u8, 0u8, 0u8]` lower with `i32` element type regardless of suffix. ✅ fixed in slice 3D (literal-suffix codegen).

#### Slice 3B — Wrapping operators `+% -% *%` · ✅ done

- `+%`, `-%`, `*%` on integer operands emit plain `add`/`sub`/`mul` regardless of build mode (no overflow check, never trap, predictable modular semantics).
- Sema rejects wrapping ops on floats and non-numeric types (E0302).
- 1 new sample: [wrap_arith.cplus](docs/examples/wrap_arith.cplus) — exercises u8 / i8 / multiplication / underflow.
- Test count: **269 total** (240 library + 29 e2e), zero warnings.

#### Slice 3C — Copy auto-derive for aggregates · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase3-copy-derivation.md](docs/design/phase3-copy-derivation.md).

- Structural rule: a type is `Copy` iff every component is `Copy`. Primitives + plain enums atomic-Copy; arrays `Copy` iff element type is; structs `Copy` iff every field is.
- `Ty::is_copy()` removed (could not answer for structs without context); replaced by `SemaCx::is_copy(&Ty)`. Added `Ty::is_atomic_copy()` for the context-free atomic cases.
- New `is_copy: bool` flag cached per `StructDef`; computed by `compute_struct_copy_flags` between field collection and method collection. Fixpoint pass (monotone, converges in ≤ N iterations).
- Move tracking now gates correctly on `cx.is_copy(&ty)`: `move`-marked args and `move self` receivers consume their source only when the type is genuinely non-Copy.
- 1 new sample: [copy_struct.cplus](docs/examples/copy_struct.cplus) — primitive-only `Point` stays usable after a pass-by-value call.
- 5 new sema tests + 1 new e2e test (`copy_struct_runs`).
- **Slice-3A test rework (predicted in design note §6.3):** 6 sema tests + 2 e2e tests that used `struct B { x: i32 }` to exercise move tracking are now `#[ignore]`d, with a comment pointing to the design note. They revive when a non-Copy aggregate type exists in C+ (string, heap-typed, or explicit `nocopy` marker — none yet).
- The §3.1 design-note codegen pointer-pass rule for non-Copy params is still deferred to Phase 6 (`noalias`).
- Test count: **267 total** (239 library + 28 e2e), 6 ignored, zero warnings.

#### Slice 3D — Literal-suffix codegen fix · ✅ done

Pre-existing bug: codegen's `gen_expr` returned `Ty::I32` for *every* integer literal regardless of suffix. Two consequences:

- Array literals: `[10u8, 20u8, 30u8, 40u8]` had elements typed as i32, producing `[4 x i32]` SSA values that clang refused to store into the `[4 x i8]` destination.
- Arithmetic on suffixed literals: `1u64 +% 2u64` computed the add at i32 width and then tried to store the i32 result into an i64 slot — invalid IR.

Most existing samples accidentally worked because they fed unsuffixed literals into typed destinations (LLVM's textual numeric-literal operand position is width-polymorphic) or because they cast at use sites. Suffixed literals flowing into typed temporaries (array literals, arithmetic) hit the bug.

Fix: `gen_expr` now reads the literal's suffix and returns the corresponding `Ty`. Unsuffixed literals still default to `Ty::I32` (same as before). 2 new codegen regression tests.

#### Slice 3E — `Drop` design note · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase3-drop.md](docs/design/phase3-drop.md). Implementation landed in slice 3F.

#### Slice 3F — `Drop` implementation · ✅ done

- **Sema:** `is_drop` flag on `StructDef`; `collect_methods` detects the magic method name `drop` and validates the signature (`mut self`, no params, no return type — otherwise E0338); `compute_struct_copy_flags` short-circuits to `is_copy = false` for Drop structs.
- **Codegen:** mirrors the `is_drop` flag in `StructInfo`; `MethodInfo.params` / `FnSig.params` extended to carry the per-param `move_` flag. `FnState` gains `drop_scopes: Vec<Vec<DropEntry>>` parallel to the binding scopes. Per-binding `i1` drop flag in `entry:`, initialized to `true` at the binding's declaration site. Scope-exit emits conditional drop calls in reverse declaration order; `return` walks every live scope before the `ret` terminator. Call-site move events (`move`-marked args, `move self` receivers) flip the source binding's flag to `false`, suppressing scope-exit drop.
- **Destructor bodies** (methods named `drop`): receiver is *not* auto-registered as a Drop binding (would recurse). Other local Drop bindings inside the destructor body register normally.
- **`move self` methods:** receiver IS registered as a Drop binding in the method scope, so drop runs at end of the method.
- **Non-`move` non-receiver params:** *not* registered. Under the current aggregate-by-value ABI they'd double-drop. Phase 6 pointer-pass + borrow-checker will revisit.
- 2 new samples: [drop_basic.cplus](docs/examples/drop_basic.cplus) (reverse-order destruction; output `1\n2\n-2\n-1\n`), [drop_move.cplus](docs/examples/drop_move.cplus) (move suppresses caller drop; output `-7\n7\n`).
- 5 new sema tests + 2 new e2e tests for Drop itself.
- **Slice-3A tests revived (8 total):** 6 sema + 2 e2e tests previously `#[ignore]`d now pass cleanly because their structs gained `impl B { fn drop(mut self) {} }`, which makes them genuinely non-Copy.
- New error code: E0338 (wrong destructor signature). E0339 reserved but not yet emitted (Phase 3 `impl` is struct-only, so a drop-on-non-struct can't be expressed).
- Test count: **284 total** (252 library + 32 e2e), 0 ignored, zero warnings.

#### Slice 3G — `defer` · ✅ done

- `defer EXPR;` statement registers the expression to run at the enclosing scope's exit.
- **Lexical scoping** (not Go's runtime stack): a defer inside an `if` body fires at end of that body, not at function end. The expression is re-emitted at scope-exit time, so it reads each operand's final value (e.g. `defer println(x)` prints x's value at scope exit, not at the defer statement).
- **Unified scope-exit stack:** `defer` shares its LIFO stack with Drop calls (per Drop design note §4.4). The codegen previously had `drop_scopes: Vec<Vec<DropEntry>>`; now `scope_exits: Vec<Vec<ScopeExit>>` with `ScopeExit::Drop` and `ScopeExit::Defer` variants. Walked in reverse registration order at scope close and at `return`.
- 2 new samples: [defer_basic.cplus](docs/examples/defer_basic.cplus) (LIFO ordering through a `return`; output `1\n5\n4\n3\n2\n`), [defer_drop.cplus](docs/examples/defer_drop.cplus) (defer interleaved with Drop in registration order; output `1\n2\n200\n-2\n100\n-1\n`).
- 3 new sema tests + 2 new e2e tests.
- Test count: **289 total** (255 library + 34 e2e), 0 warnings.

#### Slice 3H — Tagged unions + `match` design note · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase3-tagged-unions.md](docs/design/phase3-tagged-unions.md). Implementation deferred to slice 3I. Highlights:

- Extend `enum` (don't add a new keyword): `enum Maybe { Some(i32), None }`. Plain enums stay the zero-payload special case with their cheaper bare-`i32` lowering.
- **Positional payloads** only in Phase 3 (`Variant(T1, T2)`); named-field payloads deferred. 1+ payload types per variant.
- **`match e { Pat => arm, ... }`** as an expression. Patterns: variant (with optional payload patterns), wildcard `_`, binding `x`. Payload patterns one level deep.
- **Exhaustiveness** enforced at sema (E0340).
- **Copy / move:** structural rule extends — tagged union is Copy iff all payload types are Copy. Same fixpoint machinery as struct Copy auto-derive (slice 3C).
- **Drop:** Phase 3 rejects tagged unions whose variant payloads are Drop (E0344). Users who need this write a manual `fn drop(mut self) { match self { ... } }`. Compiler-synthesized variant drop is a later slice (likely Phase 5+ alongside heap types).
- **LLVM layout:** plain enum → bare `i32`; mixed enum → `{ i32 tag, [N x i8] payload }` where N is max-payload-size across variants. Construction stores tag + bitcasts payload area; match emits `switch i32` + bitcast-load per arm.
- New error codes: E0340 (non-exhaustive), E0341 (pattern/scrutinee type mismatch), E0342 (wrong payload arg count), E0343 (literal pattern not supported), E0344 (Drop payload).
- **Held: error unions `!T` and `try`** — user has flagged these for design discussion. The note (§6.6) notes a possible lowering through tagged unions but commits nothing.

#### Slice 3I — Tagged unions + `match` implementation · ✅ done

Implementation of design slice 3H. The full surface ships:

- **AST:** `EnumDecl.variants: Vec<EnumVariant>` with each variant carrying `payload: Vec<Type>`. New `ExprKind::Match { scrutinee, arms }`. New `Pattern { Wildcard, Binding(Ident), Variant { enum_name, variant_name, payload } }`.
- **Parser:** variant payload syntax `Variant(T1, T2)`; `match e { pat => body, ... }` as a primary expression (block-arm and short-form `expr ,` both supported); patterns parse `_` / bare-ident binding / `Enum::Variant(payload_patterns)`.
- **Sema:**
  - `EnumDef` extended with `variants: Vec<EnumVariantDef>` (each carrying resolved payload types), cached `is_copy` flag, `is_tagged` flag.
  - Two new collection passes: `collect_enum_payloads` (after struct fields) resolves payload types; `compute_enum_copy_flags` (fixpoint, mirrors struct case) computes `is_copy` and enforces no-Drop-payload (E0344).
  - `SemaCx::is_copy(&Ty)` extended to consult `EnumDef.is_copy`. `Ty::is_atomic_copy` no longer treats enums as atomically Copy (the tagged case depends on payloads).
  - Variant construction routed through `check_assoc_call` — `Maybe::Some(42)` is a path-call shape; sema validates against the variant's payload arity / types. Payload-less variant called with parens → E0327 (use bare path).
  - `check_match`: scrutinee must be `Ty::Enum`; pattern checking via `check_pattern` adds payload-name bindings into the arm scope; exhaustiveness via tracked covered-set + catch-all flag; arm-type-uniformity via first-arm anchor.
- **Codegen:**
  - `EnumInfo` extended with `variant_payloads`, `is_tagged`, `payload_slots`. New collect pass after struct fields.
  - Plain enums (no payloads): keep Phase-2A bare-`i32` lowering.
  - Tagged enums: `%enum.N = type { i32, [PAYLOAD_SLOTS x i64] }` declared in preamble. Each payload value occupies one i64-aligned slot — Phase-3 simplification (wastes some bytes; guarantees alignment).
  - `gen_tagged_construct`: alloca, store tag, store each payload at slot index, load aggregate.
  - `gen_match`: load tag, emit `switch i32`, one labeled arm per variant; per-arm payload binding via GEP-into-slot + load with the payload's actual type; result slot allocated lazily on first value-producing arm.
  - `alloca_named` now uniquifies (`%name.addr<N>`) so a function param `s` and a match-arm binding `s` get distinct SSA names.
- 2 new samples: [maybe.cplus](docs/examples/maybe.cplus) (Option-equivalent; output `7\n-1\n`), [shape.cplus](docs/examples/shape.cplus) (multi-arg payloads; output `48\n60\n64\n0\n`).
- 11 new sema tests + 3 new e2e tests. New error codes E0340–E0344 now active.
- Test count: **303 total** (266 library + 37 e2e), 0 warnings.

#### Slice 3J — Definite assignment · ✅ done

`let x: T;` (no initializer) is now legal; sema verifies every read is preceded by an assignment on every control-flow path.

- **AST:** `Let.init: Option<Expr>` (was `Expr`).
- **Parser:** the `= EXPR` part is optional; `let mut? NAME : TYPE ;` parses without an initializer. The `for`-header `let` form still requires an init (the natural pattern; uninit there would be useless).
- **Sema:** new `assigned: bool` flag on `LocalInfo`. Initialized `true` for `let x = …`, `false` for `let x: T;`. Reads of an unassigned binding → **E0345**. An uninitialized `let` without a type annotation → **E0346** (sema can't infer the type).
- **Flow merging:** snapshot/restore/intersect helpers on the assigned-state vector. Applied at `if`/`else` (then-branch state intersected with else-branch state) and across every `match` arm. Conservative for `while`/`for` loops (the body may not run; bindings stay in whatever pre-loop state they had — same approach as Rust).
- **First-write-into-immutable rule:** the first write to a `let x: T;` (no `mut`) is allowed regardless of `mut` — it's the binding's initialization, not a reassignment. After that write, x is treated as immutable; further writes need `mut` (E0305 if not).
- **Codegen:** uninitialized `let` skips the store; the alloca lives. Drop bindings still register their scope-exit hook at the let site — sema rejects any path that reads-before-assign so the drop only fires after an actual assignment ran.
- 1 new sample: [uninit_init.cplus](docs/examples/uninit_init.cplus) — classifies a sign into -1/0/1 using a `let label: i32;` + nested-if pattern; output `1\n-1\n0\n`.
- 8 new sema tests + 2 new e2e tests.
- Test count: **313 total** (274 library + 39 e2e), 0 warnings.

**Phase 3 ✅ done.** All settled features land:
- Ownership surface syntax + move tracking (3A) · wrapping operators (3B) · Copy auto-derive (3C) · literal-suffix codegen fix (3D) · Drop (3E/3F) · `defer` (3G) · Tagged unions + `match` (3H/3I) · Definite assignment (3J)

Deferred to later phases: `?*T` and slices need raw-pointer / borrow-checker machinery (Phase 5/6).

#### Bench — clang-parity sanity check · ✅ done

Sanity benchmark proved `cpc --release` matches `clang -O2` on representative non-aliasing workloads. Findings: a missing `-O` flag in the clang invocation was making release binaries 100×+ slower than they needed to be; once `-O2` was wired through, all three benchmarks (sum, fib, arr) come in at 1.00× ± noise. Numbers and source code in [bench.md](bench.md). The "C+ beats C on aliasing" story is a Phase-6 promise; this benchmark only confirms we haven't pessimized anything.

**LLVM features used:** all overflow-with-intrinsic forms for the full integer type set; `llvm.trap` for division-by-zero and overflow traps; `switch` instruction for tagged-union `match`; `noundef` parameter attribute (definite-assignment + Drop-flag init guarantee well-defined initial state).

**Exit met:** all samples (factorial, fibonacci, sum_range, c_for, mixed_ints, float_arith, unsigned, direction, point, mutable_struct, nested, methods, array_sum, array_struct, ownership, wrap_arith, copy_struct, drop_basic, drop_move, defer_basic, defer_drop, maybe, shape, uninit_init) build and run correctly; double-free and use-after-move caught at compile time; read of unassigned binding caught at compile time; tagged unions provide the safe error-handling surface.

### Phase 4 — Modules + tooling foundations · 6–10 weeks · ✅ done

Modules and the first wave of project-level tooling. The pairing is intentional: a manifest, a formatter, and an LSP only make sense once the language has multi-file projects.

Design notes:
- [docs/design/phase4-modules.md](docs/design/phase4-modules.md) — **modules** (explicit path-string imports with mandatory `as` prefix; no filesystem-derived namespace; `pub` visibility default-private; `Cplus.toml` manifest; whole-program compilation in Phase 4 minimum). Error codes E0401–E0410.
- `cpc fmt` — design note pending.
- LSP foundations — design note pending.

**Slice plan (per the modules note §8 + the 4A.5 interstitial):**

- Slice 4A ✅ done: manifest loading + dependency-walking driver. Resolver rewrites cross-file paths to file-id-qualified names before sema; sema/codegen untouched.
- Slice 4A.5 ✅ done: `if let` / `guard let` pattern-binding sugar over `match`. New error codes E0347–E0352. Design note: [docs/design/phase4-pattern-let.md](docs/design/phase4-pattern-let.md).
- Slice 4B ✅ done: `pub` visibility + cross-file access checks (E0403). Per-file pub sets tracked in the resolver; same-file access ignores `pub`. Per-method pub on `impl` blocks; struct fields take individual `pub field: T` markers (field-pub enforcement deferred to sema in 4C). Enums export variants via the enum's pub (no per-variant flag).
- Slice 4C ✅ done: diagnostics polish + slice-4B carry-forward closed.
  - ✅ Sema-side **enforcement** of struct-field `pub` (sema fires E0403 with "field … is private" message on cross-file field reads and struct-literal field bindings).
  - ✅ **Parser polish** for cross-file struct literals (`prefix::Type { ... }`) — now parses; resolver E0403/Struct test uses the construction form.
  - ✅ **Per-file source threading** through sema — `check_multi` entry; cross-file diagnostics render against the originating file's path + line/col. New e2e test pins it.
  - ✅ **E0401–E0410 structured diagnostics + did-you-mean.** Resolver and manifest errors now flow through the same `Diagnostic` pipeline as sema (`--diagnostics=json|short|human`). E0401 carries a `MaybeIncorrect` suggestion proposing the closest existing `.cplus` filename within the importing file's directory (edit distance ≤ 2). Manifest E0406 covers parse/missing-field/unsupported-edition; E0407 covers manifest I/O and binary-entry-missing.
- Slice 4D ✅ done: `cpc fmt` — preserving formatter (slice 4D.1). Design note: [docs/design/phase4-fmt.md](docs/design/phase4-fmt.md). Every sample in `docs/examples/` round-trips clean. `cpc fmt FILE|DIR`, `--check`, `--emit`, `--stdin`. Reformatting heuristics (collapse incidental wraps, force multi-line on overflow) deferred to 4D.2.
- Slice 4E.1 ✅ done: `cpc-lsp` skeleton + live diagnostics. Design note: [docs/design/phase4-lsp.md](docs/design/phase4-lsp.md). New `cpc-lsp` binary linking `cplus-core`; stdio JSON-RPC via `lsp-server`; `cpc lsp` subcommand `exec`s it. Pushes diagnostics on `didOpen` / `didSave`, mapped from cplus-core `Diagnostic` to LSP `Diagnostic`. Single-file and project mode (walks up for `Cplus.toml` on each check).
- Slice 4E.2 ✅ done: `textDocument/formatting` wired to `fmt::format_source`; `textDocument/codeAction` lifts diagnostic suggestions into editor Quick Fixes (`isPreferred` set for `MachineApplicable`). Per-file cache of the last cplus-core diagnostic batch backs the code-action lookup. Manifest errors now surface via the diagnostic pipeline instead of being silently swallowed. Editor integration: minimal VS Code extension under [editors/vscode/](editors/vscode/) — declares the `cplus` language, ships a TextMate grammar for syntax highlighting (comments, strings, numbers with type suffixes, keyword categories, built-in + PascalCase types, function names at definition + call sites, operator categories), spawns `cpc lsp` via `vscode-languageclient`, runs in F5 dev-host mode or as a packaged `.vsix`. Settings: `cplus.cpcPath`, `cplus.trace.server`.
- Slice 4E.3 ✅ done: `textDocument/definition` handler. Re-lexes the buffer at the cursor to find the identifier, then scans the resolver's merged program for items whose qualified name's last segment matches; jumps to the declaration site. Works for `fn`, `struct`, `enum` items; single-file and project modes. 3 new e2e tests pin same-file jump, cross-file jump (click `square` in `math::square(7)` → `pub fn square` in `math.cplus`), and the no-match case (clicking a keyword returns empty).
- Slice 4-end ✅ done (bundle): closes the small carry-forwards from earlier slices.
  - **`break` / `continue` / `loop` / `while let`** — keywords already reserved at Phase 1; new `StmtKind::Break` / `StmtKind::Continue` / `StmtKind::Loop(Block)` / `StmtKind::WhileLet { pattern, scrutinee, body }`. Parser wires the new statement forms. Lowering pass rewrites `while let PAT = E { BODY }` into `loop { match E { PAT => { BODY; }, _ => break, } }`. Sema tracks `loop_depth`; `break` / `continue` outside a loop body → new **E0353**. Codegen pushes a `(continue_label, break_label)` stack at every loop entry; for-range and C-style for routes `continue` through a dedicated `step` block so the increment (or update list) runs before re-checking the condition. New sample [docs/examples/loops.cplus](docs/examples/loops.cplus) covers all four constructs.
  - **Cross-file variant patterns** — `match e { prefix::Enum::Variant(...) => ... }` now parses as a 3-segment variant pattern (parser collapses `prefix::Enum` into the `enum_name` field) and resolves via the resolver's pattern-rewrite using the import alias. Closes a 4A carry-forward.
  - **5-file sample project** [docs/examples/projects/calc/](docs/examples/projects/calc/) — exercises the Phase-4 modules story end-to-end: `ops` (pub fns), `expr` (pub enum), `eval` (cross-file variant patterns + pub-fn calls), `util` (cross-file enum-variant constructors), `main` (orchestrator). Builds via `cpc build`; prints `-14` for `(3 + 4) * (-2)`.

#### Slice 4A — Manifest loading + multi-file driver · ✅ done

- `import "path.cplus" as name;` declarations at the top of any file. String literal token + `import` keyword added to the lexer (E0005 unterminated-string). Parser collects imports into `Program.imports` before items; `import` after an item is a parse error. `prefix::Type` parses in type position (stored as `Path("prefix::Type")` until the resolver rewrites it).
- `Cplus.toml` minimum: `[package] name version edition` + optional `[[bin]] name path`. `toml = "0.8"` crate dep. Manifest loader [cplus-core/src/manifest.rs](cplus-core/src/manifest.rs) returns absolute `root` (canonicalized) so downstream consumers can derive file ids deterministically.
- Multi-file resolver [cplus-core/src/resolver.rs](cplus-core/src/resolver.rs): walks the import graph from the entry binary (BTreeMap-keyed for deterministic ordering), canonicalizes paths for cycle/dedup detection, parses every reached `.cplus` file, then rewrites each file's AST so item declarations and cross-file references use a file-id-qualified name. The entry binary's `fn main()` is the one un-prefixed item (linker entry point). Sema and codegen are unchanged — they see a single merged `Program` of qualified names.
- File id derivation: canonicalized path relative to the manifest root, `.cplus` stripped, `/` → `.`. `src/main.cplus` → `src.main`; items become `src.main.helper`, structs `src.main.Point`, methods `src.main.Point.new`.
- Driver: new `cpc build` subcommand (no file arg) reads `./Cplus.toml`, walks imports, links to `target/{debug,release}/<bin-name>`. New `cpc --emit-ll-project` mirrors `--emit-ll FILE` for multi-file projects.
- Resolver errors: E0401 import-not-found, E0404 cyclic import, E0405 duplicate `as` prefix, E0407 manifest binary entry doesn't exist. (E0402/E0403/E0408 are reserved for 4B.) Currently surfaced via the driver's plain stderr — full sema-style structured diagnostics integration is a 4C polish item.
- 1 new sample project: [docs/examples/projects/hello_mods/](docs/examples/projects/hello_mods/) — `main.cplus` imports `math.cplus` and calls `math::square(7)`; runs and prints `49`.
- Tests added: 8 lexer (`import` keyword + string literal), 5 parser (`import`-decl + qualified type path), 6 manifest, 7 resolver, 4 e2e (hello_mods build+run, missing manifest, E0401, E0404). Test total: **344** (301 library + 43 e2e), 0 warnings.

**Known limitations carried to 4B/4C:**
- No `pub` visibility yet — every item is reachable through its import prefix regardless of marker. (The `pub` keyword still parses, so writing it now is forward-compatible.)
- Cross-file diagnostics print without line/col mapping (sema gets only the entry file's source). Threading per-file source through sema is a 4B/4C task.
- Variant patterns from cross-file enums (`match e { prefix::Color::Red => ... }`) are not yet resolved; intra-file enum matches still work.
- Manifest's `[[bin]]` is limited to exactly one binary entry.

#### Slice 4B — `pub` visibility · ✅ done

Design driver: [docs/design/phase4-modules.md](docs/design/phase4-modules.md) §2.3.

Default-private. `pub` exports the named item across the import boundary; same-file access is unaffected regardless of marker (consistent with the design note: `pub` gates cross-file access only).

- Parser accepts `pub` prefix on `fn`, `struct`, `enum`, methods inside `impl` blocks, and individual struct fields. `pub impl` is rejected (per-method `pub` instead — `impl` blocks themselves carry no visibility).
- AST nodes gained `is_pub: bool`: `Function`, `StructDecl`, `EnumDecl`, `Method`, `StructField`.
- Resolver builds per-file public surface: `pub_items` (top-level `pub` names), `pub_methods` (per-type pub methods), `item_kind` (function/struct/enum tag — used to choose between method-pub vs variant-inherits-enum-pub on three-segment paths). Cross-file qualification now runs through `check_pub_item` and `check_pub_method` before rewriting; same-file rewrites skip the check.
- Enums export variants via the enum's pub (no per-variant flag, per design note §2.3).
- New error code: **E0403** — cross-file reference to a non-`pub` item. Variants: Function, Struct, Enum, Method.
- Sample [docs/examples/projects/hello_mods/](docs/examples/projects/hello_mods/) updated to use `pub fn square` and a private `double` helper (demonstrates that private items work intra-file without leaking).
- Tests added: 6 parser tests (pub on fn/struct/enum/method/fields + `pub impl` rejection), 6 resolver tests (E0403 for function, struct, method; same-file private OK; pub enum variants OK; private enum rejected), 2 e2e tests (E0403 from `cpc build`; same-file private builds and runs). Test total: **373** (323 library + 50 e2e), 0 warnings.

**Limitations carried to 4C:**
- Field-level `pub` is parsed but not yet *enforced*. Sema will enforce it once per-file source threading lands; until then private fields are practically as accessible as public ones once their containing struct is pub. Phase 4 doesn't have cross-file field access samples yet, so this is mostly a deferred check rather than a hole users can hit easily.
- Cross-file struct-literal construction (`prefix::Point { ... }`) still doesn't parse — the parser's path-vs-struct-lit disambiguation collides with two-segment names. The E0403 test for private structs uses type-position references to work around it. Parser polish in 4C.

#### Slice 4A.5 — `if let` / `guard let` · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase4-pattern-let.md](docs/design/phase4-pattern-let.md).

Motivation: slice 3H/3I made errors plain tagged unions (correct per §2.4 + §2.8b FFI honesty), but chained fallible operations buried the success path under three or four `match` blocks. That verbosity hurts human and LLM readability — it *hides* the flow instead of exposing a rule (§2.8c sharpening). `if let` / `guard let` are pattern-match sugar over the existing `match` machinery; the desugar is locally visible, function signatures don't change, and bindings consumers see ordinary tagged-union returns.

- New keyword: `guard`. (`if`, `let`, `else` already existed.)
- Two new statement forms — both lowered to existing `match` AST before sema:
  - `if let PAT = EXPR { BODY }` and `if let PAT = EXPR { BODY } else { ELSE }` — refutable pattern; bindings scoped to body.
  - `guard let PAT = EXPR else { ELSE };` and `guard let PAT = EXPR else |COMPLEMENT| { ELSE };` — else block must diverge; the pattern's binding lives in the *enclosing* scope past the statement. Single-binding patterns only in 4A.5 (multi-binding deferred via E0352).
- `while let` deferred — depends on `break`/`continue` not yet implemented as statements; lands in a later slice bundling `break`/`continue`/`loop`/`while let`.
- Implementation: parser emits `StmtKind::IfLet` / `StmtKind::GuardLet` AST nodes; new module [cplus-core/src/lower.rs](cplus-core/src/lower.rs) runs between parser and sema, emits slice-specific diagnostics, and rewrites these nodes to equivalent match-using forms. Sema and codegen panic on any surviving IfLet/GuardLet — they should never see one.
- Sema's match-arm type unification taught to skip syntactically-diverging arms (every path ends in `return` / nested match where every arm diverges) — without this, `guard let`'s else-diverges-anyway arm trips E0302 against the success arm's payload type.
- New error codes: E0347 (irrefutable `if let` pattern), E0348 (non-diverging guard-let else), E0349 (reserved for complement non-exhaustiveness once the dedicated check lands; currently delegated to slice-3I E0343 on the synthesized match), E0350 (complement pattern overlaps success pattern), E0351 (guard-let pattern binds nothing), E0352 (multi-binding deferred).
- 3 new samples: [if_let_basic.cplus](docs/examples/if_let_basic.cplus), [guard_let_chain.cplus](docs/examples/guard_let_chain.cplus), [guard_let_complement.cplus](docs/examples/guard_let_complement.cplus).
- Tests: 1 lexer (`guard` keyword), 9 lowering (refutability + diverge + multi-binding + complement-overlap + lowering correctness), 5 e2e (the 3 samples + 2 negative tests for E0347 and E0348). Test total: **359** (311 library + 48 e2e), 0 warnings.

**Limitations carried forward:**
- Single-binding patterns only (E0352 for multi-binding). Revisit when a real motivating example appears.
- `while let` deferred to the future `break`/`continue`/`loop` slice.
- Complement exhaustiveness is checked via the synthesized match's E0343 instead of a dedicated E0349 with guard-let-aware diagnostic text; tighten when ergonomics warrant.

#### Slice 4D — `cpc fmt` (preserving formatter, slice 4D.1) · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase4-fmt.md](docs/design/phase4-fmt.md).

Phase 4D ships a **preserving** formatter: the user's structural line breaks are kept; within-line whitespace and indentation are normalized; comments are preserved at their original lexical positions. The reformatting layer (collapsing incidental wraps, forcing multi-line on >100-column overflow) is slice 4D.2.

- **Lexer**: new `tokenize_with_trivia` entry point emits `TokenKind::LineComment(String)` / `BlockComment(String)` tokens instead of discarding comments. Existing `tokenize` keeps the comment-filtered contract intact.
- **`cplus-core/src/fmt.rs`**: token-stream printer. Walks the trivia-aware token stream and re-emits each token with a same-line spacing rule + brace-nested indent. Newlines come from counting newlines in the source byte gap between consecutive token spans. Continuation lines (mid-expression, not preceded by `;`/`{`/`}`/`,`/`=>`) preserve the user's literal leading whitespace so hand-aligned continuations like `return a + b\n             + c` survive.
- **Style decisions** (locked, no config): 4-space indent; K&R braces; one space around binary operators; tight `::`, `.`, `..`, `..=`; tight `|` (complement-pattern delimiter — `|` is not used as bitwise-or in any in-tree sample yet); trailing-comma policy follows the user; trailing comments preserve user-literal leading whitespace (slice 4D.1 exception to normalization — samples use multi-space alignment for trailing `// 49` style comments).
- **Driver**: `cpc fmt FILE|DIR ...` subcommand. Default rewrites in place. Flags `--check` (no write, unified diff to stderr, exit 1 on drift), `--emit` (print to stdout, file untouched), `--stdin` (read stdin → stdout). Directory mode recurses; `target/`, `node_modules/`, `.git/` skipped.
- **Sample-preservation invariant**: every `.cplus` file under `docs/examples/` round-trips identical through `format_source`. The lib test `each_sample_round_trips` enforces this; the e2e test `fmt_check_all_samples_clean` checks `cpc fmt --check docs/examples/` exits 0. (Two typo cleanups in `nested.cplus` — double-spaces around `Line` and `to:` — landed alongside this slice; not style decisions, just typos.)
- 9 new lib tests (`fmt::tests::*`): idempotence, comment preservation, operator/path spacing, blank-line collapsing, trailing-newline enforcement, full-sample round-trip. 6 new e2e tests (`fmt_stdin_normalizes`, `fmt_check_all_samples_clean`, `fmt_check_reports_diff`, `fmt_rewrites_in_place`, `fmt_emit_leaves_file_alone`, `fmt_idempotent_in_place`). Test total: **398** (334 library + 64 e2e), 0 warnings.

#### Slice 4E.1 — `cpc-lsp` skeleton + live diagnostics · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase4-lsp.md](docs/design/phase4-lsp.md).

The Language Server lands as a third binary in the compiler-as-library family. Editors get live diagnostics over the standard LSP stdio transport; the implementation is a thin wrapper over `cplus-core` — same pipeline `cpc build` uses.

- **New crate `cpc-lsp/`** alongside `cpc/`, both linking `cplus-core`. Deps: `lsp-server` + `lsp-types` (rust-analyzer family — sync, no tokio).
- **Transport**: stdio JSON-RPC. `cpc lsp` subcommand in the `cpc` binary discovers `cpc-lsp` next to itself (cargo build / install layout) or on `PATH`, then spawns it as a foreground child — error messages from the LSP propagate through stderr cleanly.
- **Capabilities advertised**: full-text-sync (`textDocumentSync.change = 1`); save notifications without text re-send; formatting + definition advertised as `false` (placeholder for 4E.2 / 4E.3 — clients gracefully gray these out).
- **Diagnostic triggers**: `didOpen` and `didSave`. Per-keystroke `didChange` does NOT recompute (full reparse on every keystroke would spike CPU; save-triggered fits the AI-iteration loop). Re-detect project root (`Cplus.toml` walk-up) on each check — single-file mode when no manifest is reachable.
- **Pipeline**: `lexer::tokenize` → `parser::parse` → `lower::lower` → `sema::check` (single-file) or `resolver::load_project` + `sema::check_multi` (project mode). Every C+ `Diagnostic` mapped mechanically to LSP `Diagnostic` (severity, `code` as string, 1-based → 0-based positions, `source = "cpc"`). Diagnostics grouped by originating file path so cross-file errors push to the right URI.
- **Connection-lifetime correctness**: `Connection` moved by value into the main loop (not borrowed) — its sender drops when the loop exits, which unblocks the io-thread writer and lets `io_threads.join()` return. Without this the server hangs after shutdown, which was the first integration-test failure caught here.
- **Clean exit on `shutdown` + `exit`** (LSP protocol normal close) and on EOF.
- **Tests**: 4 e2e tests drive the spawned binary with framed JSON-RPC and assert the responses — initialize-with-capabilities, didOpen-publishes-diagnostics-on-bad-source, didOpen-empty-diagnostics-on-clean, unsupported-request-returns-MethodNotFound. Test total: **402** (334 library + 64 e2e + 4 LSP), 0 warnings.

**Limitations carried to 4E.3 / 4E polish:**
- Push-only diagnostics still in 4E.2 (no `textDocument/diagnostic` pull). Pull requires bumping `lsp-types` and adding the capability; deferred until a real editor user asks.
- No filesystem watcher: a `Cplus.toml` created mid-session is picked up on the next `didSave`, not instantly.
- Multi-binary project mode walks the first `[[bin]]` only; the manifest only allows one today, so the merge-across-bins design from §10 is forward-compatible plumbing for when manifest gains plural bins.
- `--log PATH` is parsed but writes are not yet wired (4E polish).
- Code-action quick-fixes are emitted only when the suggestion's target file matches the asked URI. Cross-file fixes (e.g., E0403 with a suggestion pointing at the declaration site) would need a multi-file `WorkspaceEdit`; deferred.
- No completions / hover / find-references / rename / inlay hints / code-lens / semantic tokens. Each is its own Phase 5+ slice.

#### Slice 4E.2 — formatting + code-action quick-fixes · ✅ done

- `textDocument/formatting` handler wraps `cplus-core/fmt::format_source` and returns a single whole-document `TextEdit` when the buffer differs from canonical, or `[]` when already-formatted (no spurious edits in canonical-source clients). Lex errors return `[]` rather than a separate error — the diagnostic pipeline already reports them.
- `textDocument/codeAction` handler scans the per-file cache of cplus-core diagnostics (populated by `publish_diagnostics_for`), filters to diagnostics whose primary range overlaps the asked range, and emits one Quick Fix per `Suggestion`. `is_preferred = true` when the suggestion is `MachineApplicable`. The `WorkspaceEdit` carries the suggestion's `(span, replacement)` mapped into LSP `Range` form.
- New `ServerState` field `last_diagnostics: BTreeMap<Url, Vec<cplus_core::diagnostics::Diagnostic>>` — caches the *raw* cplus-core diagnostics (not just the LSP shape) so the code-action handler can reach the suggestions; cleared when a check produces no diagnostics for a previously-marked file.
- Manifest probing in the LSP now distinguishes "no manifest" (single-file mode), "manifest error" (surface E0406 via the diagnostic pipeline), and "manifest loaded" (project mode). Previously a malformed `Cplus.toml` silently fell back to single-file mode and the error was hidden — caught by writing the 4E.2 code-action e2e test.
- 4 new e2e tests: formatting returns the canonical `TextEdit`; formatting returns no edits for canonical source; code-action offers a Quick Fix for a manifest E0406 (the synthesized `edition = "2026"` replacement); code-action returns `[]` when no diagnostics overlap the asked range. Test total: **406** (334 library + 64 e2e + 8 LSP), 0 warnings.
- **VS Code editor integration** under [editors/vscode/](editors/vscode/): `package.json` + `extension.js` (LSP client glue, ~50 lines plain JS — no TypeScript build step), `language-configuration.json` (brackets, comments, auto-close), `syntaxes/cplus.tmLanguage.json` (TextMate grammar covering comments, strings, numbers with type suffixes, keyword categories, built-in + PascalCase types, function definition + call sites, operator categories, attributes, `import "..." as N` alias coloring), `.vscode/launch.json` (pre-configured F5 dev-host launch). Documented setup in [editors/vscode/README.md](editors/vscode/README.md): F5 dev-mode or `vsce package` → install-from-VSIX. Verified by `npm install` succeeding and `node --check` on the JS / `JSON.parse` on both manifests.

#### Slice 4E.3 — goto-definition · ✅ done

Closes the LSP triad (diagnostics + formatting + jump). Strategy from the LSP design note §7: re-lex the buffer at the cursor's byte position to find the identifier, then scan the resolver's merged program for items whose qualified name's last `.`-segment matches. The cursor click on `square` in `math::square(7)` matches both single-file `square` and resolver-qualified `src.math.square`.

- Capability `definitionProvider: true` advertised.
- `textDocument/definition` dispatch maps position → byte offset → identifier token via `lexer::tokenize`, then walks the project (or single-file buffer) for matching `fn` / `struct` / `enum` items. Returns a single `Location` (or array) pointing at the item's name span; uses each origin file's `LineMap` so the line/col is right per file.
- Project mode runs `resolver::load_project` to get the merged program + per-file source map. Single-file mode parses the open buffer directly.
- `impl`-block targets and method definitions aren't indexed in 4E.3 — clicking `p.translate()` doesn't yet jump to `fn translate` inside `impl Point`. Phase-5 polish when sema's symbol table grows.
- 3 new e2e tests pin single-file goto, cross-file goto, and the no-match case. Test total bumped to **414** (335 library + 68 e2e + 11 LSP).

#### Slice 4-end — control flow + cross-file patterns + 5-file sample · ✅ done

Carry-forward bundle that closes the small deferred items from earlier slices.

- **`break` / `continue` / `loop` / `while let`** (carry-forward from 4A.5):
  - AST: new `StmtKind::Break`, `StmtKind::Continue`, `StmtKind::Loop(Block)`, `StmtKind::WhileLet { pattern, scrutinee, body }`. Keywords were already reserved at Phase 1.
  - Parser: `loop { ... }`, `break;`, `continue;`, `while let PAT = E { BODY }` (lookahead-1 on `while`).
  - Lowering: `WhileLet → Loop { match E { PAT => { BODY; }, _ => break, } }`. Refutability still required (E0347 — same as `if let`). `stmt_diverges` now treats `break` and `continue` as diverging, so `guard let` else blocks ending in `break;` / `continue;` are accepted.
  - Sema: `loop_depth` field on `SemaCx`; bumped entering `while` / `for` / `loop` bodies. `break` / `continue` outside a loop → new **E0353** ("`break` used outside of a loop"). Loops themselves are well-typed at unit.
  - Codegen: new `loop_labels: Vec<(continue_label, break_label)>` stack on `FnState`. Pushed at each loop entry, popped on exit. `break` → `br %break_label`; `continue` → `br %continue_label`. For-range and C-style for now route through a dedicated `step` block (the increment / update list lives there) so `continue` runs them before the cond re-check.
  - 1 new sample [docs/examples/loops.cplus](docs/examples/loops.cplus); 3 new e2e tests (`loops_runs`, `break_outside_loop_rejected`, `continue_outside_loop_rejected`).
- **Cross-file variant patterns** (carry-forward from 4A):
  - Parser: `prefix::Enum::Variant(...)` in a pattern position now parses as a 3-segment variant pattern. The parser collapses `prefix::Enum` into the `enum_name` field as a `::`-joined string (mirroring how qualified type names live as `Path("prefix::Type")` until the resolver rewrites them).
  - Resolver: `rewrite_pattern` now splits the enum_name on `::` and, if the prefix is a known import alias, rewrites to the qualified form. Pub-gating is applied (E0403 if the enum isn't pub).
  - 1 new resolver test pinning the rewrite. Test total: **413** (after this) → **414** with the 5-file sample test.
- **5-file sample project** [docs/examples/projects/calc/](docs/examples/projects/calc/) — satisfies the Phase-4 exit criterion ("project split across 5+ files"):
  - `ops.cplus` — pub arithmetic primitives (`add`, `mul`, `neg`).
  - `expr.cplus` — pub tagged enum `Expr { Lit(i32), Add(i32, i32), Mul(i32, i32), Neg(i32) }`.
  - `eval.cplus` — imports `expr` and `ops`; uses cross-file variant patterns in a `match` against `expr::Expr`.
  - `util.cplus` — imports `expr` for constructor functions.
  - `main.cplus` — orchestrator; imports `eval` and `util`; prints `-14` for `(3+4) * (-2)`.
  - 1 new e2e test (`calc_5file_project_builds_and_runs`) reads the in-tree project into a tempdir, runs `cpc build`, asserts exit + stdout.

**Slice 4D limitations carried to slice 4D.2:**
- Does not collapse user's incidental line wraps (a binary expression hand-wrapped to two lines stays two lines even if it would fit on one).
- Does not force multi-line on >100-column overflow.
- Does not re-indent multi-line block comments at the formatted indent — comment bodies are emitted verbatim (including any internal whitespace).
- Trailing-comment alignment is preserved literally; we don't normalize multi-space gaps before `//` to a single space. Acceptable for now since the samples deliberately align (e.g. `println(...);  // 49`).
- `|` as bitwise-or is treated as tight, which would mis-format `a | b` — no in-tree sample yet exercises this. Becomes a 4D.2 fix the moment a bitwise sample appears.

**LLVM features used:** ThinLTO/FullLTO across modules (only when separate compilation lands — Phase 4 polish).

**Exit: ✅ met.** [docs/examples/projects/calc/](docs/examples/projects/calc/) is a 5-file `Cplus.toml`-managed project that builds via `cpc build` and runs end-to-end; `cpc fmt --check docs/examples/` returns clean across every sample (lib test `each_sample_round_trips` + e2e `fmt_check_all_samples_clean` both green); `cpc-lsp` connects to VS Code via the [editors/vscode/](editors/vscode/) extension and serves live diagnostics, format-on-save (via `textDocument/formatting`), Quick Fixes (via `textDocument/codeAction`), and goto-definition (via `textDocument/definition`).

**Carry-forward to Phase 5 (and beyond) — not blocking:**
- **4D.2** — formatter reformatting heuristics. Today the formatter preserves user line breaks; it doesn't collapse incidental wraps that fit on one line nor force multi-line on >100-column overflow. Trailing-comment alignment is preserved literally. Multi-line block comments aren't re-indented at the formatted indent. None of these matter for the in-tree samples (they all round-trip); they'll matter once real users write non-canonical code.
- **4F** — `cpc test --json`. Design-blocked on the `#[test]` attribute syntax, which is a Phase-5 design carry-forward in §11. Will land alongside the test runner.
- **Multi-binding `guard let`** — E0352 still fires for `guard let Pair(a, b) = ...`. Needs anonymous tuples / multi-value lowering. Revisit when a motivating example appears.
- **LSP polish** — filesystem watcher (currently a `Cplus.toml` created mid-session is picked up on the next `didSave`, not instantly); `textDocument/diagnostic` pull capability (needs an `lsp-types` version bump); cross-file `WorkspaceEdit` in code-action quick-fixes; `--log PATH` writing (parsed but unused); LSP completions / hover / find-references / rename / inlay-hints / semantic-tokens (each is its own Phase-5+ design slice).
- **Editor support beyond VS Code** — Helix / Neovim configs are mechanical given the LSP. Documentation when a user asks.

### Phase 5 — Shared borrows + tooling polish · 3–4 months · ✅ done

C+ has no `&T` reference type (see §2.9). What Phase 5 turns on is *tracking* the shared-borrow form that already exists at the surface: `x: T` on a non-`Copy` type. This phase makes the borrow checker enforce shared-borrow rules; Phase 6 adds exclusive-borrow rules.

**Sequencing (locked in at Phase-5 kickoff):**

1. **Design notes first** — three of them, all in `docs/design/`:
