   - `phase5-borrow-shared.md` — shared-borrow tracking, conflict detection, lifetime elision, diagnostic shape. The biggest design note the project will ever produce; budget a real week. Highest risk concentration of any Phase-5+ work, so it goes first.
   - `phase5-attributes.md` — `#[...]` attribute syntax as a *general* extension point. Hard rule: attributes carry no expression-level compile-time computation (see §2.8d). First instantiation is `#[test]`; resolves the §11 Phase-5 carry-forward without inventing a one-off syntax.
   - `phase5-doctests.md` — `///` doc-comment extraction syntax, scope/imports inside doctests, error attribution. Smaller; can land after attributes.
2. **Borrow checker** — probably 4–6 sub-slices. Risk-concentrated, so it lands before tooling: if the design needs a surface change that conflicts with §2.9, that's a language-level rework and everything built on top needs revisiting. Doing it first means all later Phase-5 slices get to assume stable borrow semantics.
3. **Attributes + `cpc test`** — the `#[test]` instantiation lands together with the attribute parser plumbing. Unlocks the 4F `cpc test --json` carry-forward.
4. **Doctests** — `assert` lines inside `///` extracted, compiled, run by `cpc test`.
5. **LSP polish** — completions + find-references (sema is rich enough); then hover + rename + inlay hints. Each its own slice.

**Borrow checking:**
- Shared-borrow tracking on `x: T` / `self` parameters of non-`Copy` type — many concurrent readers fine, conflict against `mut`/`move` of the same place rejected.
- **Lifetime inference designed from C+'s actual surface, not ported from Rust.** Rust's elision rules exist because `&T` everywhere makes signatures unreadable; C+ has no `&T`, so the right framing is "what minimum elision keeps `fn longest(xs: string, ys: string) -> string` from requiring annotations Phase 5 doesn't have yet?" The design note enumerates the signature shapes C+ actually produces and picks the minimum rule set. **Bias: elide less rather than more in Phase 5.** Conservative-now-relax-later is a one-way door we can walk through; permissive-now-tighten-later is a migration we want to avoid.
- Borrow conflict detection: shared borrow vs. concurrent move of the same place.
- Borrow-checker diagnostics framework (the long pole of error-message quality work).

**Tooling:**
- **`cpc test`** — built-in test runner. `#[test]` attribute (resolved at Phase-5 kickoff in favor of attributes over a `test fn` keyword; see §2.8d). Auto-discovered, parallel by default, JSON output via `--json` (per-test pass/fail/duration/captured output). AI agents iterate via this loop.
- **Doctests** — `assert` lines inside `///` doc comments are extracted, compiled, and run by `cpc test`. Forces docs to stay correct.
- **LSP completions and find-references** — sema is now rich enough to drive these.

**Exit:** can write `fn longest(xs: string, ys: string) -> string` (both parameters borrowed-shared, return moves the chosen one) and have the checker accept it under elided lifetimes; using a moved value while a shared borrow of the same place is alive is a compile error; `cpc test --json` runs the test suite for any in-tree program.

### Phase 6 — Exclusive borrows + full aliasing rule · 3–4 months · ✅ done

Design note: [docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md](docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md).

- Exclusive-borrow tracking on `mut x: T` / `mut self` parameters of non-`Copy` type — at most one at a time, conflicts with every other access to the same place
- Aliasing-XOR-mutability: at any program point a place has either any number of shared borrows or exactly one exclusive borrow, never both
- Explicit lifetime annotation syntax for cases inference can't solve. Spelling decided: **`borrow REGION T`** at parameter / field / return-type positions. New reserved keyword `borrow`. Composes orthogonally with `mut` / `move` parameter markers (`mut x: borrow A T` is the exclusive form; `move x: T` admits no region — ownership transfer doesn't borrow). Region names are ordinary identifiers, local to one signature. Design note [phase6-borrow-exclusive.md](docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md) §4.2 records the reasoning for picking `borrow REGION T` over the alternatives (apostrophe-prefix lifetimes; `where return borrows ...` clauses).
- Partial-place tracking via `Place::projections` (Phase-5 5BC.5 plumbing) activates — `mut buf.left` and `mut buf.right` no longer conflict.
- Drop analysis with conditional moves (different branches consuming different values); static analyzer drives drop-flag codegen specialization (definitely-moved → no drop call; definitely-not-moved → unconditional drop call).
- Iterator-invalidation, data-race, dangling-pointer cases all rejected at compile time.

**LLVM features used:** **`noalias` parameter attribute on the underlying pointer for every `mut x: T` (non-`Copy`)** — the borrow checker proves uniqueness, so we can tag the LLVM parameter and unlock aggressive load/store reordering (this is one of the main reasons borrow-checked code can outperform C); atomic instructions (`load atomic`, `store atomic`, `cmpxchg`, `atomicrmw`, `fence`) with C11 ordering specifiers (`monotonic`/`acquire`/`release`/`acq_rel`/`seq_cst`) for `Atomic[T]` lowering.

**Exit:** A small in-tree test program implementing a `Vec[T]`-style growable array compiles cleanly and rejects iterator invalidation (`for x in vec { vec.push(...) }` errors at compile time).

### Phase 7 — Generics + interfaces · 2–4 months · ✅ complete

Design note: [docs/design/phase7-generics.md](docs/design/phase7-generics.md).

- Parametric functions and types: `fn max[T: Ord](a: T, b: T) -> T`. **Square-bracket** parameter lists, not `<T>` — sidesteps angle-bracket parse ambiguity (the C++ `vector<vector<int>>` issue and Rust's `::<>` workaround).
- New `interface` keyword: `interface Ord { fn compare(self, other: Self) -> i32; }`. Implementations via `impl Ord for Point { fn compare(self, other: Point) -> i32 { ... } }`.
- Type-parameter bounds: `T: Ord + Eq` (`+` joins multiple bounds). Bounds checked at instantiation; satisfied iff every named interface has an `impl Interface for ConcreteType` block.
- `Self` keyword inside `interface` and `impl Interface for Type` blocks — substituted to the implementing type at impl-resolution.
- **Monomorphization** at codegen: each `(generic_fn, [concrete_types])` pair gets its own LLVM function. Name mangling: `Pair[i32, Vec[u8]]::new` → `@Pair__i32__Vec__u8.new`. Work-queue with `BTreeSet` dedup; runs until empty. **Mangled names are an implementation detail and never source-typeable** — users always write `Pair[i32, Vec[u8]]::new` / `Option[i32]::Some(v)` at both value-site *and* pattern-site. Any place a mangled name leaks into source today (e.g. match arms in 7GEN.5d) is a known wart to be closed by 7GEN.5e via type-directed pattern resolution.
- **No dynamic dispatch.** Phase 7 is monomorphization-only — no `dyn Interface` equivalent, no vtables. Static-only generics; dynamic dispatch is a separate later design decision.
- **Coherence (orphan rule):** `impl Interface for Type` admitted only in the file that defines either `Interface` or `Type`. Prevents incoherent overlap.
- Reserved error codes: E0500–E0511. New keywords: `interface`, `Self` (the latter context-restricted to interface/impl bodies).
- ~~Heap allocation primitives + allocator-as-parameter convention (§2.2) are a **parallel slice 7HEAP**~~ — **reframed 2026-05-13: 7HEAP is no longer a phase.** Phase 10's `extern fn` + raw pointers + `unsafe` made heap primitives expressible at user level (proven by [docs/examples/owned_string.cplus](docs/examples/owned_string.cplus)); the only remaining language-level need is `size_of[T]()` and `align_of[T]()` intrinsics so user code can compute byte counts for typed allocations. Those land as a small Phase-11 slice. `Allocator` is library-not-language work: a user-defined `interface Allocator` (Dart's `package:ffi` pattern) with implementations that wrap libc — the compiler never needs to know what an allocator is. Closure note in §11 resolved-log; no separate design note required.
- Implementation slicing: 7GEN.1 (generic-fn parser ✅) → 7GEN.2 (generic-type parser ✅) → 7GEN.3 (interface + impl ✅) → 7GEN.4 (sema substitution + interface-impl validation ✅) → 7GEN.5a (generic-fn inference + monomorphization ✅) → 7GEN.5b (`::[T]` turbofish for generic-fn calls ✅) → 7GEN.5c (generic-struct instantiation ✅) → 7GEN.5d (generic-enum instantiation ✅) → 7GEN.5e step 1 (source-level generic-enum patterns ✅) → 7GEN.5e step 2 (generic methods on concrete-typed impls + turbofish on method/assoc calls ✅) → 7GEN.5e step 3 (generic-typed impls `impl Box[T] {}` ✅) → 7GEN.5e step 4 (bound checking E0502 ✅) → 7GEN.6 (blessed interfaces Copy/Eq/Ord/Hash/Clone ✅) → 7EXIT (inline-typed exit demo ✅, [docs/examples/phase7_generics.cplus](docs/examples/phase7_generics.cplus)) → 7HEAP (reframed 2026-05-13: dropped as a phase; `size_of[T]()`/`align_of[T]()` land in Phase 11, Allocator is library work).

**Exit:** A generic `Pair[A, B]` and a generic `Vec[T]`-style array can be defined and used in test programs; the type checker correctly monomorphizes per-instantiation.

### Phase 8 — Strings (Swift-inspired, UTF-8) · 1–2 months · ✅ shipped (view layer in compiler; owned layer at user level)

**Why a dedicated phase.** §2.1 reserves `string` and `cstring` as foundational types but defers the implementation. Most Phase-1–7 demos print numbers because `println(&str)` doesn't exist yet — the language is unusable for real programs until strings land. This phase makes C+ pleasant for non-numeric work without committing to a stdlib (§2.6 stays out of scope).

**Design lineage: Swift, minus closures.** Swift's `String` is the closest match to what C+ wants: value semantics, copy-on-write under the hood, UTF-8 native storage (Swift 5+), and a clean cstring bridge. We adopt that model and drop the parts that don't fit:

- ✅ **Take from Swift:** UTF-8 storage; value semantics with COW; opaque storage layout (users can't reach in and index bytes by accident); a separate `Substring` / `str` view type; deliberate friction around random-access indexing (forces users to pick a view first — bytes vs. scalars vs. grapheme clusters); explicit `to_cstring()` / `from_cstring()` for FFI.
- ❌ **Drop from Swift:** closures (`{ x in ... }`) — out of scope for C+, period. String interpolation requiring closures (Swift's `\(...)` is technically an expression, not a closure — that's fine; the closure-based custom-interpolation API is what we skip). The trailing-closure DSL pattern (`s.replace { ... }`) doesn't exist for us; same operations come through plain method calls.
- ⏸️ **Defer:** grapheme cluster API (needs Unicode tables or an ICU dep — too heavy for this phase), normalization (NFC/NFD), localization, regex (separate phase).

**Three types, three layers:**

| Type | Lifetime | Storage | Use |
|---|---|---|---|
| `string` | owned, growable | heap (depends on 7HEAP) | the default — local variables, fields, return types |
| `str` | borrowed view | pointer + length into someone else's bytes | function parameters; string literals |
| `cstring` | borrowed view | null-terminated raw pointer | FFI only — never produced from C+ literals |

String literals `"hello"` have type `str` (not `string`) — they point at a static read-only UTF-8 blob in the binary's data segment. To get an owned `string` you call `"hello".to_string()` or equivalent.

**Core operations (concrete API surface):**

- `str::len(self) -> usize` — byte length, not character count
- `str::is_empty(self) -> bool`
- `str::as_bytes(self) -> u8[]` — borrowed view into the underlying UTF-8 bytes
- `str::starts_with(self, prefix: str) -> bool`, `ends_with`, `contains`
- `string::new() -> string` — empty owned string
- `string::with_capacity(n: usize) -> string`
- `string::push_str(mut self, s: str)`
- `string::push(mut self, c: u32)` — code-point append (validates ≤ 0x10FFFF, encodes as UTF-8 bytes)
- `string::to_cstring(self) -> cstring` — allocates a NUL-terminated copy (cstring owns the buffer; rejects strings containing internal NUL bytes with a runtime trap or returns a `Result`, decide at design time)
- `cstring::to_string(self) -> string` — copies bytes up to NUL, validates UTF-8 (Result-returning, since C strings can be arbitrary bytes)
- `+` operator on `string + str` and `string + string` (consumes the LHS, returns owned)
- `==` / `!=` comparison via blessed `Eq` impl

**Interpolation: Swift-style `"\(expr)"` (deferred to 8.B).** First cut ships without interpolation — users do `string::new() + "n = " + n.to_string()`. The `\(...)` desugar (parse → `str` concat tree → calls to each part's `to_string()`) is a clean follow-up slice; the spec is settled (Swift's syntax, our restriction: no closures, so the embedded expression is a plain expression, not a block).

**Indexing semantics — deliberately strict.** No `s[i]` operator returning `u8` or `char`. Users must explicitly choose a view: `s.as_bytes()[i]` for byte access, `s.scalars()` (Phase-8 deferred) for code-point iteration, `s.graphemes()` (post-Unicode-tables) for user-perceived characters. This matches Swift's "you can't accidentally index in the middle of a multi-byte character" guarantee, achieved by removing the operator rather than by making it dynamic.

**No null strings.** `string` and `str` are never null; nullable string is `?string` per §2.1 (the existing nullable opt-in). This avoids C/C++'s "is this `char*` empty or NULL?" ambiguity.

**Implementation slicing:**
- **8.STR.1** — `str` type + literal lowering: `str` as a built-in `(ptr, len)` struct; string literals compile to a static `[N x i8]` in the data segment; `str::len()`, `str::is_empty()`, `str::as_bytes()`. No heap yet. Unblocks `println("hello")` once `println` learns the overload.
- **8.STR.2** — `println(s: str)` intrinsic (extends the existing `println(n: i32)` machinery). Emits a `printf("%.*s", len, ptr)` or `write(1, ptr, len)`. Same intrinsic-style codegen as `println(i32)`.
- **8.STR.3** — `string` owned type (depends on 7HEAP). `new`, `with_capacity`, `push_str`, `push`, drop. Blessed `Drop` via the existing destructor machinery.
- **8.STR.4** — `cstring` view type + `to_cstring`/`from_cstring`. Settle the embedded-NUL policy (trap vs. Result) at design time; trap is simpler and matches C semantics.
- **8.STR.5** — `+` operator overloading for strings only (not general operator overloading — that stays out of scope per §2.8). Adds a compiler-internal `__string_concat` intrinsic and rewrites `+` on `string`/`str` operands.
- **8.STR.6** — `Eq`/`Hash` impls for `str` and `string`. Probably ships alongside .3 since hash tables want it.
- **8.STR.B** — interpolation `"\(expr)"` (separate slice, lands after the core).

**Reserved error codes:** E0600–E0610 for string-specific diagnostics (embedded NUL in `to_cstring`, invalid UTF-8 from `cstring`, etc.). Block reserved so codes don't collide with Phase-7's E0500–E0511.

**LLVM features used:** static UTF-8 blob in `.rodata` for string literals; the existing `ccc` calling convention for the heap-allocator calls in `string::with_capacity`/`push_str`; intrinsic codegen pattern from Phase 1's `println`.

**Exit:** the FizzBuzz demo at [docs/examples/fizzbuzz.cplus](docs/examples/fizzbuzz.cplus) (currently emits integer codes) is rewritten to print real `"Fizz"` / `"Buzz"` / `"FizzBuzz"` strings via `println(str)`, and a sample program builds a `string` from concatenations and calls a libc function via `to_cstring()` end-to-end.

### Phase 9 — Identity exploration (TypeScript-flavored review) · ❌ rejected (2026-05-13)

**Status: rejected after case-by-case audit.** Decision recorded in chat session 2026-05-13; closure summary below.

**Why rejected.** A case-by-case walk through the major TS surface choices (mutability defaults, function keyword, aggregate types, generics bracket, null handling) showed that every TS-flavored alternative falls into one of three buckets:

1. **Flips a safety default** — `let`/`const` makes mutability the default (regression from C+'s opt-in `mut`). `null`/`undefined` makes every reference type silently nullable (regression from explicit `Option[T]`).
2. **Violates the "no several ways to do the same thing" principle** — Rust-style turbofish `::<T>` at call sites is one form for declarations, another for calls. `class` ships with constructors *and* struct-literal construction would still work, leaving two ways to build a value.
3. **Pays parser/semantic complexity for purely visual wins** — Context-sensitive `<T>` parsing accumulates TS's decade of corner cases. `class` either fights C+'s separation of data layout from behavior (Option 3B) or is a cosmetic rename that buys nothing (Option 3C).

The deeper reason: **TypeScript's surface syntax is inseparable from its object-oriented assumptions.** `class`/`this`/constructors, decorators-as-runtime, `null`/`undefined` nullability, the `function`+arrow split — all of these encode "objects have identity, mutability is the default, references can be absent." C+ deliberately rejects each of those assumptions. TS-flavored syntax without TS semantics would be either dishonest (looks TS, behaves C+) or impractical (the cosmetic-only subset is empty after audit).

**What was retained as principle, not as phase work:**
- **No several ways to do the same thing** (except universally-accepted duplications like `for`/`while`) — applied going forward.
- **Function over syntax** — visual familiarity loses to safety. Locked in chat 2026-05-13.

**What's still on the table as independent work (NOT under a "TS audit" banner):**
- `type Foo = Bar` aliases — useful regardless of TS heritage; reconsider as a Phase 11 polish slice if a real use case surfaces.
- `null` literal restricted to raw pointers in `unsafe` for FFI ergonomics (Cocoa interop needs it) — design captured in [objc-c-interop/notes.md](objc-c-interop/notes.md).
- String interpolation — already a deferred Phase 8 item, decoupled from this rejection.

**The marketing answer.** "Looks like Rust" perception is still real. Addressing it lives elsewhere: better example programs, a "What C+ is *not*" one-pager, AI-native tooling work — none of which require a syntax reskin.

**Removed from scope:** all 9.ID.* slices (audit, docs, alias, opt, null, lit, fn, async, interp, reject). The design register at `docs/design/phase9-identity.md` was never created and won't be.

### Phase 10 — C interop hardening · 1–3 months · ✅ core complete (cross-platform verification deferred)

- `extern fn` declarations: the foundation lands earlier in Phase 1; this phase is calling-convention hardening and edge cases
- ABI compliance verified on x86_64 Linux first, then macOS/ARM, then Windows
- Struct layout compatibility (`#[repr(C)]`-equivalent)
- Varargs in `extern fn`
- `cstring` ↔ `string` conversions (full polish — Phase 8 lands the minimal bridge)
- `cpc-bindgen` (separate tool, not language feature) as a stretch goal

**LLVM features used:** `ccc` calling convention for `extern fn`; ABI parameter attributes (`byval`, `sret`, `inreg`, `nest`) to match the platform C ABI on struct-passing edge cases; varargs handled via LLVM's per-target rules; ThinLTO/FullLTO link-time optimization across modules.

**Exit:** a program calling libc to open and read a file works end-to-end across all supported platforms.

### Phase 11 — Polish · indefinite

(LSP, formatter, test runner, structured diagnostics all landed earlier.)

- `size_of[T]()` / `align_of[T]()` intrinsics (slice 11.LAYOUT) — both safe, both take a single type arg via turbofish (`size_of::[i32]()`), both return `usize`. Codegen via LLVM GEP-null trick (`ptrtoint (getelementptr T, ptr null, i64 1) to i64` for sizeof; `ptrtoint (getelementptr {i1, T}, ptr null, i64 0, i32 1) to i64` for alignof). Unblocks user-level `Allocator` interface + `Vec[T]` (reframe replacing 7HEAP — see §11 resolved-log entry 2026-05-13). **✅ shipped 2026-05-13.**
- Integer-to-raw-pointer cast (slice 11.INTPTR) — `0 as *T` inside `unsafe { }`. P3 from the null-handling design (design.md). Sema extends `cast_allowed` for the type pair, gates on `unsafe_depth > 0` with **E0801**. Codegen emits `inttoptr` (with `zext`/`sext` widening if the source is narrower than i64). The FFI-null spelling for C+; no `null` keyword added. **✅ shipped 2026-05-13.**
- `#[link_name = "..."]` attribute on extern fns (slice 11.LINKNAME) — aliases the linker symbol so multiple typed signatures can resolve to the same C symbol. Load-bearing for ObjC's `objc_msgSend` pattern (and any C library that needs same-symbol-many-typed-shapes). New parser shape `#[name = value]`, new `ArgsSpec::ExactlyOneStr` in attrs validation, `link_name: Option<String>` on sema and codegen `FnSig`, codegen dedups `declare` emission across aliased symbols and uses the link_name at call sites. Sema rejects on non-extern fns with **E0356**. **✅ shipped 2026-05-13.**
- Function pointer types and values (slice 11.FN_PTR) — `fn(T1, T2) -> R` in type position, bare-ident type-directed coercion to fn pointer values. Final compiler gap for the ObjC interop story (needed for `class_addMethod(class, sel, IMP imp, types)`). Design note at [docs/design/phase11-fn-pointers.md](docs/design/phase11-fn-pointers.md). **✅ shipped 2026-05-13** — see resolved-log entry below.
- Better error messages (continuous; borrow-checker diagnostics are the long pole)
- Debugger support (DWARF — largely free from LLVM via `!DIFile` / `!DISubprogram` / `!DILocation` metadata; ideally wired up earlier so source positions don't have to be retrofitted)
- Sanitizer flags (`cpc --asan` / `--ubsan` / `--tsan` / `--msan`) — instrumented user binaries via LLVM's existing pass infrastructure
- Package manager (dependency resolution, registry — extends Phase 4 manifest)
- Documentation generator (extends Phase 5 doctests)
- Effect tracking design exploration (deferred speculative feature; see §11)
- Built-in contracts design exploration (deferred speculative feature; see §11)
- CLI niceties

---

## 4. LLVM strategy

LLVM is doing most of the heavy lifting. This section catalogs what we use it for, organized by category. Per-phase usage is annotated inline in §3.

### 4.1 Codegen freebies

Things LLVM does so we don't have to.

- **`alloca` + `load`/`store` + `mem2reg` pass.** Every local gets an `alloca`; reads and writes use `load`/`store`; the `mem2reg` pass promotes well-behaved locals to SSA registers and inserts PHI nodes. This is the single biggest gift — we don't write SSA construction. Same approach as clang and rustc.
- **`getelementptr` (GEP).** All pointer arithmetic, struct field access, and array indexing. Typed and target-aware. Notoriously confusing at first; spend an afternoon on the GEP FAQ before Phase 2.
- **Optimization passes.** The `-O0`/`-O1`/`-O2`/`-O3` pipeline is free. Inlining, dead-code elim, GVN, LICM, instcombine, loop vectorization, sccp. We emit straightforward IR; LLVM does the smart work. Within ~5% of clang's output without ever writing an optimization ourselves.
- **DWARF debug info.** `!DIFile` / `!DISubprogram` / `!DILocation` metadata gives gdb/lldb support, source-level breakpoints, and stack traces. Wire it up early — retrofitting source positions through every instruction is painful.

### 4.2 Intrinsics that match C+ semantics directly

- **Checked arithmetic.** `llvm.sadd/ssub/smul.with.overflow.iN` (signed) and `llvm.uadd/usub/umul.with.overflow.iN` (unsigned). Returns `{result, overflow_bit}`. Branch on the bit to call `llvm.trap`. Direct match for our debug-mode trap-on-overflow rule. Release mode uses plain `add`/`sub`/`mul`.
- **`llvm.trap` and `unreachable`.** `llvm.trap` emits the architecture's trap (UD2 / BRK). What runtime panics call. `unreachable` is a control-flow hint for places we've proven can't be reached (post-`return`, exhaustive match defaults, post-`llvm.trap` blocks).
- **Atomic instructions.** `load atomic` / `store atomic` / `cmpxchg` / `atomicrmw` / `fence` with ordering specifiers `monotonic` / `acquire` / `release` / `acq_rel` / `seq_cst`. One-to-one with our C11 memory model. `Atomic[T]` (compiler-blessed library types) lower verbatim.

### 4.3 Performance unlocks the borrow checker hands us

This is where C+ can outperform C in some workloads. The borrow checker proves things the C compiler isn't allowed to assume.

- **`noalias` parameter attribute.** Every `mut x: T` (non-`Copy`) is provably non-aliasing. Tag the underlying pointer parameter with `noalias` and the optimizer reorders loads/stores aggressively. Rust does this on `&mut T`; C+ does the same on the equivalent surface form (see §2.9). Phase 6.
- **`nonnull` and `dereferenceable(N)`.** Non-null pointers are the default in C+; `*T` and all parameter-passed values are guaranteed non-null at the pointer level. Tagging with `nonnull` elides null checks; `dereferenceable(N)` says "≥ N bytes here are valid." Phase 2/3.
- **`align` attribute / metadata.** Pointer alignment guarantees enable better load/store codegen on strict-alignment targets.
- **`noundef` parameter attribute.** Definite assignment + non-null + initialized values let us promise this widely; LLVM uses it to eliminate UB-related conservatism in optimization.

### 4.4 ABI / interop machinery

- **Calling conventions.** `ccc` (C-compatible, default) for `extern fn`; `fastcc` for non-`extern` C+ internals (better register usage on some targets). Phase 10.
- **Parameter ABI attributes.** `byval`, `sret`, `inreg`, `nest` — for matching the platform C ABI on struct-passing edge cases. The most error-prone part of C interop; LLVM handles the per-target rules.
- **Varargs.** `declare i32 @printf(ptr, ...)` — LLVM handles platform-specific calling conventions for varargs (which differ wildly between x86_64 SysV and ARM AAPCS).

### 4.5 Tooling that's just there

- **Sanitizers.** `cpc --asan` / `--ubsan` / `--tsan` / `--msan` — instrumented user binaries. Also useful for self-testing the compiler during development. Phase 11.
- **ThinLTO / FullLTO.** Cross-module link-time optimization. Just a flag on the linker invocation. Phase 4 onward.
- **PGO / AutoFDO hooks.** Available if and when profile-guided optimization is wanted. Not on the roadmap but free if needed.

### 4.6 Out of scope (don't spend time on)

- Exception handling (`landingpad` / `invoke` / `resume`) — C+ has no exceptions.
- Garbage collection statepoints — N/A.
- JIT (MCJIT / ORC) — we're AOT.
- Coroutines — no async/await in C+.
- Polly (polyhedral loop optimizer) — beyond scope.

### 4.7 Phase-by-phase summary

| Phase | LLVM features |
|-------|---------------|
| 1 | `alloca`/`load`/`store` + `mem2reg`; basic instructions; `llvm.sadd.with.overflow.i32` + `llvm.trap`; `printf` extern |
| 2 | `getelementptr`; aggregate types; `extractvalue`/`insertvalue`; `nonnull`/`dereferenceable` |
| 3 | All overflow intrinsics; `switch` for `match`; `noundef` |
| 4 | ThinLTO/FullLTO across modules |
| 5 | (no new LLVM features — borrow analysis is on our IR, not LLVM's) |
| 6 | `noalias` on `mut x: T` (non-`Copy`); atomic instructions + orderings |
| 8 | `ccc` calling convention; ABI parameter attributes; varargs |
| 9 | DWARF metadata; sanitizer passes |

---

## 5. Tooling architecture (AI-native)

C+ treats tooling as Phase 1–4 plumbing, not Phase 11 polish. The unifying principle: **the language gives tools as much information as possible, and the tools are present and excellent from early phases.** Pre-AI languages got away with bolt-on tooling. C+ doesn't.

### 5.1 Compiler-as-library

The compiler is split into:

- **`cplus-core`** — library crate. Lexer, parser, AST, sema, codegen, diagnostics. Stable Rust API consumed by every tool.
- **`cpc`** — binary crate, ~200 lines. Argument parsing and dispatch into `cplus-core`. Exposes `cpc build`, `cpc check`, `cpc parse`, `cpc fmt`, `cpc test`, `cpc lsp`.
- **`cpc-lsp`** — separate binary (Phase 4) that links the same `cplus-core`.

This is a Phase-1 architectural decision. Any tool ever written for C+ uses the same library that the compiler does — no separate reimplementation, no tool drift.

### 5.2 Structured diagnostics

Every error and warning is structured, not a printf string. JSON shape (per-diagnostic):

```json
{
  "file": "foo.cplus",
  "span": { "start_line": 12, "start_col": 5, "end_line": 12, "end_col": 8 },
  "severity": "error",
  "code": "E0042",
  "message": "expected `;` after expression",
  "suggestions": [
    { "description": "insert `;`", "span": {...}, "replacement": ";" }
  ]
}
```

`cpc --diagnostics=json` emits this; `cpc --diagnostics=human` (default) renders the human-readable form on top of the same data. Suggestions are machine-applicable: an AI agent can apply a fix without round-tripping through an LLM.

This format is part of the language's stable interface from Phase 1. Every error site in the compiler produces a structured diagnostic; the rendering layer is downstream.

### 5.3 Determinism

Same inputs → byte-identical outputs. Required so AI agents can hash-compare to verify changes.

- `BTreeMap` not `HashMap` in any code path that affects output (codegen, diagnostics ordering, AST emit).
- Sorted iteration over collections.
- No timestamps, build paths, or other environmental data baked into output.
- Deterministic codegen — no nondeterministic optimizer choices.

### 5.4 Built-in subcommands

A single binary, multiple modes. All of them link `cplus-core`.

- `cpc build foo.cplus -o foo` — full pipeline; produces a binary.
- `cpc check FILE` — lex + parse + sema; no codegen. The fast feedback loop.
- `cpc parse FILE [--json]` — AST dump. JSON mode is for tools.
- `cpc check FILE --json` — type-resolved IR dump.
- `cpc fmt FILE` — canonical formatter, in place.
- `cpc test [PATH]` — discover + run `#[test]` functions and doctests.
- `cpc lsp` — start the LSP server (delegates to `cpc-lsp` binary).
- `cpc --tokens FILE` — debug helper (already exists).
- `cpc --ast FILE` — debug helper (already exists).
- `cpc --emit-ir` — debug helper (Phase 0 frozen IR).

### 5.5 AST/IR as serialized data

Every AST node and IR node derives `serde::Serialize` from the start. Tools we don't anticipate yet will rely on this. Cost is near zero if the AST avoids `Rc<RefCell<…>>` cycles; cost is enormous to retrofit.

### 5.6 Doctests

`///` doc comments may contain `assert` expressions:

```cp
/// Returns the larger of two i32s.
///
/// Examples:
///   assert max(1, 2) == 2;
///   assert max(-5, -10) == -5;
fn max(a: i32, b: i32) -> i32 { ... }
```

`cpc test` extracts these, compiles each as a test function, runs them. Documentation that doesn't compile is a test failure. AI is excellent at writing doc comments with examples; this gives those examples teeth.

Design note required before Phase 5 implementation: extraction syntax, scope/imports inside doctests, error attribution.

### 5.7 Editions (deferred)

Not implemented yet, but the design intent is recorded so we don't paint ourselves into a corner. Eventually each `.cplus` file or project will declare its edition; the compiler handles each edition's syntax and semantics. Currently all code is treated as edition `2026` implicitly. We add the system when we actually need to break something.

### 5.8 Locality of reasoning

A single function should be readable using only the function and the signatures of what it calls. C+ already excludes the worst offenders (macros, decorators, inheritance, comptime). Future additions are evaluated against this constraint.

### 5.9 AI recovery

C+ assumes AI-generated code will often be wrong. The compiler and tools are designed to minimize the cost of finding and fixing those errors — **AI recovery** is the loss function that the principles in §5.1–§5.8 are optimizing. This section names what that means concretely and how we'll eventually measure it.

**Qualitative goals.** Most are promised elsewhere; bringing them together to articulate the recovery property:

- **Diagnostics identify the smallest useful span.** A missing semicolon highlights the gap, not the surrounding statement. A type mismatch highlights the mismatched value, not the whole expression. Cross-checked at every error site we add. *(New constraint, applies everywhere.)*
- **Generated fixes do not require parsing human prose.** Every suggestion is `(span, replacement)` per §5.2. AI agents apply fixes by string substitution against structured fields, not by NLP on `message`. *(Structural property of the diagnostic format.)*
- **Stable diagnostic JSON** — §5.2 commits the format. Tools and agents rely on the shape across versions.
- **Structured test output** — §5.4 (`cpc test --json`). Iteration loops read pass/fail/duration/output without parsing human-readable test output.
- **Canonical formatter output** — §5.4 (`cpc fmt`). Diffs between AI revisions stay small because formatting doesn't drift.
- **Explicit imports** — §2.8 forbids glob imports as default; missing-import errors are local, repairable without project-wide search.
- **Sound types, no `any`** — §2.8. The type system always rejects what's actually broken; never silently passes broken code through to runtime.
- **Locality of reasoning** — §5.8. A function plus the signatures it calls suffices to understand it; AI generations don't need to globally reason to be correct.

**Quantitative metrics (future).** Once a corpus of broken AI-generated C+ programs exists, we evaluate the compiler against it:

- % diagnosed with a precise error code (vs. a generic "expected token" fallback)
- % where the diagnostic carries a `MachineApplicable` or `MaybeIncorrect` suggestion
- % repaired in one agent pass (apply suggestions → recompile → pass)
- % repaired without changing the program's intended behavior (requires per-program intent labels — hardest to measure; needs differential testing or human review)

**The corpus does not exist yet.** Building it is research work: collect real broken programs from AI tools in the wild, label them with intent, freeze as a regression suite. Tracked in §11. Until that lands, the bullets above are aspirational, not SLOs.

---

## 6. Per-feature design-note workflow

Before implementing any non-trivial feature, write a short doc in `docs/design/` (1–2 pages):

1. **Problem.** What does this solve?
2. **Syntax.** With 3–5 examples.
3. **Semantics.** Including edge cases.
4. **Interactions.** With every already-implemented feature.
5. **Open questions.**

Keep these short. The cost is an hour and they prevent multi-day rewrites. Throw them away when implementation reveals the design was wrong — that's the point.

---

## 7. Project layout

```
.
├── Cargo.toml                    workspace
├── plan.md                       this file
├── docs/
│   ├── design/                   per-feature design notes, before implementing
│   ├── spec/                     reference manual, written late
│   └── examples/                 sample programs that must compile
├── cplus-core/                   library crate — all language logic
│   └── src/
│       ├── lib.rs                re-exports the public API
│       ├── lexer.rs
│       ├── parser.rs
│       ├── ast.rs
│       ├── sema.rs               name resolution, type checking
│       ├── codegen.rs            LLVM IR generation
│       └── diagnostics.rs        structured-error infrastructure (§5.2)
├── cpc/                          binary crate — thin CLI wrapper
│   ├── src/
│   │   ├── main.rs               argument parsing + dispatch into cplus-core
│   │   └── hello.ll              Phase-0 frozen IR (vestigial)
│   └── tests/
│       └── e2e.rs                program → compile → run → assert output
└── cpc-lsp/                      binary crate (Phase 4) — also links cplus-core
    └── src/
        └── main.rs
```

The cplus-core/cpc/cpc-lsp split is the §5.1 compiler-as-library architecture. Every tool ever written for C+ uses the same `cplus-core` library, no separate reimplementations.

---

## 8. Testing strategy

- **Unit tests** for lexer, parser, sema components.
- **Snapshot tests** for IR output of canonical programs. Catches regressions in codegen.
- **End-to-end tests**: program → compile → run → assert stdout/exit code. The most important kind. Each phase adds programs.
- **Negative tests**: programs that must fail to compile, asserting the specific error.
- **Differential tests** (Phase 10+): if a program is valid both as our language and as C, output should match clang.

A new feature is not done until it has unit + e2e + at least one negative test.

---

## 9. How to use this plan with Claude Code

For any implementation task:

1. Identify the phase and feature in §3.
2. If the feature has no design note yet, write one in `docs/design/` first (§6). Get review.
3. Implement in this order: lexer → parser → AST → sema → IR → tests.
4. Each change adds at least one e2e test program in [cpc/tests/](cpc/tests/).
5. If a phase's scope shifts, update this plan in the same change.

Do not skip step 2.

---

## 10. References

- LLVM Kaleidoscope tutorial — covers ~70% of IR generation patterns needed for Phase 1–2.
- Zig language reference — closest existing point in design space, especially for comptime, error unions, allocator-passing, slices.
- Rust reference — for module system, generics, and ownership ideas.
- Crafting Interpreters (Nystrom) — frontend techniques, even though it targets a tree-walking interpreter.
- Engineering a Compiler (Cooper & Torczon) — semantic analysis and IR construction.
- LLVM Language Reference — authoritative on IR semantics; consult before assuming what an instruction does.

---

Enables the quantitative metrics in §5.9 to become real measurements. Research work — depends on having enough AI tools producing C+ to scrape. Plausibly Phase 4+ once tools exist.

Slice 4B carry-forward (must land in slice 4C — do not drop):
- [x] **Enforce `pub` on struct fields.** Landed in slice 4C (this session). Sema's `check_field` and `check_struct_lit` now consult the field's `is_pub` and the access site's file context. Cross-file private-field read/construction → E0403. Same-file access ignores `pub`. AST gained `Item.origin_file` so sema knows the access site's file; `StructDef.origin_file` records the declaring file; `StructDef.fields` is now `Vec<(String, Ty, bool)>` with the third tuple element being the field's `is_pub`. 4 new e2e tests pin the behavior.
- [x] **Per-file source threading through sema for cross-file diagnostics.** Landed in slice 4C (this session). Resolver's `LoadedProject` now carries a `BTreeMap<FileId, (PathBuf, String)>` of every reached file. Sema's new `check_multi` entry takes the map; `SemaCx` builds a `BTreeMap<FileId, FileCtx>` with each file's pre-computed `LineMap`. `err()` routes to the current item's file context; every top-level item-iteration pass (collect_type_names, collect_struct_fields, collect_enum_payloads, compute_enum_copy_flags, collect_methods, check_methods, collect_functions, check_main_signature, check_functions) sets `current_file = item.origin_file` so diagnostics point at the file they originated from. New e2e test `cross_file_sema_error_renders_in_imported_file` pins the behavior: an E0302 inside an imported `math.cplus` renders with `math.cplus:line:col`, not `main.cplus:...`. Single-file `check()` is now a thin wrapper over `check_multi` with an empty file map.
- [x] **Parser polish for cross-file struct literals (`prefix::Type { ... }`).** Landed in slice 4C (this session). The parser's ident path now branches into struct-lit handling when it sees `{` after a `::`-qualified path (respecting `no_struct_lit` in `if`/`while`/`for` heads). 2 new parser tests; the resolver's E0403/Struct test was switched from its type-position workaround to the natural construction form.

Design notes needed before their phase (per §6):
- [x] Phase 3: ownership surface syntax (`x: T` / `mut x: T` / `move x: T`; receivers symmetric; returns always moves) — see [docs/design/phase3-ownership.md](docs/design/phase3-ownership.md)
- [x] Phase 3: `Copy` derivation rules — structural auto-derive; aggregates are `Copy` iff every component is `Copy`. See [docs/design/phase3-copy-derivation.md](docs/design/phase3-copy-derivation.md). Note: implementation requires reworking slice-3A's E0335 tests (they target structs that will become Copy under the new rule).
- [x] Phase 3: `Drop`/destructors — magic `fn drop(mut self)` method; reverse-order scope-exit; drop flags suppress dropping of moved-out bindings; Drop forces `is_copy = false`; `defer` and drop share a single LIFO scope-exit stack. See [docs/design/phase3-drop.md](docs/design/phase3-drop.md). New error codes E0338/E0339.
- [x] Phase 3: tagged unions + `match` — extend `enum` with positional payloads; `match` expression with variant/wildcard/binding patterns; exhaustiveness; LLVM lowering as `{ i32 tag, [N x i8] payload }`; plain enums stay bare-`i32`. See [docs/design/phase3-tagged-unions.md](docs/design/phase3-tagged-unions.md). New error codes E0340–E0344.
- [x] Phase 3: error handling — **`!T` and `try` rejected.** Errors are plain tagged unions (slice 3H); users write `match` at every fallible call site. Rationale recorded in §2.4 + §2.8b (FFI honesty) + §2.8c (verbosity is fine, LLM is primary writer). No more design work needed here.
- [x] Phase 4: modules — explicit path-string imports with mandatory `as` prefix (`import "math.cplus" as math;`); no filesystem-derived namespace; no `use`/no glob/no narrowing; `pub` default-private for items, fields, and methods; `Cplus.toml` manifest with `[package]` + `[[bin]]`; whole-program compilation in Phase-4 minimum; `impl` rooted in same file as its type. See [docs/design/phase4-modules.md](docs/design/phase4-modules.md). New error codes E0401–E0410. (Redesigned post-discussion 2026-05-11 — see history entry below.)
- [x] Phase 4: `cpc fmt` style decisions (indent, line length, alignment, comment handling) — see [docs/design/phase4-fmt.md](docs/design/phase4-fmt.md). Slice 4D.1 (preserving formatter) landed; 4D.2 (reformatting heuristics) carried.
- [x] Phase 4: LSP transport, capability set, what diagnostics to surface live — see [docs/design/phase4-lsp.md](docs/design/phase4-lsp.md). Slice 4E.1 (skeleton + diagnostics) landed; 4E.2 (formatting + code-actions) and 4E.3 (goto-definition) carried.
- [x] Phase 5: `docs/design/phase5-borrow-shared.md` — shared-borrow tracking, conflict detection, lifetime elision (designed from C+'s surface, not ported from Rust — see Phase 5 sequencing note), diagnostic shape. Highest-risk Phase 5 work; lands first. See [docs/design/phase5-borrow-shared.md](docs/design/phase5-borrow-shared.md). Reserves error codes E0370–E0378 (renumbered from a draft E0354+ that collided with the attributes note). Implementation in 5–6 sub-slices (5BC.1–5BC.6).
- [x] Phase 5: `docs/design/phase5-attributes.md` — `#[...]` syntax + parser rules + the declarative-only constraint (§2.8d). First instantiation is `#[test]`; resolves the prior "`#[test]` vs `test fn`" carry-forward in favor of `#[test]`. See [docs/design/phase5-attributes.md](docs/design/phase5-attributes.md). Reserves error codes E0354–E0360.
- [x] Phase 5: `docs/design/phase5-doctests.md` — `///` extraction syntax, scope/imports inside doctests, error attribution. See [docs/design/phase5-doctests.md](docs/design/phase5-doctests.md). Reserves error codes E0361–E0362.
- [x] Phase 6: `docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md` — exclusive-borrow tracking (`mut x: T` / `mut self` on non-`Copy`); aliasing-XOR-mutability; explicit lifetime annotation surface (spelling deferred to slice 6BC.5 — three candidates enumerated); `noalias` codegen; partial-place activation; drop-flag specialization. See [docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md](docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md). Reserves error codes E0380–E0386 (E0374 is the Phase-5-reserved partial-place code that activates here). Implementation in 5–7 sub-slices (6BC.1–6BC.5 + 6BC.codegen + 6BC.opt).
- [x] Phase 7: `docs/design/phase7-generics.md` — parametric polymorphism via `[T]` brackets; bounded polymorphism via `T: Ord + Eq`; `interface Name { ... }` declarations + `impl Interface for Type { ... }` blocks; `Self` keyword; monomorphization at codegen; coherence (orphan rule); reserved error codes E0500–E0511. Implementation in 7–8 sub-slices (7GEN.1–6 + 7HEAP + 7EXIT). Explicitly out of scope for Phase 7 first cut: dynamic dispatch / `dyn Interface`, associated types, higher-kinded types, const generics, specialization, auto-derive attributes. See [docs/design/phase7-generics.md](docs/design/phase7-generics.md) §1–§9.
- [x] Phase 6: lifetime annotation spelling. **`borrow REGION T`** at type position (parameter / field / return). New reserved keyword `borrow`. Composes orthogonally with `mut` / `move` parameter markers. Region names are ordinary identifiers, local to one signature. Picked over the Rust-shaped apostrophe-prefix form (which imports the tick-letter cosmetic and a separate `<'a>` declaration list) and over the `where return borrows ...` clause form (which separates constraint from parameters and risks confusion with Phase-7 generic constraints). Reasoning: §2.8c "verbosity exposes hidden rules" — `borrow A T` reads top-to-bottom and tells a reader-without-context exactly what the annotation means, where `'a` is opaque until learned. See [phase6-borrow-exclusive.md](docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md) §4.2.
- [ ] Phase 7+ (speculative): effect tracking syntax (`fn pure`, `fn allocates`, etc.) — Koka/Roc/OCaml 5 references
- [ ] Phase 7+ (speculative): contracts syntax (`requires`, `ensures`) — Eiffel/Dafny references

Resolved (kept for history):
- **Phase 11 library proof-points + small bug fixes landed (2026-05-13):** three "well-scoped, ready to start" items from the post-FN_PTR status snapshot, all delivered in one session:
  - **`?T` audit** — verified no `?` token, no `?T` parse paths, no nullable-type machinery anywhere in the codebase. The `?T` reservation was design-note-only and never landed. Closed.
  - **Allocator + VecI32 reference library** — [docs/examples/phase11_vec_allocator.cplus](docs/examples/phase11_vec_allocator.cplus). Demonstrates the Dart-FFI pattern in pure C+ source: `interface Allocator` + `CMalloc` impl wrapping libc `malloc/realloc/free`, plus a concrete `VecI32` with `push` (realloc-on-grow) / `get` / `set` / `drop`. Uses `size_of::[i32]()` for byte-count math, raw pointer reinterpretation for the typed buffer, full Drop semantics. **Sample exits 36** (sum of 1..=8 via 8 pushes, exercising the realloc path from cap 4 → 8 → 16). Round-trips clean through `cpc fmt`. The fully-generic `Vec[T, A: Allocator]` is partially specced in the sample's header comment but blocked on two known deferred limitations (generic-fn return types mentioning generic structs don't substitute T at the call site; `Type[args]::assoc_fn(...)` shape not yet wired) — concrete VecI32 demonstrates the pattern without those.
  - **`cocoa-min` package** — [objc-c-interop/cocoa-min/hello_appkit.cplus](objc-c-interop/cocoa-min/hello_appkit.cplus) + [build.sh](objc-c-interop/cocoa-min/build.sh) + [README.md](objc-c-interop/cocoa-min/README.md). Reproduces [objc-c-interop/hello_appkit_c.c](objc-c-interop/hello_appkit_c.c) entirely in C+ source. Compiles via `cpc --emit-ll`, links against `-framework Cocoa -lobjc` via clang. Verified end-to-end: runs the AppKit event loop (process stays alive past `[NSApp run]` entry, would draw an 800x500 window if a GUI were attached). Exercises all four Phase-11 ObjC slices simultaneously: 11.LINKNAME (10 typed `objc_msgSend` aliases via `#[link_name = "objc_msgSend"]`), 11.INTPTR (`0 as *u8` for NULL sender args), 11.FN_PTR (the `should_terminate_after_last_window_closed` C+ fn coerced to `fn(*u8, *u8, *u8) -> i8` and passed as IMP to `class_addMethod`), 11.LAYOUT (`size_of` available but not actually used in the demo), plus Phase 10 (`extern fn` + raw pointers + `unsafe` + `#[repr(C)]` for NSRect/NSPoint/NSSize). New e2e test `phase11_cocoa_min_compiles_and_links` (macOS-only) pins regression. **This is the first real C+ desktop app.**
  - **Collateral bug fixes** uncovered while writing the Vec sample:
    - **Raw-pointer reinterpretation cast** (`*u8 as *T`) added to `cast_allowed` in [cplus-core/src/sema.rs](cplus-core/src/sema.rs) and to `gen_cast` in [cplus-core/src/codegen.rs](cplus-core/src/codegen.rs). Gated on `unsafe_depth > 0` with E0801 (same gate as int→ptr). Codegen is a no-op — both ends lower to LLVM `ptr`. The standard idiom for treating an allocator-returned byte buffer as a typed pointer. New sema unit tests + 2 e2e tests pin clean-in-unsafe / E0801-outside-unsafe.
    - **`expr_value_ty` extended with `ExprKind::Cast`** in [cplus-core/src/codegen.rs](cplus-core/src/codegen.rs). Pre-existing codegen bug: if-expressions whose arms ended in a cast (`if c { 8 as usize } else { 16 as usize }`) returned `None` as their type, no result slot was allocated, the if produced no value, and `let init` crashed with "let init produces a value". Fix recognizes primitive Path types and recursive RawPtr at the cast target. New e2e test `phase11_if_expr_with_usize_arms_compiles`.
    - **Formatter spacing** for unary-prefix `*p` (deref) and type-position `*T` after `as` (cast target) in [cplus-core/src/fmt.rs](cplus-core/src/fmt.rs). Pre-existing bug surfaced by the Vec sample: `*p` formatted as `* p` (treating `*` as binary), `as *i32` formatted as `as * i32` (the type-position-anchor set didn't include `As`). Extended `needs_space_between_ctx` to recognize `As` and `LBracket` as type-position anchors for `*`, plus a unary-prefix detection for `*` after expression-start tokens (operators, openers, statement boundaries).
  - **Test total: 869** (682 library + 176 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Formatter round-trips every sample clean.
- **Phase 11 slice 11.FN_PTR (function pointer types + values) landed (2026-05-13):** the final compiler gap from the ObjC interop notes. After this slice, **the `cocoa-min` package is fully library work** — no further compiler changes needed for the ObjC desktop-app story. Design note (pre-implementation spec): [docs/design/phase11-fn-pointers.md](docs/design/phase11-fn-pointers.md). **Coordinated changes:**
  - **AST**: new `TypeKind::FnPtr { params: Vec<Type>, return_type: Option<Box<Type>> }`. Threaded through every TypeKind-matching site: borrowck (CopyOracle's `definitely_non_copy` + `is_type_copy_internal` — FnPtr is Copy), codegen (`ty_from`), monomorphize (`rewrite_self_in_type`, `subst_type_ast`, `type_ast_to_ty`, `ty_to_type_ast`), resolver (`rewrite_type` recurses into params + return), sema (`resolve_type`, `resolve_field_type_with_subst`, `substitute_param_in_type_ast`).
  - **Ty**: new `Ty::FnPtr { params: Vec<Ty>, return_type: Box<Ty> }`. Added to `is_atomic_copy`, `name`, `subst_ty`, `ty_display`. Codegen's `is_copy_ty` returns true; `llvm_ty` returns `"ptr"`. Two new mangling sites in sema and monomorphize (`mangle_ty_for_name`, `mangle_ty`) render fn-pointer types as `fn_p1_p2_ret_r` for symbol-safe names.
  - **Parser**: new `TokenKind::Fn` branch in `parse_type`. Consumes `(`, parameter type list, optional `-> R`. Distinguished from declaration form because parse_type is never called at item-declaration position.
  - **Sema**:
    - `resolve_value_ident` extended with a `expected: Option<Ty>` parameter. When expected is `Ty::FnPtr { .. }` and the name resolves to a non-generic fn, return the fn's signature as `Ty::FnPtr` (the coercion). Without an expected-FnPtr hint, fn-as-value keeps the historical **E0312** ("function used as a value"). Generic fns named in value position fire new **E0821** ("cannot take address of generic function `X` without specifying type parameters").
    - `check_call` adds two pre-dispatch indirect-call paths. (1) When callee is `Ident(name)` and the local's type is `Ty::FnPtr`, validate args against the pointer's param types and return the pointer's return type. Arity mismatches fire **E0308**; turbofish on a FnPtr-typed local fires **E0501** ("indirect calls do not accept type arguments"). (2) When callee is `Field { receiver, name }` and the field's type is `Ty::FnPtr`, same indirect-call dispatch via the struct's field table. Falls through to the existing named-call / method-call paths when neither pattern matches.
    - `check_expr_kind` passes `expected` through to `resolve_value_ident` so the coercion fires in the right contexts (let-init, struct-field-init, fn-arg, return position — every site that has an expected-type hint already does the right thing).
  - **Codegen**:
    - `gen_expr`'s Ident arm: when `name` is in `self.sigs` (a fn), emit the SSA value `@<symbol>` (using `link_name` if set) with type `Ty::FnPtr` derived from the sig. No instruction needed — LLVM accepts a function-symbol literal as a `ptr` value.
    - `gen_call` adds two indirect-call paths matching sema's:
      - Ident-bound-to-FnPtr-local: `%v = load ptr, ptr <slot>`, then `gen_indirect_call(%v, params, return, args)`.
      - Field-of-FnPtr-type: `gen_place(receiver)` → struct address, `getelementptr` to the field, `load ptr`, then `gen_indirect_call`.
    - New helper `gen_indirect_call(callee_val, params, return_type, args)`: evaluates each arg, emits `call <retty> %callee(<args>)` (or `call void` for unit-returning callbacks). All indirect calls use the C calling convention by default.
  - **Formatter**: new spacing rule in `needs_space_between_ctx` — when prev is `Fn` and curr is `LParen`, suppress the space. This is unambiguous because `fn(...)` only ever appears in fn-pointer type position (declaration form `fn name(...)` has an ident between the `fn` and the `(`).
  - **Sample**: [docs/examples/phase11_fn_pointers.cplus](docs/examples/phase11_fn_pointers.cplus) — exercises bare-ident coercion, fn-as-fn-param, struct-of-callbacks. Returns 42. Round-trips clean through `cpc fmt`.
  - **Smoke verified**: cross-language FFI works — passed a C+ fn to libc's `atexit` and observed the C runtime calling our fn during process teardown. The headline ObjC-interop-style pattern.
  - **Tests added** (9 sema unit + 5 e2e = 14): sema pins clean-cases for let-binding / no-return / struct-field / fn-param / extern-fn-sig coercion; rejects signature mismatch (E0302), bare-fn-without-expected (E0312), generic-fn-as-pointer (E0821), wrong arity (E0308). E2E: `phase11_fn_pointer_demo_runs` (the sample), `phase11_fn_pointer_indirect_call_via_local_runs`, `phase11_fn_pointer_struct_field_runs`, `phase11_fn_pointer_to_libc_atexit_runs` (cross-language FFI — pass C+ fn to libc, observe callback), `phase11_fn_pointer_signature_mismatch_rejected_e0302`. **Test total: 864** (682 library + 171 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored.
  - **What this unblocks**: the `cocoa-min` package now writes entirely in C+ source — `class_addMethod(class, sel, app_should_terminate_handler, types)` resolves with `app_should_terminate_handler` as a named C+ fn coerced to the C-ABI fn-pointer type that `class_addMethod` expects via its `extern fn` declaration. Combined with **11.LINKNAME** (`#[link_name = "objc_msgSend"]` for the typed-msgSend aliases), **11.INTPTR** (`0 as *u8` for NULL sender args), **11.LAYOUT** (`size_of[NSRect]()` for any struct-allocation needs), and **Phase 10** (`extern fn`, raw pointers, `unsafe`, varargs, `#[repr(C)]`), every primitive the C reference at [objc-c-interop/hello_appkit_c.c](objc-c-interop/hello_appkit_c.c) uses is now expressible in C+. The next step is a `cocoa-min` package itself; that's user library work, not compiler work.
  - **What's deferred** (recorded for future):
    - **Generic fn instantiations as fn pointers** (`let id_i32: fn(i32) -> i32 = identity::[i32];`). Sema's expected-FnPtr coercion only handles non-generic fns today; the turbofish form would need its own path. Defer until motivated.
    - **Method pointers** — `let translate: fn(*Point, i32, i32) = Point::translate;`. Methods have implicit `self`; modeling that needs extra type-system machinery. ObjC delegates work via plain fns (the C reference's `app_should_terminate_after_last_window_closed` is a free function, not a method), so this isn't blocking.
    - **Function pointer equality** — `cmp1 == cmp2` for callback de-registration APIs. Defer until a real consumer asks.
    - **Variadic fn pointers** — `fn(*u8, ...) -> i32` for `printf`-style. Not needed for ObjC (msgSend uses fixed-arity typed aliases via `#[link_name]`).
    - **Function pointer null literal** — `0 as fn(...)` parses today (the parser accepts a generic int-to-ptr cast and sema gates on Ty::RawPtr) but specifically casting to FnPtr isn't yet wired into `cast_allowed`. Trivial to add when a user case appears (e.g. `signal(SIGTERM, 0 as fn(i32))` to clear a signal handler).
- **Phase 11 slices 11.INTPTR (`0 as *T`) + 11.LINKNAME (`#[link_name = "..."]`) landed (2026-05-13):** the second and third compiler gaps from the ObjC interop notes ([objc-c-interop/notes.md](objc-c-interop/notes.md)) closed in one session. Together with 11.LAYOUT (also 2026-05-13), these complete two of the three blockers for a real `cocoa-min` package; only slice 11.FN_PTR (function pointer types and values) remains. **Coordinated changes:**
  - **11.INTPTR (integer-to-raw-pointer cast, P3 from null design):** [cplus-core/src/sema.rs](cplus-core/src/sema.rs) `cast_allowed` extended with `from.is_int() && matches!(to, Ty::RawPtr(_))`; `check_cast` enforces `unsafe_depth > 0` after the type-shape check, firing E0801 ("integer-to-pointer cast requires `unsafe { ... }`") on the cast span. Codegen ([cplus-core/src/codegen.rs](cplus-core/src/codegen.rs) `gen_cast`) emits `inttoptr i64 %v to ptr` with a leading `sext`/`zext` to i64 when the source is narrower (LLVM's `inttoptr` requires its operand to be the pointer-width integer; on our 64-bit targets that's i64). Sema unit tests pin clean-in-unsafe / E0801-outside-unsafe / `usize as *T` / `**i32` nested cast. E2E: `phase11_int_to_ptr_cast_inside_unsafe_compiles` (runs `unsafe { 0 as *u8 }` through `free(null)`, which is a POSIX no-op, exit 0), `phase11_int_to_ptr_cast_outside_unsafe_rejected_e0801`. This is the implementation of P3 from the null-handling design — the FFI-null spelling. The word "null" never enters the source vocabulary; P1/P2/P5 from the null principles all stay intact.
  - **11.LINKNAME (`#[link_name = "..."]`):** new parser shape — `parse_one_attribute` admits `#[name = value]` after the path ident (in addition to the existing `#[name]` and `#[name(...)]` shapes). The `value` is parsed as Str or Ident and stored as a single positional `AttrArg::Str` / `AttrArg::Ident`, so attrs-validation reads the same shape it would from `#[name("value")]`. New `ArgsSpec::ExactlyOneStr` variant in [cplus-core/src/attrs.rs](cplus-core/src/attrs.rs); new `link_name` entry in `KNOWN_ATTRS` with `targets: TARGET_FN`. New `emit_expected_str_arg` helper for E0355 ("requires exactly one string-literal argument"). Parser's `parse_extern_fn` no longer rejects attributes — Phase-10's `attributes are not supported on extern declarations in slice 10.FFI.1` restriction relaxed (was originally placeholder; now needed for link_name). Sema's `FnSig` gained `link_name: Option<String>` populated by new `extract_link_name(&[Attribute])` helper in `collect_functions`; sema fires **E0356** on `link_name` placed on non-extern fns ("`#[link_name]` is only valid on `extern fn` declarations"). Codegen's `FnSig` gained the same field, populated identically; `gen_function`'s extern path now uses `sig.link_name.as_deref().unwrap_or(&f.name.name)` as the symbol both for `declare` emission and the printf/memcmp preamble-dedup check. New per-codegen-pass `emitted_extern_symbols: HashSet<String>` threaded through `gen_function` so two extern decls aliasing the same symbol emit exactly one `declare`. Call sites (`gen_named_call` after the existing intrinsic dispatch) use the link_name at the `@<symbol>` position when present. Sema unit tests pin clean shape / E0356-on-non-extern / two-decls-same-symbol-clean. E2E: `phase11_link_name_aliases_symbol_runs` (declares libc's `abs` under the C+ name `my_abs`, calls it, asserts exit 42), `phase11_link_name_emits_alias_in_ir` (IR shape: `declare i32 @abs(i32)` with no `@my_abs`), `phase11_link_name_dedups_multiple_decls` (two aliases → exactly one `declare`, both callable), `phase11_link_name_on_non_extern_fn_rejected` (E0356 from `cpc build`).
  - **Tests added** (7 sema unit + 6 e2e = 13): see the per-slice notes above. **Test total: 850** (673 library + 166 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Formatter still round-trips every sample clean.
  - **What's still deferred for ObjC**: **slice 11.FN_PTR** — function pointer types (`fn(T1, T2) -> R`) and values (bare-ident type-directed coercion). Required for `class_addMethod(class, sel, IMP, types)` and any C callback API. Design note landed at [docs/design/phase11-fn-pointers.md](docs/design/phase11-fn-pointers.md) (2026-05-13) — pending user approval before implementation. ~1 day estimated. After 11.FN_PTR, the `cocoa-min` package is fully library work, no further compiler changes needed.
- **Phase 11 slice 11.LAYOUT (`size_of[T]()` / `align_of[T]()` intrinsics) landed (2026-05-13):** the load-bearing slice from the 7HEAP reframe. Two new compiler intrinsics that take exactly one type argument via turbofish (`size_of::[i32]()`), no value arguments, return `usize`. Both are safe (no `unsafe` block required) — they're pure compile-time-resolvable layout queries that LLVM constant-folds at -O1+. **Coordinated changes**:
  - **Sema** ([cplus-core/src/sema.rs](cplus-core/src/sema.rs) `check_named_call`): new intrinsic-recognition branch inserted *before* the E0501 turbofish-on-non-generic-fn rejection. Validates `type_args.len() == 1` (else E0501 "takes exactly 1 type argument"), validates `args.is_empty()` (else E0302 "takes no value arguments"), resolves the single type arg via `resolve_type` (any unresolved name fires the existing E0303 path), returns `Ty::Usize`. Same shape as the existing `println` / `str_ptr` / `str_len` / `str_from_raw_parts` intrinsic dispatch — compiler-known names, not user-overloadable.
  - **Codegen** ([cplus-core/src/codegen.rs](cplus-core/src/codegen.rs) `gen_named_call`): signature widened to accept `type_args: &[Type]` (also threaded through `gen_call` and the call dispatch at `gen_expr`'s `ExprKind::Call` match arm — previously discarded with `..`). New emission branches for both intrinsics:
    - `size_of`: `%p = getelementptr T, ptr null, i64 1` + `%r = ptrtoint ptr %p to i64`. The GEP-null trick: at offset `sizeof(T) * 1` from null, then convert to integer.
    - `align_of`: `%p = getelementptr {i1, T}, ptr null, i64 0, i32 1` + `%r = ptrtoint ptr %p to i64`. LLVM places T at the alignment boundary of T after the i1's storage, so the offset of T's start equals alignof(T).
    - Both call `ty_from(&type_args[0], &self.types)` to recover the `Ty` from the AST type, then `llvm_ty` for the LLVM rendering. Aggregate types feed through unchanged — `size_of::[Point]()` resolves to `Point`'s mangled name (or post-monomorphize concrete name for generic-struct instantiations).
  - **Monomorphize** ([cplus-core/src/monomorphize.rs](cplus-core/src/monomorphize.rs) `rewrite_expr` Call arm): bug fix — previously cloned `type_args` verbatim, so `size_of::[T]()` (or any intrinsic taking a type arg) inside a generic body would keep the literal `T` and panic at codegen on `Ty::Param("T")`. Fix: substitute each type_arg via `subst_type_ast` with the active `subst` map. Now `fn typed_size[T]() -> usize { return size_of::[T](); }` correctly monomorphizes into one concrete function per instantiation. The companion `rewrite_expr_self` (Self-name rewrite pass) was already correct — line 416 had been calling `rewrite_self_in_type` on each type_arg since slice 7GEN.5e step 3; only the subst-pass had the latent bug.
  - **Sample** [docs/examples/phase11_size_of.cplus](docs/examples/phase11_size_of.cplus): exercises both intrinsics on primitives (i8/i32/i64) and an aggregate (`Point` struct with two i32 fields). Prints the 6 primitive layouts + 1 struct layout, exits with the size of Point (8 bytes on x86_64/aarch64). Round-trips clean through `cpc fmt`.
  - **Tests added** (11 sema unit + 3 e2e = 14): sema pins clean-cases for primitives / struct / raw pointer / inside-generic-fn / usize-arithmetic; rejects missing type arg (E0501), wrong arity (E0501), value arg (E0302), unknown type (E0303). E2E: `phase11_size_of_align_of_demo_runs` (the headline sample's exit + stdout shape), `phase11_size_of_inside_generic_fn_runs` (locks the monomorphize substitution fix), `phase11_size_of_no_type_arg_rejected` (E0501 from `cpc build`). **Test total: 837** (666 library + 160 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored.
  - **What this unblocks**: the Dart-FFI-style `Allocator` interface pattern is now expressible entirely at user level. Pseudocode:
    ```
    interface Allocator {
        fn allocate(self, bytes: usize, align: usize) -> *u8;
        fn deallocate(mut self, ptr: *u8, bytes: usize);
    }
    struct CMalloc {}
    impl Allocator for CMalloc {
        fn allocate(self, bytes: usize, align: usize) -> *u8 { return unsafe { malloc(bytes) }; }
        fn deallocate(mut self, ptr: *u8, bytes: usize) { unsafe { free(ptr); } }
    }
    fn vec_with_capacity[T, A: Allocator](alloc: A, n: usize) -> Vec[T, A] {
        let bytes = n *% size_of::[T]();
        let p = alloc.allocate(bytes, align_of::[T]());
        return Vec[T, A] { ptr: p, len: 0, cap: n, alloc: alloc };
    }
    ```
    Each piece — `interface`, generic structs, generic impls, `extern fn malloc/free`, `size_of[T]()`, `align_of[T]()` — exists today. No further compiler work needed for the Allocator + Vec[T] story to land as a user library.
  - **Known formatter limitation surfaced (not blocking, deferred)**: the formatter doesn't yet recognize `*` after `[` (turbofish open bracket) as a type-position anchor, so `size_of::[*u8]()` reformats to `size_of::[* u8]()`. Sema and codegen accept the type correctly (`size_of_raw_pointer_type_clean` sema test pins this); only the round-trip-clean assertion on a sample using `[*u8]` would fail. The Phase-11 sample sticks to non-pointer type arguments to keep the sample-round-trip invariant green. Fix: extend `needs_space_between_ctx` in [cplus-core/src/fmt.rs](cplus-core/src/fmt.rs) to add `LBracket` to the type-position anchor set for `*`. ~5 line fix, separate polish slice when motivated.
  - **What's deferred for the full Dart-style story** (all library work, no language change required): writing the `Allocator` interface + `CMalloc` impl + generic `Vec[T, A]` + `Arena` (auto-free-on-defer) as a hand-rolled `cpc-alloc` package or in-tree sample. Until a real consumer asks for it, the pattern is documented but not landed.
- **7HEAP reframed as a Phase-11 polish slice (2026-05-13).** Originally scoped as a separate phase delivering heap-allocation primitives + an Allocator-as-parameter convention so growable `Vec[T]` could ship. After Phase 10 landed (`extern fn` + raw pointers + `unsafe` + varargs + `#[repr(C)]`), the heap-primitives half of 7HEAP became fully expressible at user level — proven by [docs/examples/owned_string.cplus](docs/examples/owned_string.cplus), which builds a typed owned-string-with-Drop on top of `extern fn malloc/free` with zero compiler support beyond Phase-10 primitives. The Dart-FFI parallel (a chat-session observation) sharpened the reframe: Dart's `package:ffi` provides an `Allocator` abstract class with `malloc`/`calloc` implementations that wrap libc directly — no parallel runtime, no GC integration, just a typed Dart API over the C heap. That pattern fits C+ exactly, because (a) §2.8b FFI honesty already forbids surface syntax that implies machinery the ABI doesn't carry, (b) C+ has no managed heap so the Dart GC/FFI split collapses to "the heap is the C heap, period," and (c) §2.6 stdlib-out-of-scope partitioning puts `Allocator` in user libraries, not the language. **What's left at the language level**: only `size_of[T]()` and `align_of[T]()` — pure compile-time-resolvable intrinsics that let user code compute byte counts for typed allocations. Both land as Phase-11 slice 11.LAYOUT (above). **What's library work**: an `interface Allocator { fn allocate(self, bytes: usize, align: usize) -> *u8; fn deallocate(mut self, ptr: *u8, bytes: usize); }`, a `CMalloc` impl wrapping libc, and a generic `Vec[T, A: Allocator]` built on those — all writable in C+ source today (modulo the size_of/align_of intrinsics). No separate design note needed; the Dart parallel + the OwnedString sample together document the pattern. **Phase 8 owned `string`** (deferred earlier with the same blocking reason as 7HEAP) gets unblocked alongside — once 11.LAYOUT lands, `string` becomes a library type built on top of `Allocator`. The same reframe.
- **Phase 10 (C interop hardening) core complete.** All four implementation slices landed in one session — 10.FFI.3 (`unsafe { }` blocks), 10.FFI.4 (varargs in extern fn), 10.FFI.5 (`#[repr(C)]` attribute), and 10.FFI.6 polish (formatter + exit demo). C+ now has the FFI surface needed to call any C library: declare external symbols, pass and receive raw pointers, gate dangerous operations behind explicit `unsafe` blocks, call variadic C functions like `printf`, and mark structs with stable C-compatible layout. The Phase-10 exit demo at [docs/examples/phase10_ffi.cplus](docs/examples/phase10_ffi.cplus) combines every Phase-10 feature in 27 source lines: `malloc → store via `*p` → printf via varargs → free`, all wrapped in `unsafe { }`, exit code 42 with stdout `"sum=42 count=3"`. Coordinated changes:
  - **10.FFI.3 — `unsafe { }` blocks**: new `ExprKind::Unsafe(Block)`. The `unsafe` keyword (reserved since Phase 1) now opens a block expression that's parsed exactly like a regular Block. Sema tracks `unsafe_depth: u32`; entering an `Unsafe` block increments, leaving decrements. Five operations gated by `unsafe_depth == 0` → **E0801**: pointer dereference `*p`, pointer indexing `p[i]`, calls to any extern fn (tracked via new `extern_fns: HashSet<String>` populated by `collect_functions`), the `str_from_raw_parts(p, n)` intrinsic. Pointer arithmetic `p + n` stays safe (it's just math; no memory access). `str_ptr(s)` / `str_len(s)` stay safe (they extract bytes from the fat-pointer, no UB possible). The block is statement-position-aware: added to `is_block_like` so `unsafe { ... } return 0;` parses without a trailing `;` (mirroring `if { ... }` / `match { ... }`). Threaded through 8 exhaustive-match sites in borrowck (4), codegen (3), lower, resolver, monomorphize (2) — `ExprKind::Unsafe(b)` aliases `ExprKind::Block(b)` for every pass except sema where the gating happens.
  - **10.FFI.4 — varargs in extern fn**: new lexer token `TokenKind::Ellipsis` (`...`). Lexer's `.` handler now upgrades `..` to `Ellipsis` on a third dot before falling through to `DotDotEq` / `DotDot`. New AST field `Function.is_variadic: bool`. `parse_extern_fn` consumes optional `, ...` after the last fixed param (variadic on non-extern fns is a parse error — the `...` only appears in `parse_extern_fn`). `FnSig` (sema and codegen both) gained `is_variadic: bool`. Sema call-site rule: variadic fns require `args.len() >= sig.params.len()` (fixed minimum), tail args type-check at their natural type. Codegen emits `(fixed_types, ...)` in the `declare` and the full function-type prefix at call sites (`call i32 (ptr, ...) @printf(...)` — LLVM requires this for varargs). Codegen-preamble dedup: extern fns named `printf` or `memcmp` skip their `declare` (they're already emitted by the preamble for the `println(str)` and `==`-on-str intrinsics; declaring twice would clash at link time).
  - **10.FFI.5 — `#[repr(C)]`**: new `AttrSpec` variant `ArgsSpec::OneIdentFrom(allowed_set)` in [cplus-core/src/attrs.rs](cplus-core/src/attrs.rs). New `repr` attribute in `KNOWN_ATTRS`: target `TARGET_STRUCT` only, args `OneIdentFrom(&["C"])`. New diagnostic helper `emit_bad_repr_arg` for E0355 with the "requires exactly one of: `C`" message. `StructDef.is_repr_c: bool` records the flag at `collect_type_names` time (`s.attributes.iter().any(|a| a.path.name == "repr")`). Codegen impact today is zero — our default struct layout already matches C on x86_64 for primitive-typed fields; the attribute is a *stability* commitment that future codegen optimizations (potential field reordering for size) won't break the C-ABI promise for `#[repr(C)]`-marked structs. Generic struct instantiations don't inherit `is_repr_c` — revisit when a real use case (FFI-compatible generic types) appears.
  - **10.FFI.6 — polish**: formatter gained two new spacing rules. (a) Type-position `*` (e.g. `*u8` in `extern fn malloc(n: usize) -> *u8;`) now formats tight on both sides — pre-fix it emitted `* u8` as if `*` were a binary operator. Implemented via new `prev_prev_kind` tracking in the Printer; when `prev` is `Star` and `prev_prev` is `Colon` / `Arrow` / `Star`, suppress the binary-op spacing. (b) Attribute prefix `#[` (e.g. `#[repr(C)]`) is tight — pre-fix it emitted `# [repr(C)]`. Implemented as a one-line rule: after `Pound`, no space.
  - **Existing tests updated**: the seven sample programs and six e2e tests that exercised extern fns / pointer ops at top-level now wrap them in `unsafe { ... }` blocks. The [owned_string.cplus](docs/examples/owned_string.cplus) sample's `OwnedString` impl methods each include the relevant `unsafe` scope (malloc/free wrapped in `unsafe { ... }`, push_str's memcpy + pointer arith wrapped, etc.). No test was dropped — every assertion still holds.
  - **Tests added** (12 sema unit + 5 attrs unit + 3 parser unit + 4 e2e + 2 samples = 26): sema pins (a) deref-outside-unsafe → E0801, (b) extern-call-outside-unsafe → E0801, (c) variadic extern fn accepts extra args clean, (d) variadic extern fn with too-few-fixed-args → E0308; attrs pins `#[repr(C)]` clean on struct, missing arg → E0355, invalid arg → E0355, target=fn → E0356, target=enum → E0356; parser pins extern fn with varargs, Ellipsis token, `*` token retained. E2E: `phase10_exit_demo_runs` (full FFI exit demo, exit 42 + stdout `"sum=42 count=3\n"`), `phase10_varargs_printf_runs` (varargs printf prints "answer = 42\n", returns 12), `phase10_repr_c_struct_runs` (clean build + run on `#[repr(C)]` struct), plus all six pre-existing Phase-10 e2e tests updated with `unsafe` wrappers. **Test total: 823** (655 library + 157 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Sanity bench at clang -O2 parity (0.95x build, 1.00x runtime).
  - **Reserved error codes**: E0801 — "operation requires `unsafe` block" (single code covers deref, indexing, extern call, str_from_raw_parts; the message identifies the specific operation). Allocated from the Phase-10 block E0800–E0810.
  - **What's deliberately deferred** (recorded for completeness):
    - **Cross-platform ABI verification.** Today verified on x86_64 macOS (the dev platform). x86_64 Linux, aarch64 macOS, and Windows-MSVC haven't been smoke-tested for ABI edge cases (struct-passing rules, varargs register conventions, `byval` / `sret` parameter attributes for large aggregates). This is hardware/infra work, not language work — Phase 10 ships the language surface and trusts LLVM's per-target C-ABI lowering. A future hardening pass per platform is the natural follow-up; not blocking.
    - **`cpc-bindgen`** (separate tool, marked stretch goal in original Phase-10 plan). Not implemented. Hand-written `extern fn` declarations work for now; cpc-bindgen lands when hand-writing bindings becomes painful (i.e., when a real C library is being consumed at scale).
    - **Calling-convention overrides** beyond the default `ccc`. Future syntax like `extern "fastcall" fn ...` or `extern "stdcall" fn ...` for non-default conventions (Windows API, etc.). Reserved as a future-syntax slot in the design; no in-tree consumer yet.
    - **ABI parameter attributes for large aggregates** (`byval` / `sret`) — these would be needed when passing a struct >2 registers across an extern fn boundary on some platforms. Today small structs pass through LLVM's default; large structs may or may not match the platform C ABI on x86_64 Linux specifically. Verified-against-a-real-target is the path forward.
- **Phase 10 slice 10.FFI.2 (pointer operations) + Phase 8 owned layer (user-level) landed.** With raw-pointer deref / store / indexing / arithmetic + three `str` bridge intrinsics (`str_ptr`, `str_len`, `str_from_raw_parts`), the owned-string story is **expressible entirely in user-level C+ source** — no compiler-blessed `string` type required. The Phase-8-and-10 exit demo at [docs/examples/owned_string.cplus](docs/examples/owned_string.cplus) defines `struct OwnedString { ptr: *u8, len: usize, cap: usize }` with `with_capacity` / `push_str(str)` / `as_str() -> str` / `drop`, builds `"Hello, " + "world!"`, prints `Hello, world!`, and exits with code 13 (the byte length). Drop fires on scope exit; memcpy from `str` literal bytes into the malloc'd buffer works through the FFI pointer ops. Coordinated changes across six files:
  - **Sema** (`Ty::Deref` path in `check_unary`): the long-standing E0312 rejection on `*p` is gone. Type rule: `*p` on `*T` returns `T`; on any other type fires E0302 ("dereference requires a raw pointer"). New `target_is_writable_place` branch admits `*p = v` as a write through the pointer (no mutability requirement on the pointer binding itself — what's mutated is the target memory). Indexing `p[i]` on `*T` returns the pointee (parallel rule to arrays). Pointer arithmetic `p + n` / `p - n` (for `n: usize`) returns `*T` — special-cased in `check_binary` before the numeric-operands gate. Three new compiler intrinsics added alongside `println`: `str_ptr(s: str) -> *u8`, `str_len(s: str) -> usize`, `str_from_raw_parts(p: *u8, n: usize) -> str` — each rejects mistyped args with E0302.
  - **Codegen**: `gen_unary` Deref arm emits `load TYPE, ptr %p`. `gen_place` Deref arm returns the pointer value itself (no extra alloca) so `*p = v` lowers to `store TYPE %v, ptr %p`. `gen_index` branches on receiver type — RawPtr loads the pointer from its slot and emits `getelementptr inbounds T, ptr %p, i64 %idx` (no bounds check — the pointer's length is unknown); arrays keep their existing bounds-checked GEP. `gen_binary` recognizes `RawPtr + usize` / `RawPtr - usize` before the float/integer dispatch and emits GEP; subtraction negates the index first. The three str-intrinsics emit `extractvalue { ptr, i64 } %s, 0` / `..., 1` and `insertvalue` chains respectively.
  - **Formatter** (`needs_space_between_ctx`): new context-aware spacing rule for `*` in type position. Pre-existing rule treated `*` as a binary operator (spaces around it). Without the fix, `extern fn malloc(n: usize) -> *u8;` would reformat to `... -> * u8;` and break sample round-trip. Solution: track `prev_prev_kind` in the Printer struct; when `prev` is `*` and `prev_prev` is `:` / `->` / `*` (the type-position anchor set), suppress the binary-op spacing.
  - **One concrete deferral, documented in the demo file's comments**: realloc-on-overflow for `push_str` isn't implemented in the sample — it pre-allocates capacity at construction. Wiring it is a 5-line `extern fn realloc(...)` + capacity check; deferred only because the demo doesn't need it. The full Vec-style growable-buffer pattern is the natural next polish step.
