  - **Tests added** (5 sema unit + 3 e2e + 1 sample = 9): sema pins deref-clean, deref-non-pointer-E0302, store-clean, indexing-clean, arithmetic-clean. E2E: `phase10_pointer_roundtrip_via_malloc_runs` (malloc → store → load → free → 42), `phase10_pointer_index_and_arithmetic_runs` (p[0/1/2] + (p+1) → 32), `phase10_owned_string_sample_runs` (the headline — runs the in-tree sample, asserts stdout `"Hello, world!"` and exit code 13). **Test total: 811** (646 library + 154 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Sanity bench at clang -O2 parity (~0.93x build, ~1.00x runtime).
  - **What's still deferred — explicitly**:
    - **`unsafe { ... }` gating.** Pointer operations are currently allowed anywhere. The plan reserves `unsafe` for Phase-10-or-later; gating the dangerous ops behind `unsafe` blocks is a follow-up. Until then, pointer code is dangerous by convention only.
    - **Phase 8 owned `string` as a built-in type.** The original Phase-8 plan had `string` as compiler-blessed. After 10.FFI.2 it's expressible at user-level, so the compiler doesn't need to know about it. The future home of a "stdlib" `String` / `Vec[T]` / `HashMap[K, V]` etc. is a separate stdlib project (§2.6 still out of scope for this plan).
    - **8.STR.5 `+` operator for strings.** §2.8 forbids user-defined operator overloading; the original plan made `+` a compiler-internal intrinsic on `string`. With user-level owned strings, there's no built-in target for `+` to overload; concat is `s.push_str(other.as_str())`. Re-evaluate when (and if) a stdlib `String` type is blessed.
    - **8.STR.4 `cstring` type.** A separate `cstring` newtype distinguishes "NUL-terminated for C interop" from owned UTF-8. Can be expressed as `struct cstring { ptr: *u8 }` at user level once a `from_string(s: string) -> cstring` helper exists; needs runtime NUL-check (sample-level work, not language work).
    - **8.STR.6 `Hash` for `str`.** Same situation — once a stdlib lands, hashing becomes `impl Hash for str { fn hash(self) -> u64 { ... fn body using as_bytes ... } }`. No compiler work.
  - **Reframing of Phase 8 status**: the view layer ships in the compiler (str + literals + escapes + println + `==`/`!=`). The owned layer lives at user level. Both are now functional. The headline original-Phase-8 commitment ("growable owned `string` you can pass between functions") is met by user-level construction.
- **Phase 10 slice 10.FFI.1 (extern fn + raw pointer type) landed.** The FFI foundation that Phase 1 had advertised but never implemented. C+ source can now declare external C symbols and bind them at link time; raw pointer types (`*T`, including nested `**T`) parse, type-check, and lower to LLVM `ptr`. The headline demo is the canonical libc smoke test: `extern fn abs(x: i32) -> i32; fn main() -> i32 { return abs(0 -% 42); }` compiles, links against the system libc's `abs`, and returns 42. **This is the dependency that was blocking the rest of Phase 8** — owned `string` + `to_cstring` + `+` concat + `Hash` can now be written as a user-level layer over `extern fn malloc/free/memcpy` instead of as compiler special-cases. Coordinated changes across nine files:
  - **AST** (`Function`): new field `is_extern: bool`. When `true`, the `body` field holds a synthesized empty `Block` (avoids touching every AST-walking site with an `Option<Block>` migration). New `TypeKind::RawPtr(Box<Type>)` for `*T`.
  - **Parser** (`parse_item` + new `parse_extern_fn`): admits `extern fn NAME(params) -> ret;` at item position. `pub` rejected (the C symbol is always reachable; `pub` is meaningless). Generic params rejected (extern symbols are concrete). Attributes rejected on extern fns in this slice (no use case yet). Trailing `;` required (no body). `parse_type` gained a `TokenKind::Star` branch — `*T` in type position unambiguously starts a raw pointer (`*` is the multiply operator elsewhere, but binary `*` only appears in expression position).
  - **Sema** (new `Ty::RawPtr(Box<Ty>)`): atomic-Copy: yes (a pointer is just an address — 8 bytes on 64-bit). `resolve_type` handles `TypeKind::RawPtr` by recursing on the inner type. `check_function` short-circuits when `is_extern` (no body to walk). The signature still flows into `fns` via `collect_functions` so calls type-check normally — `abs(0 -% 42)` checks arg shape against the declared `i32` parameter; passing `true` fires E0302 with the usual recipe.
  - **Resolver**: extern fn names are *not* file-qualified (the C symbol is fixed). `collect_items` skips inserting extern fns into the `all`/`local_items` table, so call-site rewriting leaves `abs` literal; `rewrite_fn` skips the name qualification but still walks param/return types (in case they reference C+ structs).
  - **Codegen**: `gen_function` branches on `is_extern` — emits `declare TYPE @name(PARAM_TYPES)` (no body, no parameter attributes) and returns early. Param attributes (`noalias`/`readonly` from 6BC.codegen) are skipped for extern fns; those are only sound for C+ fns whose call sites the borrow checker has analyzed. `Ty::RawPtr(_)` lowers to LLVM `"ptr"` regardless of pointee (pointee info is sema-only). `is_copy_ty` and `ty_from` both handle the new variant.
  - **Monomorphize**: `mangle_ty` and `ty_to_type_ast` handle `Ty::RawPtr` (mangled as `ptr_<inner>` for symbol-safe rendering). `subst_type_ast` and `rewrite_self_in_type` recurse into `TypeKind::RawPtr`. Extern fns survive monomorphize unchanged (they're never generic).
  - **Borrowck**: `CopyOracle::definitely_non_copy` returns false for `TypeKind::RawPtr` (raw pointers are atomic-Copy); `is_type_copy_internal` returns true. Pointers participate in `mut`/`move` parameter analysis as Copy types (no borrow tracking, no E0370 family fires on them).
  - **Tests added** (6 sema unit + 7 parser unit + 3 e2e = 16): sema pins clean extern fn use, E0302 on wrong-type arg, `*u8` param accepted, `let p: *u8 = malloc(...)` clean (allocator return bound to local), `**i32` nested pointer accepted, Copy semantics (pointer can be passed to two functions without move tracking). Parser pins basic extern fn shape, no-return-type variant, body-rejected, `pub`-rejected, generic-params-rejected, `*u8` parses to RawPtr, nested `**i32` parses as `RawPtr(RawPtr(i32))`. E2E: `phase10_extern_fn_abs_runs` (compile + link against libc + run → exit 42), `phase10_extern_fn_emits_declare_not_define` (IR shape lock), `phase10_raw_pointer_in_extern_signature_compiles` (pointer flows through end-to-end). **Test total: 803** (641 library + 151 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Sanity bench at clang -O2 parity (~0.93–0.97x build, ~1.00x runtime).
  - **What's deferred to 10.FFI.2+**: **pointer operations** — deref `*p`, indexing `p[i]`, pointer arithmetic `p + n`, address-of `&x`. Today a `*u8` value can be stored, returned, and passed; no operations on the bytes it points to. Unblocking owned `string` requires deref + store-through-pointer (`*p = byte`) for `push_str`, plus pointer arithmetic for slicing. **Varargs in extern fns** — `extern fn printf(fmt: *u8, ...) -> i32;`. The `...` token isn't parsed; printf calls are still compiler intrinsics. **String literal → `*u8` conversion** — at the bridge between Phase-8 `str` and 10.FFI.1 pointers. Either a `str::as_ptr()` builtin (cheap, 1 LOC) or implicit conversion. **`unsafe` block reservation** — the design note says pointer operations live inside `unsafe { ... }`; the block syntax isn't parsed yet. **Struct-layout compatibility** (`#[repr(C)]`-equivalent) — open question whether to land as an attribute or default to "C+ struct layout matches C unless otherwise specified" (Phase 7 §coherence + §2.8d implies the latter).
  - **What's now unblocked for Phase 8**: the owned `string` slice (8.STR.4 → 8.STR.6) becomes a user-level construct once 10.FFI.2 lands the deref/store operations. The recipe per the Phase-8 deferred-rationale paragraph is `extern fn malloc(n: usize) -> *u8;` + `struct string { ptr: *u8, len: usize, cap: usize }` + `impl string { ... }` + `impl Drop for string`. None of that needs the compiler to special-case heap allocation.
- **Phase 8 partial (view layer) landed; owned layer deferred.** Slices 8.STR.1–.3 (str + literals, `println(str)`, `==`/`!=` on str) ship a fully usable string-view stack: programs can use string literals, type-annotate with `str`, pass str values around, print them, and compare them byte-by-byte. The FizzBuzz exit demo at [docs/examples/fizzbuzz.cplus](docs/examples/fizzbuzz.cplus) now prints real `"Fizz"`/`"Buzz"`/`"FizzBuzz"` strings instead of integer codes. Owned `string` + `to_cstring` + `+` concat + `Hash` are explicitly deferred until C interop foundations land (see below). Coordinated changes:
  - **Lexer**: string literals now decode `\n`/`\t`/`\r`/`\\`/`\"`/`\0` escape sequences (Phase 4's lexer rejected backslash entirely). The token payload is the *decoded* UTF-8 bytes — by the time parser sees `Str(...)`, escape processing is done. Unicode `\u{HHHH}` escapes are deferred (needs UTF-8 encoding of code points).
  - **AST + parser**: new `ExprKind::StrLit(String)`. `parse_primary` accepts `TokenKind::Str` and emits a `StrLit` expression. `can_start_expr` widened so a string literal works as a statement-start expression.
  - **Sema**: new `Ty::Str` variant. Atomic-Copy: yes (a view, not an owner). Resolves from the type name `str` in `resolve_type`. Built-in `println` becomes a *type-dispatched intrinsic*: `println(i32)` and `println(str)` both accept, neither user-overloadable (§2.8 still rules; the dispatch is compiler-internal). Argument typed neither i32 nor str fires **E0302** with a "println accepts i32 or str" recipe. `Ty::Str` participates in `==`/`!=` (sema accepts and returns Bool; codegen does the right thing — see below).
  - **Codegen**: a new pre-pass `collect_and_emit_str_lits` walks the program before function emission, dedupes string literals by content, and emits `@.str.N = private unnamed_addr constant [N+1 x i8] c"...\00"` globals (length includes a trailing NUL so a future `to_cstring()` can hand the same buffer to C). The expression's SSA value is built via two `insertvalue` instructions into `{ ptr, i64 }` (16 bytes on 64-bit, passed by value). `println(str)` extracts (ptr, len), truncates len to i32, and calls `printf` with the format string `@.fmt_str_nl = "%.*s\n\0"`. `==`/`!=` on `str` operands lowers to a length-prechecked `memcmp` call: equal lengths route through `call i32 @memcmp(...)`; unequal lengths short-circuit to `false` via the same alloca+branch pattern used by `gen_short_circuit`. New IR declarations in the preamble: `declare i32 @memcmp(ptr, ptr, i64)`.
  - **Threaded plumbing**: `FnState` gained a `&'a StrLitTable` field; both `gen_function` and `gen_method` callers now thread `&str_lits` through `FnState::new`. `is_copy_ty` and `llvm_ty` both pattern-match `Ty::Str`. `ty_from` accepts `"str"` so type annotations work in field/param positions (this was the bug that initially crashed `let s: str = "x"` until the codegen-side name lookup got the `"str"` mapping).
  - **Tests added** (6 codegen + 6 sema + 3 e2e + 1 sample = 16): codegen pins literal-global emission shape, content-dedup, fat-pointer construction via insertvalue, `%.*s` format string for `println(str)`, memcmp call for `==`, escape byte `\0A` for `\n`. Sema pins clean type-annotated and inferred literal use, `println(str)` clean, `println(true)` rejected with E0302, str `==` returns bool, str in fn params. E2E: `phase8_println_str_runs`, `phase8_str_equality_runs`, `phase8_fizzbuzz_exit_demo_runs` (locks the 15-line FizzBuzz output structurally). **Test total: 787** (628 library + 148 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Sanity bench at clang -O2 parity (~0.90–0.97x build, ~1.00–1.02x runtime).
  - **What's deferred — owned `string` + concat + cstring + Hash (slices 8.STR.4–.6).** The root cause is that **C interop foundations don't actually exist yet** despite the plan suggesting they "land earlier in Phase 1." Only the lexer's `Extern` token landed. The full path — parser for `extern fn name(params) -> ret;`, raw pointer type `*T`, codegen wiring for `declare ptr @malloc(i64)` etc. — is still in front of us in Phase 10. Without that path, owned `string` would have to be a deeply special-case built-in: codegen would emit its own malloc/free calls (like it does for `printf`), and `string::push_str(mut self, s: str)` would compile to a hardcoded codegen pattern. That's the wrong direction: strings should be a thin user-level layer on top of `extern fn malloc/free/memcpy`, the way they would naturally be written *in C+* once interop works. Doing the special-case version now would create dead code we'd delete the day Phase 10 lands.
    - **Concrete recommendation**: land slice **10.FFI.1** (parser + sema + codegen for `extern fn` declarations + raw pointer type `*T`, ~300–500 LOC) before resuming Phase 8. Once 10.FFI.1 is in, `string` becomes a user-level struct in a future `cpc-strings` library or compiler-bundled prelude — no special-case codegen required. The path is: `extern fn malloc(n: usize) -> *u8;` + `struct string { ptr: *u8, len: usize, cap: usize }` + `impl string { ... }` + `impl Drop for string { fn drop(mut self) { free(self.ptr); } }`.
    - **What stays cleanly inside Phase 8**: the view layer that *did* land. There is no scope-cut regret here — the view layer is independently useful (`println("Hello")`, `s == "expected"`, FizzBuzz with real strings), and was the load-bearing piece for the demos that motivated this phase.
- **Phase 7 (generics + interfaces) complete:** all sub-slices except 7HEAP have landed. The Phase-7 exit demo at [docs/examples/phase7_generics.cplus](docs/examples/phase7_generics.cplus) compiles and runs cleanly, returning 42. It exercises every Phase-7 feature in one program: a generic struct `Pair[A, B]` with methods (`first(self) -> A`, `second(self) -> B`), a generic enum `Maybe[T]` with source-level patterns (`Maybe[i32]::Some(v) =>` / `Maybe[i32]::None =>`), a generic function with inference + a `T: Copy` bound, a blessed-interface user impl (`impl Ord for Point { fn cmp(...) -> i32 }`), and a generic method on a concrete impl with turbofish (`b.cast::[i32](0)`). E2E test `phase7_exit_demo_runs` locks the exit code at 42.
  - **What Phase 7 ships**: parametric polymorphism via `[T]` brackets (struct, enum, fn, method); bounded polymorphism via `T: Ord + Eq`; `interface Name { ... }` declarations + `impl Interface for Type { ... }` blocks; five compiler-blessed interfaces (`Copy`, `Eq`, `Ord`, `Hash`, `Clone`); `Self` keyword; monomorphization at codegen; coherence (orphan rule); error codes E0500–E0511.
  - **Test surface**: 771 total (615 library + 145 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. The Phase 7 work added 160 net tests since Phase 6 close (was 611). Sanity bench preserved at clang -O2 parity throughout.
  - **What's deferred — slice 7HEAP**: heap allocator (`malloc`/`free` + allocator-as-parameter convention from §2.2) is its own phase. Without heap, growable collections (Vec[T] with push/pop) can't be expressed; the exit demo uses inline-typed generics instead. This is a deliberate scope cut — generics-without-heap covers `Pair[A, B]`, `Option[T]`/`Maybe[T]`, `Result[T, E]`, `Box[T]`-by-value, and all generic-method-on-generic-typed-impl patterns. The literal `Vec[T] { push(...), pop(...) }` ergonomic demo needs heap to be meaningful; lands in 7HEAP (heap-allocator slice that must precede Phase 8 strings).
  - **Other carry-forwards** (low priority — no in-tree use case): bounds on built-in primitives (`impl Ord for i32` — currently rejected; workaround is newtype wrapping); method-level generic bounds inside generic-typed impls (`impl Vec[T] { fn map[U: Clone](...) }` — `GenericImplMethodTemplate` doesn't yet carry method-bound info); generic-method-level recursive instantiation; auto-derive attributes (`#[derive(Eq)]` — design note records "first cut: don't"); body-checking of generic-typed-impl method bodies at template-collection time (deferred until bound-driven method resolution can stabilize signatures).
- **Phase 7 slices 7GEN.5e step 4 + 7GEN.6 (bound checking E0502 + blessed interfaces Copy/Eq/Ord/Hash/Clone) landed together:** generic bounds (`T: Ord`, `T: Copy`, `T: Ord + Eq`) are now validated at every instantiation site, and the five compiler-blessed interfaces are registered before user code parses. Users can write `impl Ord for Point { fn cmp(self, other: Point) -> i32 { ... } }` against the compiler's signature, and `fn max[T: Ord](a: T, b: T)` rejects `max(p, p)` for an `impl`-less `Point` with **E0502**. Coordinated changes:
  - **Sema — blessed interface registration**: new `register_blessed_interfaces` runs in `check_with_files_inner` before `collect_interfaces`. Inserts `Copy` (marker, no methods), `Eq` (`fn eq(self, other: Self) -> bool`), `Ord` (`fn cmp(self, other: Self) -> i32`), `Hash` (`fn hash(self) -> u64`), `Clone` (`fn clone(self) -> Self`). `Self` in those sigs is `Ty::Param("Self")`, consistent with the user-declared-interface convention. Any user `interface Eq { ... }` fires E0301 (duplicate type definition) — the names are reserved.
  - **Sema — manual Copy rejection (E0510)**: `validate_interface_impls` short-circuits when the interface is `Copy` and emits **E0510** "`Copy` cannot be manually implemented; it is structurally inferred from field types". The structural Copy flag (`is_copy` on StructDef/EnumDef, computed by `compute_struct_copy_flags`) remains the source of truth for `T: Copy` bound satisfaction.
  - **Sema — bound-checking machinery**: new `satisfies_bound(ty, bound)` returns true when `ty` satisfies a single interface bound: `Copy` routes through the structural `is_copy`; other bounds look up `interface_impls: HashSet<(interface_name, target_struct_name)>` keyed by the target's source name. New `check_generic_bounds(param_names, bounds, args, span, ctx)` iterates `(param, bound) ∈ bounds[i]` and emits **E0502** with `"type `T` does not satisfy bound `B` on type parameter `N` of CTX"` per violation. Wired into all four instantiation paths: `check_generic_named_call` (turbofish + inference branches), `check_generic_method_call` (method-level generics), `resolve_generic_instantiation` (generic struct `Wrapper[Point]`), `resolve_generic_enum_instantiation` (generic enum `Maybe[T: Ord]`).
  - **Sema — sig storage**: `GenericFnSig` gained `bounds: Vec<Vec<String>>` parallel to `generic_params`. `MethodSig` gained `generic_bounds: Vec<Vec<String>>` (empty for non-generic methods and for method-level generics inside generic-typed impls today). Five MethodSig construction sites updated.
  - **Existing tests touched**: `interface_decl_method_signature_clean` and `impl_interface_for_struct_matching_signature_clean` renamed their illustrative interface from `Ord` → `Compare` (no longer in the blessed-names namespace). The `phase7_generic_decls_and_impl_interface_clean` e2e test did the same swap.
  - **Tests added** (8 sema unit + 2 e2e = 10): sema unit pins (a) `impl Ord for Point` clean against blessed Ord, (b) `interface Ord` redeclaration fires E0301, (c) manual `impl Copy for X` fires E0510, (d) bound violation in generic-fn call fires E0502, (e) bound satisfied (after `impl Ord for Point`) clean, (f) `T: Copy` satisfied structurally by i32 clean, (g) `T: Copy` violated by a Drop struct fires E0502, (h) bound violation at generic-struct instantiation fires E0502. E2E: `phase7_bound_satisfied_runs` (builds + runs, returns 42 via `pick[T: Copy](42, 0)`) and `phase7_bound_violated_rejected_e0502` (negative case verifying E0502 in stderr). **Test total: 770** (615 library + 144 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Sanity bench still at clang -O2 parity.
  - **What's deferred**:
    - **Bounds on built-in primitives**: `impl Ord for i32` doesn't work today (`impl` targets must be structs). `T: Copy` against `i32` works (structural Copy is type-agnostic), but `T: Ord` against `i32` fails. Workaround: wrap in a newtype struct. Proper fix would route `impl Iface for Primitive` through a builtin-primitive method table; deferred until a real use case shows up.
    - **Compiler-implemented blessed-method bodies for primitives**: e.g. providing a default `Eq` for primitive integers without requiring user impls. Same trade-off as above — would either need a parallel primitive-method table or a virtual prelude that adds `impl Eq for i32 { ... }` syntactically. Out of scope for Phase 7.
    - **Method-level generic bounds inside generic-typed impls** (`impl Vec[T] { fn map[U: Clone](self, f: U) }`). The `GenericImplMethodTemplate` records method generic-params but doesn't yet carry their bounds; flow into the populated `MethodSig.generic_bounds` is empty today. No tested case yet.
    - **Auto-derive attributes** (`#[derive(Eq, Ord, Hash, Clone)]`). The design note (line 1114) records the rule "first cut: don't, can relax later." Manual impls are the only path today.
- **Phase 7 slice 7GEN.5e step 3 (generic-typed impls: `impl Box[T] { fn get(self) -> T }`) landed:** the Phase-7 exit-demo shape now works. A program defining `struct Box[T]` + `impl Box[T] { fn get(self) -> T; fn set(mut self, v: T); }` and using `Box[i32]` compiles and runs end-to-end. Methods on generic-typed impls survive the receiver's type instantiation: when sema synthesizes the concrete `Box__i32` StructDef, it also populates its methods table from the impl template, substituting `T → i32` and `Self → Box__i32`. Monomorphize emits one synthesized concrete `ImplBlock` per struct instantiation, carrying the substituted method bodies. Coordinated changes across two files:
  - **Sema**: `SemaCx` gained `generic_impl_methods: HashMap<String, Vec<GenericImplMethodTemplate>>` keyed by generic template name. `collect_methods` routes any impl with non-empty `target_generic_params` into a new `collect_generic_impl_methods` helper that (a) verifies the target is a known generic-struct template, (b) pushes impl-level + method-level param scopes for type resolution (Ty::Param values are now allowed in param/return types), (c) records each method as a `GenericImplMethodTemplate` carrying its receiver, pre-Param-resolved params, return type, impl-level and method-level generic param names. `resolve_generic_instantiation` (when synthesizing `Box__i32`) walks `generic_impl_methods[name]` and for each template builds the `T → concrete` substitution, applies it via `subst_ty` to params/return, then substitutes `Self → Ty::Struct(new_id)` via `subst_self`, and inserts a regular `MethodSig` on the new struct. Method-call dispatch (`b.get()`) then works through the existing path — sema sees the synthesized struct has `get` in its methods table.
  - **Monomorphize**: new helper `synthesize_generic_typed_impls` runs for each ItemKind::Impl with non-empty `target_generic_params`. For each matching entry in `mono.struct_instantiations` (same template name + arity), it builds the impl-level substitution map, clones each method, applies `subst_type_ast` (existing helper) to param/return types, applies `rewrite_self_in_type` (new) to replace `Path("Self")` references with `Path("Box__i32")`, then walks the body via `rewrite_block_with_self` (new) which first does the standard subst rewrite and then a second-pass `Self`-name rewrite over expression types and `Self`-named struct literals. The original generic-typed impl is dropped from the output (no `out_items.push`). Synthesized impls carry `target_generic_params: []`, `target: Ident(mangled)`, and concrete method clones.
  - **Codegen**: unchanged — the synthesized concrete impls feed through the existing non-generic method codegen path. The earlier `m.generic_params.is_empty() else continue` skip from step 2 plus the dropped generic templates from this step mean codegen never sees Ty::Param.
  - **Tests added** (3 sema unit + 2 e2e = 5): sema unit pins (a) `impl Box[T] { fn get(self) -> T }` clean, (b) `impl Box[T] { fn replace(mut self, v: T) }` clean with payload-uses-T, (c) two-param `impl Pair[A, B] { fn first(self) -> A; fn second(self) -> B }` clean. E2E: `phase7_generic_typed_impl_runs` (build + run, returns 42) and `phase7_generic_typed_impl_mut_self_runs` (mutable setter + getter, returns 42). **Test total: 759** (606 library + 142 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Sanity bench still at clang -O2 parity.
  - **What's deferred to a later slice**:
    - **Body-checking of generic-typed-impl method bodies in sema.** Today bodies are not body-checked at template-collection time (the StructDef doesn't exist yet, and Ty::Param has no operations available without bounds). Errors in template bodies surface only at instantiation time via codegen — which means a typo in a generic method body might compile if the type happens to permit the operation but fail surprisingly on a different instantiation. This is the same trade-off Rust pre-1.0 had before bounds drove early-check. Fixes properly with slice 7GEN.5e step 4 (bounds) + a per-instantiation sema pass.
    - **`impl Vec[T]` with array-of-T slice fields.** The headline `Vec[T]` exit demo needs `T[]` (slice of T) field support; today the slice-element type is a `Ty::Param("T")` which works for storage but doesn't have the heap-backed `push`-grows-the-array semantics. That's the 7HEAP slice's job.
    - **Generic-method-level generics inside generic-typed impls** (`impl Vec[T] { fn map[U](self, f: U) -> Vec[U] }`). Sema's `GenericImplMethodTemplate` carries the method-level `[U]`, and `resolve_generic_instantiation` preserves it on the populated MethodSig — but the method-call dispatcher in `check_method_call`/`check_generic_method_call` doesn't yet propagate method-instantiations through. No tested case today; will need wiring when the use case shows up.
    - **Bound checking E0502** (`impl SortedList[T: Ord] { ... }`) — same deferral as elsewhere; needs step 4 + blessed-interface table.
- **Phase 7 slice 7GEN.5e step 2 (generic methods on concrete-typed impls + turbofish on method/assoc calls) landed:** the headline two `E0312` rejections from 7GEN.5b are gone. Users can now write generic methods inside concrete-typed impls and call them with explicit turbofish or via inference. Generic-typed impls (`impl Vec[T] { ... }`) remain deferred to step 3. Coordinated changes across six files:
  - **AST**: `Method` gained `generic_params: Vec<GenericParam>`; `ImplBlock` gained `target_generic_params: Vec<GenericParam>` for `impl Foo[T] { ... }` (parsing only at this step; sema/codegen wiring lands in step 3). `MethodSig` gained `generic_params: Vec<String>`.
  - **Parser**: `parse_method` consumes optional `[T, U: Bound]` after the method name (shared `parse_generic_params` helper). `parse_impl_block` consumes optional `[T]` on inherent impl targets. `parse_postfix` turbofish gate widened from `Ident` only to `Ident | Path | Field` callees — so `v.method::[T](...)` and `Type::method::[T](...)` both parse to `Call { type_args, ... }`. `parse_primary` path-segment collection now stops at `::[` to let the turbofish handler downstream pick it up. Six new parser unit tests pin all shapes.
  - **Sema**: `collect_methods` pushes method's `generic_params` onto `type_params_stack` before resolving param/return types, so `Ty::Param("T")` becomes the resolved form (instead of E0303). `check_method` does the same for body checking. New `check_generic_method_call` mirrors the top-level `check_generic_named_call` shape: when sig has generic_params, route either through explicit-args validation (turbofish path — checks arity, builds subst from type_args) or inference (each `Ty::Param` slot unifies against the arg's concrete type via `unify_param_against_concrete`). Each unfilled param fires **E0500**; arity mismatches fire **E0501**; per-arg type mismatches fire **E0302** with the *substituted* expected type. Turbofish on a non-generic method/assoc-fn fires E0501 with a "takes no type arguments" message. `check_method_call` and `check_assoc_call` both accept `type_args: &[Type]`; the existing `check_assoc_call` callsite from `check_generic_enum_call` passes empty.
  - **MonoInfo / SemaCx**: new field `method_instantiations: BTreeSet<(struct_name, method_name, [Ty])>` (internal `(StructId, String, [Ty])` form on SemaCx, converted at export). Per-call instantiation also recorded in the existing `call_monos: HashMap<ByteSpan, [Ty]>` so monomorphize can key by span — same machinery the fn-call path uses.
  - **Monomorphize**: `rewrite_item_calls` Impl arm now synthesizes one concrete `Method` per `method_instantiations` entry matching `(target_name, method_name)`, dropping the generic template; the synthesized clone has `generic_params: []`, mangled name (`method__T1__T2`), and substituted param/return/body. `rewrite_expr` Call arm widened: in addition to the existing Ident-callee fn-name rewrite, it now handles Field callees (rewrite `name` to mangled) and Path callees (rewrite segment[1] to mangled) when `call_monos` reports type args for that span AND `method_instantiations` confirms the method is generic. The receiver of a method-call is recursively rewritten before the Field is constructed.
  - **Codegen**: generic methods are skipped pre-monomorphization (two sites: the method generation loop and the method-info collection pass). Post-monomorphize, every method has `generic_params: []` and feeds through the existing concrete-method codegen path unchanged.
  - **Tests added** (5 sema unit + 2 e2e + 6 parser unit = 13): sema unit pins `p.cast::[i32](42)` clean, inference clean (`p.cast(42)`), `P::ident::[i32](42)` clean, arity mismatch fires E0501, non-generic-method turbofish fires E0501. E2E exercises full pipeline: `phase7_generic_method_with_turbofish_runs` (returns 42) + `phase7_generic_assoc_call_with_turbofish_runs` (returns 42). Parser tests pin `impl Vec[T]`, `impl Pair[A, B]`, `impl Sorted[T: Ord]`, empty-bracket rejection, method-call turbofish (`v.cast::[i32](7)`), assoc-call turbofish (`Vec::new::[i32]()`). **Test total: 755** (604 library + 140 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Sanity bench still at clang -O2 parity (~0.94–0.97x build, ~1.00x runtime).
  - **What's deferred to step 3 (generic-typed impls)**: `impl Vec[T] { ... }` parses today but sema does not wire impl-level `target_generic_params` into method body scope. So `impl Vec[T] { fn push(self, item: T) }` would fire E0303 on the `T` in `item: T` because the method itself doesn't declare `T`. Implementing this is the load-bearing piece for the Phase-7 exit demo and is the next slice's focus. Also deferred: (1) bound checking on generic-method calls (E0502 — `T: Ord` requires `T` has `impl Ord`); (2) generic methods returning aggregates that themselves contain `T` (`fn collect[T]() -> Vec[T]` — needs step 3 too); (3) cross-module generic methods through `prefix::Type::method::[T](...)` — parser's 3-segment path collection currently flattens before turbofish detection; needs targeted fix.
- **Phase 7 slice 7GEN.5e step 1 (source-level generic-enum patterns) landed:** the headline fix for the mangled-name leak from 7GEN.5d. Users now write `Option[i32]::Some(v)` (or unqualified `Option::Some(v)`) in match arms — no `Option__i32` anywhere in source. The `Option__i32` form still parses incidentally (the EnumDef name happens to equal the mangled string) but is no longer documented or in tests. The internal mangling remains an implementation detail at the symbol-table layer, on par with LLVM's `%enum.0`. Coordinated changes across five files:
  - **AST** (`PatternKind::Variant`): added `type_args: Vec<Type>`. Empty for non-generic enums and for unqualified patterns relying on type-directed resolution; non-empty when the user wrote `Option[i32]::Some(v)`.
  - **Parser** (`parse_pattern`): after the first ident, optionally consume `[type_args]` before `::`. Patterns have no `[i]` indexing, so the `[` is unambiguous. Two new diagnostic paths: (a) `Option[i32]` with no `::Variant` follow-up errors with a recipe ("`expected ::Variant after generic-enum name in pattern`"); (b) `prefix::Enum[T]::Variant` cross-file generic patterns error out — would need resolver-level prefix rewriting with type args, deferred.
  - **Sema** (`check_pattern`): three acceptance shapes. (1) `Foo::Bar` against a concrete enum named `Foo` (existing behavior). (2) `Option[i32]::Some` against an `Option[i32]` scrutinee — resolves the type args via `resolve_generic_enum_instantiation`, then compares the resulting EnumId against the scrutinee's. (3) `Option::Some` (no type args) against an `Option[i32]` scrutinee — type-directed: accepted when `pat_enum.name` matches the scrutinee enum's `generic_base` source name. The fallback never fires when `type_args` is non-empty, so `Option[bool]::Some(_)` against an `Option[i32]` scrutinee correctly fires E0341.
  - **EnumDef**: new field `generic_base: Option<String>` set in `resolve_generic_enum_instantiation` to the source-level generic name (`"Option"`). Plain (non-generic) enums leave it `None`. Mechanically what powers shape (3) above.
  - **Resolver** (`rewrite_pattern`): now walks `type_args` through `rewrite_type`, so cross-file type arguments to a same-file generic enum (`Option[other_mod::Point]::Some(v)`) get prefix-qualified correctly. (The orthogonal cross-file *enum* case — `other_mod::Option[i32]::Some(v)` — is parser-rejected today; will be revisited if needed.)
  - **Tests added** (4 parser + 4 sema + 1 e2e + existing demo updated = 9 new + 1 modified): parser unit tests pin (a) explicit single type-arg, (b) explicit two type-args (`Result[i32, string]::Ok(v)`), (c) unqualified pattern leaves `type_args` empty, (d) `Option[i32]` without `::Variant` rejects. Sema unit tests pin (a) explicit `Option[i32]::Some(v)` clean, (b) unqualified `Option::Some(v)` clean (type-directed), (c) wrong-type-arg `Option[bool]::Some(_)` against `Option[i32]` scrutinee fires E0341, (d) payload binding has the concrete instantiation type (not `Ty::Param`). The existing `phase7_generic_enum_option_runs` e2e test was rewritten to use `Option[i32]::Some(v)` in arms instead of `Option__i32::Some(v)`; new `phase7_generic_enum_unqualified_pattern_runs` exercises the type-directed shape. **Test total: 742** (593 library + 138 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. Sanity bench still at clang -O2 parity (0.93–0.94x build, 1.00–1.01x runtime).
  - **What's deferred to 7GEN.5e steps 2-4**: (1) Turbofish on method / assoc calls (`v.method::[i32]()`, `Type::method::[i32]()`) — currently E0312-rejected. (2) Generic methods inside `impl` blocks (`impl Vec[T] { fn push(...) }`). (3) Bound checking E0502 — `max[T: Ord](a: T, b: T)` should verify `T` has an `impl Ord` at the instantiation site. (4) Cross-module generic-enum patterns (`other_mod::Option[i32]::Some(v)` in a match arm) — would need the resolver's prefix-rewriting to thread `type_args` through `qualify_external`. No load-bearing demos need it yet.
- **Phase 7 slice 7GEN.5d (generic-enum instantiation: `Option[T]::Some(7)`) landed:** generic enums now work end-to-end. A program with `enum Option[T] { Some(T), None }`, `let a: Option[i32] = Option[i32]::Some(35);`, and `match` over the instantiated form compiles and runs.
  - **AST**: new `ExprKind::GenericEnumCall { enum_name, type_args, variant, args }` — captures `Option[i32]::Some(7)` or `Option[i32]::None` (the no-parens case has `args: []`). Type-position `Option[T]` already worked via 7GEN.5c's `TypeKind::Generic`.
  - **Parser**: `parse_primary`'s ident-followed-by-`[...]` lookahead extended with a third case: when `]` is followed by `::`, it's a generic enum constructor. The earlier branch (`]` then `{`) handles generic struct literals; the new branch consumes the type args, the `::`, the variant name, and an optional `( ... )` arg list.
  - **Sema**: new `enum_generic_templates: HashMap<String, EnumDecl>` + `enum_instantiations: BTreeMap<(name, [Ty]), EnumId>` tables. `collect_type_names` routes generic enums into the template table (skipping the regular `enum_by_name`). `collect_enum_payloads` and `compute_enum_copy_flags` skip generic templates. New `resolve_generic_enum_instantiation` mirrors the struct path: synthesizes a concrete `EnumDef` per unique `(name, args)` with substituted payload types. `resolve_type` now tries the enum table first when the name matches. New `check_generic_enum_call` resolves the enum, then either short-circuits (payload-less + no parens → bare-variant value) or delegates to `check_assoc_call` with the mangled name + variant.
  - **MonoInfo**: gained `enum_instantiations: BTreeMap<(name, [Ty]), EnumInstantiationInfo>` (parallel to `struct_instantiations`). Carries the mangled name + concrete variant payloads.
  - **Monomorphize**: emits synthesized `ItemKind::Enum` items per instantiation. `subst_type_ast`'s `struct_lookup` now also carries enum mangled names (merged at the top of `monomorphize`). `rewrite_expr` adds a `GenericEnumCall` arm: when args is empty, rewrites to a bare `Path { [mangled_enum, variant] }`; otherwise to `Call { callee: Path { ... }, args }`. The two-shape split mirrors the source-level distinction between `Maybe::None` and `Maybe::Some(7)`.
  - **Threaded across passes**: `ExprKind::GenericEnumCall { args: elements, .. }` unions with the existing `ArrayLit { elements }` pattern in borrowck (6 sites), codegen (2 sites), lower (1 site), resolver (1 site) — both recurse over a `Vec<Expr>` of arg expressions, so the existing iter-and-recurse logic applies unchanged.
  - **Match arm ergonomic caveat (recorded for follow-up)**: today the user writes the mangled name in the pattern position: `match o { Option__i32::Some(v) => ..., Option__i32::None => ... }`. The source-level `Option[i32]::Some(v)` pattern syntax isn't yet parsed — it requires extending `parse_pattern` with the same `Ident[args]::Variant(...)` lookahead. Lands as part of a follow-up since the type-driven inference for match patterns is a bigger conversation (Rust resolves `Some(v)` against the scrutinee's type — C+ today requires the path-qualified form even for non-generic enums).
  - **Tests added** (4 sema unit + 2 e2e = 6): `generic_enum_used_at_type_position_clean`, `generic_enum_constructor_clean`, `generic_enum_wrong_arity_e0501`, `generic_enum_unknown_template_e0303`. E2E: `phase7_generic_enum_option_runs` (the headline — `unwrap_or(Some(35), 0) + unwrap_or(None, 7) = 42` end-to-end), `phase7_generic_enum_emits_distinct_types` (two instantiations produce two distinct LLVM enum types). **Test total: 733** (585 library + 137 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 29 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **What's deferred to 7GEN.5e / 7GEN.6**: (1) **Source-level generic-enum patterns** in `match` arms (`Option[i32]::Some(v) =>`) — needs `parse_pattern` extension; users today type the mangled name. The bigger underlying question is whether C+ should add type-directed pattern resolution (Rust-style `Some(v) =>` against a known-typed scrutinee) — a separate slice. (2) Generic methods (`Pair[i32]::new(...)`, `impl Vec[T] { fn push(...) }`). (3) Bound checking E0502. (4) Turbofish on method/assoc calls. (5) Aggregate-typed generic args (`Pair[Option[i32], bool]`) — same `type_ast_to_ty` limitation as the struct side.
- **Phase 7 slice 7GEN.5c (generic-struct instantiation: type position + struct literal) landed:** users can now use generic structs at use sites. A program like `struct Pair[A, B] { first: A, second: B } fn main() -> i32 { let p: Pair[i32, i32] = Pair[i32, i32] { first: 7, second: 35 }; return p.first + p.second; }` compiles and runs, returning 42. Distinct instantiations (e.g. `Pair[i32, i32]` and `Pair[bool, i32]`) emit distinct mangled LLVM struct types (`%Pair__i32__i32`, `%Pair__bool__i32`).
  - **AST**: two new variants.
    - `TypeKind::Generic { name: String, args: Vec<Type> }` — generic type instantiation in type position (param types, return types, let-annotations, struct fields).
    - `ExprKind::GenericStructLit { name: Ident, type_args: Vec<Type>, fields: Vec<StructLitField> }` — generic struct literal in expression position (`Pair[i32, i32] { ... }`).
  - **Parser**: two paths.
    - `parse_type` admits `Ident[type_args]` after the ident's `::`-qualification loop. Disambiguation from arrays is structural — arrays start with `[`, not with an ident.
    - `parse_primary` admits `Ident[type_args] { ... }` as a generic struct literal. New helper `scan_past_bracket` peeks past the matching `]` to look for the disambiguating `{`. If `{` follows, the brackets carry type-args; if anything else follows, the brackets are indexing. The lookahead is bounded by the token vec (pre-lexed), so cost is constant.
  - **Sema**:
    - New `struct_generic_templates: HashMap<String, StructDecl>` on `SemaCx`. Generic struct decls in `collect_type_names` go here instead of the regular `struct_by_name` table — they're not concrete types until instantiated.
    - New `struct_instantiations: BTreeMap<(name, [Ty]), StructId>` dedupes per-instantiation synthesized structs.
    - New `resolve_generic_instantiation(name, args, span)` is called from `resolve_type` when it encounters `TypeKind::Generic`. It resolves each arg, builds the mangled name, looks up the cache; on miss it clones the template, substitutes Param types in field types via `resolve_field_type_with_subst`, registers a new `StructDef` with the mangled name, and returns the new `Ty::Struct(id)`. Fires **E0303** when the generic name is unknown, **E0501** when the arity is wrong.
    - New `check_generic_struct_lit` for the expression-side path: resolves the generic instantiation, then delegates to the regular `check_struct_lit` with the mangled name. This means all the field-validation rules (E0319 duplicate / E0320 unknown / E0321 missing / E0322 extra) are reused unchanged.
    - `MonoInfo` gained `struct_instantiations: BTreeMap<(name, [Ty]), StructInstantiationInfo>` so monomorphize can emit synthesized AST struct items and rewrite Generic→Path references.
  - **Monomorphize**:
    - For each entry in `mono.struct_instantiations`, synthesize an `ItemKind::Struct(StructDecl { name: mangled, fields: rendered_concrete_types, generic_params: [], ... })` and append to the output Program. Field types are rendered from sema's resolved `Ty` values via new `ty_to_type_ast`.
    - The original generic-struct templates are dropped (mirrors how generic fns are dropped post-mono).
    - `subst_type_ast` extended with a `TypeKind::Generic` arm: substitute fn-generic params in each arg, then look up the result in `struct_lookup` to rewrite to `TypeKind::Path(mangled)`. The `struct_lookup` is threaded through every walker.
    - `rewrite_item_calls` extended: also rewrite types in fn signatures (params + return) and in non-generic struct field types. Without this, a non-generic fn `use_pair(p: Pair[i32, i32])` would survive to codegen with `TypeKind::Generic` in its signature.
    - New `ExprKind::GenericStructLit` arm in `rewrite_expr` rewrites the literal to a regular `StructLit` with the mangled name. Codegen never sees `GenericStructLit`.
    - New helper `type_ast_to_ty` does the reverse direction (AST `Type` → `Ty`) needed to key into `struct_lookup` with the same `Ty` shape sema used. Currently handles primitives + arrays + borrows; aggregate-typed args (`Pair[Pair[i32, bool]]`) hit a limitation — the inner aggregate's `Ty` requires the StructId table which monomorphize doesn't carry. Recorded as a future-slice item; no in-tree test exercises it yet.
  - **Codegen**: untouched except for one panic arm in `ty_from` for `TypeKind::Generic` (should be unreachable post-mono). The synthesized struct items flow through the normal Phase-2 `collect_types` path; LLVM emits `%Pair__i32__i32 = type { i32, i32 }` and field accesses work via the standard GEP path.
  - **Tests added** (5 sema unit + 2 e2e = 7): `generic_struct_used_at_type_position_clean`, `generic_struct_literal_clean`, `generic_struct_distinct_instantiations_share_template`, `generic_struct_wrong_arity_e0501`, `generic_struct_unknown_template_e0303`. E2E: `phase7_generic_struct_instantiation_runs` (the headline 42-return demo through `cpc build`), `phase7_generic_struct_emits_distinct_mangled_types` (verifies both `%Pair__i32__i32` and `%Pair__bool__i32` appear in the IR). **Test total: 727** (581 library + 135 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 29 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **What's deferred to 7GEN.5d / 7GEN.6**: (1) **Generic enum instantiation** — `Option[i32]::Some(7)` and `Result[i32, string]`. Same shape as generic structs but the AST surface is `Path { segments }`-driven, so the parser + sema need analogous extensions. (2) **Generic methods on instantiated structs** — `Pair[i32, i32]::new(7, 35)`. Needs `Type::method` calls to admit `::[T]` on the receiver. (3) **Aggregate-typed generic args** — `Pair[Pair[i32, bool], i32]`. The lookup map's key shape (`(String, Vec<Ty>)`) supports it; the codegen-side `type_ast_to_ty` helper needs a way to look up StructIds by name to construct the right `Ty::Struct(id)`. Land when motivated. (4) **Bound checking on generic-struct instantiations** — `SortedList[Point]` should verify `Point: Ord`. Same E0502 family that's deferred for generic-fn calls. (5) **Generic-struct field access through Param** — inside a generic-fn body, `p.first` where `p: Pair[T, U]` and Pair is generic doesn't yet flow because the fn body sees `Ty::Param("T")`-typed values, not the instantiated struct. This unlocks once generic-fns can accept generic-typed parameters.
- **Phase 7 slice 7GEN.5b (`::[T]` turbofish for generic-fn calls) landed:** users can now pin type arguments explicitly when inference can't (or shouldn't), and the compiler validates explicit type-args carefully:
  - **AST**: `ExprKind::Call` gained `type_args: Vec<Type>` — empty for non-generic calls / inferred generic calls; non-empty when the user wrote `name::[T1, T2](...)`. Threaded through 12 destructure sites across borrowck (5 sites), codegen (2 sites), lower (1 site), monomorphize (1 site), resolver (1 site), sema (1 dispatch site).
  - **Parser**: `parse_postfix` detects `::[` immediately after a plain-ident expression and routes to a new branch that consumes `::`, `[`, type-args, `]`, then the regular `( args )`. A new `peek_kind_n(usize)` helper gives one-token lookahead so `parse_primary` knows to leave `::[` alone (its existing path-greedy `::` consumer would otherwise call `expect_ident()` and reject `[`). The turbofish is admitted only when the callee is a plain `Ident` — turbofish on method calls (`v.method::[i32]()`) and associated-function calls (`Type::method::[i32]()`) is rejected with E0312 in this slice and revisited when 7GEN.5c lands generic methods.
  - **Sema**: `check_call` now takes a `type_args: &[Type]` slice and routes to the right path. `check_named_call` dispatches to `check_generic_named_call` for generic fns and rejects turbofish on non-generic fns with **E0501** ("function `name` takes no type arguments but N were provided"). `check_generic_named_call` checks an explicit-args path before inference: arity mismatch fires E0501 with the expected/actual counts. When arity matches, each type-arg is resolved (so `Pair[i32]` and other future generic-type references will flow through `resolve_type` once 7GEN.5c lands), the substitution map is built directly, and each call argument is type-checked against the *substituted* parameter type — so a bool passed to `identity::[i32](true)` fires **E0302** with "expected `i32`, got `bool`" pointing at the offending arg. Recording into `fn_instantiations` and `call_monos` uses the explicit args; monomorphize emits the same mangled name path (`identity__i32`) whether the args came from inference or the user.
  - **Diagnostic polish for E0500**: the inference-failure message now suggests `::[T]` as the fix recipe — closing the loop with the new turbofish surface. Old text said "7GEN.5a requires each generic param to appear as the type of at least one argument"; new text says "supply `::[T]` turbofish or use `T` in an argument position."
  - **Tests added** (4 sema unit + 2 e2e = 6): `turbofish_at_call_site_compiles_clean` (the positive shape), `turbofish_wrong_arity_e0501` (E0501 on count mismatch), `turbofish_on_non_generic_fn_e0501` (non-generic fn rejects turbofish), `turbofish_arg_type_validated_against_substituted_param` (E0302 when the arg type doesn't match the substituted param type — a mismatch the inference path would also have caught, but explicit path uses substituted-against-actual rather than inference-driven). E2E: `phase7_turbofish_explicit_type_args_runs` (`identity::[i32](7) + identity::[i32](35)` returns 42 end-to-end), `phase7_turbofish_arity_mismatch_rejected_e0501`. **Test total: 720** (576 library + 133 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 29 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **What's deferred to 7GEN.5c**: (1) **Generic-type instantiation** (`Pair[i32, bool]::new(...)`, `Option[i32]::Some(7)`) — the load-bearing piece of 7GEN.5c. Needs `TypeKind::Generic { name, args }` in the AST and a parser branch, plus sema's `resolve_type` extension to look up the generic-type template and register a per-instantiation StructDef/EnumDef, plus codegen's per-instantiation struct/enum lowering. (2) **Turbofish on method / assoc-fn calls** — `v.foo::[i32]()` and `Type::method::[i32]()`. Rejected today with E0312; lands alongside generic methods inside `impl` blocks. (3) **Bound checking (E0502)** — when the user writes `max::[Point](a, b)` with `T: Ord`, sema should verify `Point` has an `impl Ord for Point`. (4) **Return-type-only inference** — `fn default[T]() -> T` still fires E0500 because no parameter slot pins T; the diagnostic now points at the turbofish recipe as the fix.
- **Phase 7 slice 7GEN.5a (minimal generic-fn inference + monomorphization) landed:** the first end-to-end generic call path. A program like `fn identity[T](x: T) -> T { return x; } fn main() -> i32 { return identity(7) + identity(35); }` now compiles and runs, returning 42. Two coordinated changes:
  - **Sema inference + instantiation collection**: new `GenericFnSig` table on `SemaCx` (separate from `fns` — a fn is in exactly one of the two tables based on whether `generic_params` is empty). `collect_functions` routes generic fns into `fns_generic`. `check_named_call` dispatches generic-fn calls through a new `check_generic_named_call` that unifies each parameter's `Ty::Param("T")` against the corresponding arg's concrete type (via `unify_param_against_concrete`), substitutes the return type (`subst_ty`), and records two pieces of monomorphization info on the context: `fn_instantiations: BTreeSet<(name, [Ty])>` (unique instantiations) + `call_monos: HashMap<ByteSpan, [Ty]>` (per call-site type args, keyed by the Call expression's span). Reserves error code **E0500** for "cannot infer type parameter `T`" (fires when a declared generic param never appears as the top-level type of any parameter — the inference strategy can't pin it). Type-mismatch under inference re-uses **E0302** ("parameter is `T` but argument has type `bool`"). New sema entry point `check_multi_with_mono` returns `(Vec<Diagnostic>, MonoInfo)` so the driver can hand the `MonoInfo` to the monomorphize pass. The single-argument `check` / `check_multi` entries stay as thin wrappers that discard the `MonoInfo`.
  - **New `cplus-core/src/monomorphize.rs` pass** consuming the `MonoInfo` after sema + borrowck pass. For each unique `(generic_fn, [concrete_args])` pair: clones the generic-fn template, builds a `name -> concrete_ty` substitution map, walks the template's parameter types / return type / body via a deep AST-rewriter (`subst_type_ast` for `Type` nodes; `rewrite_expr` / `rewrite_stmt` / `rewrite_block` for the body), produces a fresh `Function` AST with `generic_params: Vec::new()` and a mangled name. Mangling format: `name__T1__T2`, where each `Ti` renders via `mangle_ty` — primitives use their literal name (`i32`, `bool`), aggregates use their source name (sema's struct/enum table), arrays render as `arrN_<elem>` so the structure survives without bracket characters LLVM identifiers reject. Generic-fn call sites are then rewritten via a separate walker that consults `mono.call_monos` by span — when the callee is a plain `Ident` matching a known generic name, the callee's name is replaced by the mangled form. Generic-fn templates themselves are *removed* from the output Program (codegen would have skipped them anyway; removing keeps the post-mono program uniform — every fn is concrete).
  - **Helper traits**: needed to derive `Ord`/`PartialOrd`/`Hash` on `Ty` (and transitively on `StructId`/`EnumId`/`Span`) so `Ty` can be a `BTreeSet` element and a `HashMap` key.
  - **Pipeline wiring**: `cpc/src/main.rs` calls `sema::check_multi_with_mono` at both project-mode and single-file entry points (the project-mode `compile`, `build_ir`, and `build_program` paths). After borrowck completes, a new `run_monomorphize` helper rebuilds the struct/enum name tables (mirroring sema's `collect_type_names` order) and invokes `monomorphize::monomorphize` with a closure that renders any `Ty` to its source name. The post-mono program is what codegen sees. `cpc-lsp` deliberately stays on `check_multi` — the LSP only needs diagnostics, not the post-mono program; monomorphization isn't useful for the diagnostic surface.
  - **Scope kept narrow**: (1) Generic *functions* only — generic types (`struct Pair[A, B]`, `enum Option[T]`) parse and sema-check but aren't yet instantiable at use sites (no constructor sugar that names them with type args). (2) Inference rule: each generic param must appear as the top-level type of at least one parameter; nested-only / return-only params fire E0500. (3) No bound checking yet (E0502 deferred — needs the bound-resolution pass that pulls interface-method tables into scope). (4) No turbofish `::[T]` syntax — every call must be type-inferable from arg shapes. (5) Generic methods inside `impl` blocks are deferred. (6) Generic-fn body type-checking still happens at sema time with `Ty::Param`-typed params — operations on Param values that don't have a structural interpretation (e.g. `x + 1` where x: T) hit ordinary sema rejection. Today only the identity-shape pattern (`return x;`, `let y = x;`) works without bounds; richer bodies need 7GEN.5b's bound-driven method resolution.
  - **Tests added** (4 monomorphize unit + 2 e2e = 6): `identity_call_synthesizes_concrete_fn_and_rewrites_callee`, `distinct_instantiations_emit_distinct_fns` (calling `id` with i32 and bool produces both `id__i32` and `id__bool`), `mangle_separates_args_with_double_underscore` (mangling shape pin), `non_generic_program_passes_through_unchanged` (non-generic regression). E2E drives the full pipeline: `phase7_generic_fn_inferred_call_runs` (the headline 42-return demo), `phase7_generic_fn_distinct_instantiations_emit_distinct_symbols` (verifies both `@id__i32` and `@id__i64` appear in the IR for a program that calls `id` with both type args). **Test total: 714** (572 library + 131 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 29 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **What's deferred to 7GEN.5b / 7GEN.5c**: (1) **Generic-type instantiation**. `Pair[i32, bool]::new(...)` and `Option[i32]::Some(7)` need parser changes for the `::[T]` turbofish + sema changes to substitute through struct/enum templates + codegen changes to register one instantiation per `Ty::Struct` / `Ty::Enum` instance. (2) **Bound checking + interface-method dispatch**. `fn max[T: Ord](a: T, b: T) -> T { if a.compare(b) > 0 { return a; } return b; }` needs the call `a.compare(b)` to look up `Ord`'s method table for `T`. Without bound-driven method resolution, generic-fn bodies are limited to operations that don't depend on T's concrete operations. (3) **Generic methods inside `impl` blocks** — `impl Vec[T] { fn push[U](&mut self, val: U) }` requires extending the monomorphize work-queue to walk method templates too. (4) **Return-type-driven inference** for cases like `fn default[T]() -> T`. Today returns-only params fire E0500. (5) **Recursive generic calls** — calling a generic fn from inside a generic fn. The current implementation collects instantiations from sema, but if `id[T]` calls itself (or another generic), the call site there sees `Ty::Param("T")` not a concrete type, so inference fails. Resolving needs a worklist that processes instantiations and discovers new ones.
- **Phase 7 slice 7GEN.4 (sema type-param scoping + interface impl validation) landed:** the sema half of Phase 7 — generic items now sema-clean instead of firing E0303, `Self` resolves correctly inside `impl`/`interface` contexts, and `impl Interface for Type` blocks are validated structurally. Six coordinated changes:
  - **New `Ty::Param(String)` variant** in [cplus-core/src/sema.rs](cplus-core/src/sema.rs). Represents an in-scope generic type parameter. `is_atomic_copy()` returns false (conservative — bound-aware Copy resolution lands when the `Copy` interface itself does); `name()` returns `"type-param"`. Threaded through 2 codegen pattern matches (`is_copy_ty`, `llvm_ty`) — both `panic!()` if Param reaches codegen (pre-7GEN.5, generic items are codegen-skipped before they can produce a Param-typed value).
  - **Type-param scope stack** on `SemaCx`: `type_params_stack: Vec<HashSet<String>>` pushed/popped via `push_type_params` / `pop_type_params` at every site that enters a generic item — `collect_struct_fields`, `collect_enum_payloads`, `collect_functions`, `check_function`. Receivers' `Self` magic uses a parallel `self_type_stack: Vec<Ty>` pushed in `collect_methods` and `check_method` so method body resolution sees the concrete target. `resolve_type` consults both before erroring E0303: Self → self_type_stack.last(); name-matches-param → `Ty::Param(name)`; else fall through to enum/struct registry.
  - **Interface registry**: new `InterfaceDef { name, methods: HashMap<String, MethodSig>, origin_file }` struct + `interfaces: HashMap<String, InterfaceDef>` on `SemaCx`. New `collect_interfaces` pass runs right after type-name collection. Each interface method is resolved with a synthetic `Self` type-param frame pushed so any `Self` in the signature becomes `Ty::Param("Self")`, ready for substitution at impl-validation time. Duplicate interface names fire E0301; duplicate methods within an interface fire E0326.
  - **`impl Interface for Type` validation**: new `validate_interface_impls` pass collects all five reserved diagnostics. **E0503** (missing method) walks every declared interface method, looks it up in the target's method table; missing → diagnostic. **E0504** (extra method) walks the impl block's methods directly, rejects any not declared by the interface. **E0505** (signature mismatch) compares interface vs impl signatures after `subst_self(&Ty, target)` substitutes every `Ty::Param("Self")` to the implementing type; receiver kind, parameter count, `mut` / `move` markers, parameter types, and return type must all match. **E0506** (duplicate impl) tracks a `HashSet<(String, String)>` of `(interface_name, target_name)` pairs. **E0507** (orphan rule) — impl's `origin_file` must equal either the interface's or the target's `origin_file`. Unknown interface name → E0303; unknown target type → E0325.
  - **`Self` outside impl/interface**: new **E0508** ("`Self` is only valid inside an `interface` or `impl` body"). Fires on type-position `Self` when both `self_type_stack` is empty and `Self` is not in `type_params_stack` (the interface-collection frame is the only place where `Self` is a generic param).
  - **Parser polish**: `parse_type` admits `TokenKind::SelfUpper` and emits `Type::Path("Self")` so sema sees a uniform path-shaped type. Without this, `fn loose(x: Self)` failed at parse with "expected type, found token" — the token was lexed but never consumed by `parse_type`.
  - **Codegen generic-item skipping**: pre-monomorphization (7GEN.5 work), codegen skips items with non-empty `generic_params` — `generate_inner`'s function loop, `collect_sigs`, and `collect_types`' three passes (name registration, field resolution, enum-payload resolution) all early-continue. Non-generic items + interface impls on concrete types emit normally. Without this, `Pair[A, B]`'s field types resolve to `Ty::Error` (the codegen-side type-resolver has no notion of param scope) and `llvm_ty` panics.
  - **Tests added** (18 lib + 3 e2e = 21): lib covers `Ty::Param` recognition (generic fn / multi-param fn / generic struct / generic enum / unknown-type-still-errors / no-leakage-outside-generic-fn), Self handling (outside-impl rejected E0508 / inside-inherent-impl resolves / inside-interface-impl substitutes), interface validation (declaration-clean / matching-impl-clean / E0503 missing / E0504 extra / E0505 sig-mismatch / E0505 wrong-Self-return / E0506 duplicate / E0301 duplicate-name / E0303 unknown-interface). E2E drives `cpc build` end-to-end: `phase7_generic_decls_and_impl_interface_clean` (the smoke file with `interface Ord` + `struct Pair[A, B]` + `enum Maybe[T]` + `impl Ord for Point` + `fn identity[T]` builds and `main` returns 7), `phase7_impl_interface_missing_method_rejected_e0503`, `phase7_self_outside_impl_rejected_e0508`. **Test total: 708** (568 library + 129 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 29 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **What's deferred to 7GEN.5 / 7GEN.6**: **call-site bound checking** (E0500 unknown generic param at instantiation, E0501 wrong arg count, E0502 type does not satisfy bound, E0509 inference fails) — needs the `::[T]` turbofish parser at call sites and per-call substitution maps. **Monomorphization**: walking a work-queue of `(generic_item, [concrete_types])` pairs, emitting one mangled LLVM function/type per unique instantiation. **Blessed interface declarations** for `Copy` / `Drop` / `Eq` / `Ord` / `Hash` / `Clone` — where they live (synthetic module vs. stdlib prelude vs. compiler builtin), how `Copy` is structurally derived but rejects manual impls (E0510). **Variance** of type params (the design note's invariance default with future opt-in). **Receiver coercion** for `impl Interface for T` calls — today `t.method()` dispatches to the target's method table; if `method` happens to come from an interface impl the dispatch is identical, but interface-method-via-bound-on-generic-param (`fn f[T: Ord](a: T) { a.compare(...) }`) would need the bound to project into a method-lookup table, which is 7GEN.5 work.
- **Phase 7 slices 7GEN.1 + 7GEN.2 + 7GEN.3 (parse-only surface for generics + interfaces) landed:** the three parse-layer slices ship together — sema and codegen stay generics-blind until 7GEN.4 / 7GEN.5 lands. Three coordinated changes:
  - **7GEN.1 — generic-fn parsing**: new `parse_generic_params()` consumes optional `[T, U: Bound1 + Bound2]` after `fn name`. `Function` AST gains `generic_params: Vec<GenericParam>`; new `GenericParam { name: Ident, bounds: Vec<Ident>, span }` carries name + bounds. Empty `[]` is a parse error (would be syntactically ambiguous noise). Trailing commas admitted. 9 new parser unit tests pin non-generic, single-param, multi-param, single-bound, multi-bound, mixed-bounds-per-param, pub+attribute combos, empty-bracket rejection, trailing-comma admission.
  - **7GEN.2 — generic struct/enum parsing**: same `parse_generic_params()` wired into `parse_struct_decl` and `parse_enum_decl`. `StructDecl` and `EnumDecl` AST gain matching `generic_params` field. 8 new parser unit tests: `Holder[T]`, `Pair[A, B]`, `SortedList[T: Ord]`, non-generic structs stay empty, `Option[T]`, `Result[T, E]`, non-generic enums stay empty, `pub struct Vec[T]` combo.
  - **7GEN.3 — interface declarations + `impl Interface for Type`**: new reserved keyword `interface`. New `TokenKind::Interface`. New AST `ItemKind::Interface(InterfaceDecl)` variant carrying name + methods + pub + attributes. New `InterfaceMethod` for the body's signature-only declarations (method bodies end with `;`, not `{ ... }` — `E0xxx` at parse if user writes a body). New parser `parse_interface_decl` + `parse_interface_method`. `ImplBlock` AST gains `interface_name: Option<Ident>` so `impl Ord for Point { ... }` and plain `impl Point { ... }` share one shape; parser detects the interface form by peeking for `for` after the first ident. 9 new parser unit tests: single-method interface, multi-method, no-return-type method, body-rejected with helpful error, pub combo, `impl Interface for Target` happy path, plain inherent impl still works without `interface_name`, `mut self` receiver in interface, associated-function-no-receiver shape (`fn default() -> Self;`).
  - **Threaded through 11 exhaustive-match sites**: borrowck (2 spots), codegen (2 spots), resolver (rewrite_item + qualified-name collection + ItemKindTag enum + PrivateKind enum), sema (one spot), attrs (interface gets struct-like attribute validation for Phase-7 first cut), lower (interface bodies have no expressions to lower — no-op), cpc-lsp's goto-definition (interface names are jumpable items). New `ItemKindTag::Interface` and `PrivateKind::Interface` round out the resolver's discriminator enums; their `Display` impls render as "interface" for diagnostics.
  - **Scope deliberately parse-only**: a program using generic functions or types fails sema with `E0303 unknown type T` because sema's type-resolution hasn't been taught about type parameters yet — that's 7GEN.4's job. Interface declarations parse but don't enforce coherence, signature-match, etc. — also 7GEN.4. This is correct sliced rollout: the parse layer lands first, sema follows, codegen follows. **Test total: 687** (550 library + 126 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 29 sample programs (including [docs/examples/veci32_invalidation.cplus](docs/examples/veci32_invalidation.cplus) Phase-6 exit demo) all compile and run clean. Sanity bench at clang -O2 parity preserved.
- **Phase 7 generics design note landed:** [docs/design/phase7-generics.md](docs/design/phase7-generics.md), 446 lines. Locks in: **square-bracket parameter lists** (`fn max[T: Ord](a: T, b: T) -> T`) chosen over angle-brackets to sidestep the C++ `vector<vector<int>>` parse ambiguity and Rust's `::<>` turbofish workaround. **`interface` keyword** (not `trait`) for the declaration form — interfaces are pure operation-sets, no inheritance connotations; `interface` matches Java/Go/TypeScript usage and reads naturally. **`Self` magic type** inside interface/impl bodies; admitted as a synonym for the impl target in inherent `impl Type { ... }` blocks too (matches Rust). **`+` for multiple bounds** (`T: Ord + Eq`). **`::[T]` turbofish** at call sites when inference fails (`identity::[i32](0)`). **Monomorphization-only** at codegen — no `dyn Interface`, no vtables; Phase 7 ships static generics, dynamic dispatch is a separate later decision. **Coherence: strict orphan rule** — `impl Interface for Type` admitted only in the file defining either side. **Compiler-blessed interface decls** for Copy/Drop/Eq/Ord/Hash/Clone; users implement most, but Copy is structural-only (no manual `impl Copy for X` — E0510) and Drop folds into the existing magic-method machinery. **Name mangling**: `Pair[i32, Vec[u8]]::new` → `@Pair__i32__Vec__u8.new`, recursive `__`-flattening. **Reserved error codes E0500–E0511** with a small gap before Phase 6's E0386 for polish slices. Deferred to Phase 7+: where-clauses (`where T: Ord, U: Clone`), generic methods inside impl blocks (`impl Vec[T] { fn map[U](...) }`), associated types (Rust's `Iterator::Item`), const generics (`Vec[T; N]`), HKT, specialization, auto-derive for Eq/Ord/Hash (Phase 7 first cut requires explicit impls — matches §2.8c verbosity-exposes-rules). **Heap allocation is parallel slice 7HEAP** with its own design note; generics-without-heap are usable for inline types like `Pair[A, B]` independently. 14 open questions recorded — biggest are 7HEAP sequencing (lands before or after 7GEN.5), the Allocator interface design, where the blessed interface declarations physically live (synthetic compiler-internal module vs. stdlib prelude vs. compiler-builtin names), and auto-derive for Eq/Ord/Hash (rule first cut: don't, can relax later).
- **Phase 6 ✅ done.** All sub-slices landed (in order): 6BC.1 (intra-call exclusive-borrow conflicts E0380/E0381/E0382) → 6BC.2 (cross-statement exclusive-borrow tracking + E0383 + Rule E1-mut / E2-mut elision) → 6BC.3 (partial-place activation via `Place::projections` + E0374) → 6BC.4 (Rule E3-mut multi-`mut`-param body-flow analysis + E0384 emission) → 6BC.5 (explicit `borrow REGION T` annotation syntax with new `borrow` keyword) → 6BC.codegen (`ptr noalias` on `mut x: T`, `ptr readonly` on `x: T`) → 6BC.opt (static drop-flag specialization + method-call receiver-claim cross-statement check). Test total at Phase-6 close: **661** (524 library + 126 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 29 sample programs (28 originals + the new `veci32_invalidation.cplus` Phase-6 exit demo) all compile and run clean. Sanity bench still at clang -O2 parity on all four axes.
  - **Phase-6 exit criterion met.** The plan.md exit reads: "A small in-tree test program implementing a `Vec[T]`-style growable array compiles cleanly and rejects iterator invalidation." Delivered via [docs/examples/veci32_invalidation.cplus](docs/examples/veci32_invalidation.cplus) — a fixed-capacity `VecI32` with `cursor(self) -> VecI32` (Rule E2 shared self-borrow) and `push(mut self, i32)` (mut self / exclusive). Calling `push` while a cursor is alive fires **E0381** as required ("cannot call `v.push(...)` while `v` is shared-borrowed by `cur`"). Pinned by two new e2e tests: `phase6_exit_iterator_invalidation_rejected` (negative — must reject) and `phase6_exit_sequential_pushes_accepted` (positive — sequential `v.push(...)` calls compile fine without an outstanding cursor).
  - **What's deferred to Phase 7+** (not blocking Phase-6 exit): generic-parameter syntax `[T]` (Phase 7 — `Vec[T]` becomes literal). Heap allocation primitives. `Atomic[T]` (sibling design note still pending). E0385 (mismatched annotations) — verifying that an annotated function's body actually borrows from the declared region. E0386 (struct field requires annotation) — sema-level enforcement that non-Copy borrow-field types must carry a `borrow REGION T` annotation. `'static`-equivalent region for program-lifetime values (string literals motivate it, lands when string-literal types land). Receiver-kind plumbing into SigTable so `check_method_receiver_claim` can distinguish `mut self` from `self` calls (current 6BC.opt rule is conservative — treats all method calls on borrowed receivers as potentially-conflicting, which is sound but slightly over-strict for `self`-only methods on a shared borrower).
- **Phase 6 slice 6BC.opt (static drop-flag specialization + method-call receiver-claim) landed:** the optimizer-friendly half of Phase 6. Two changes:
  - **Static drop-flag specialization** ([cplus-core/src/codegen.rs](cplus-core/src/codegen.rs)): a pre-pass per function walks the body collecting binding names used at `move`-position arg or `move self` receiver. Bindings NOT in the moved set get **`DropDisposition::Always`** — `register_drop` skips the `i1` drop-flag alloca, the initial `store i1 true`, and `emit_conditional_drop` emits a direct unconditional `call void @T.drop(ptr ...)`. Bindings in the moved set keep the Phase-5 runtime mechanism (alloca + flag-load + conditional). Most Drop bindings in practice are let-and-drop (never moved); they all light up the optimized lowering. The drop_basic sample's IR shrinks from 5+ basic blocks of conditional-drop machinery to a single unconditional call per binding; runtime output unchanged (still prints `1\n2\n-2\n-1\n`).
  - **Method-call receiver-claim cross-statement check** ([cplus-core/src/borrowck.rs](cplus-core/src/borrowck.rs)): new `check_method_receiver_claim` in `apply_call`. When the callee is a `Field { receiver, method }` expression on an Ident-rooted receiver and the receiver's place has any live borrow, the call site rejects: shared borrow → **E0381**, exclusive → **E0383**. This closes the gap that let iterator-invalidation patterns through pre-6BC.opt: a method call's receiver-as-arg wasn't routed through the intra-call mut-position scan, so `vec.push(...)` after `let cur = vec.cursor()` compiled silently. The check fires before `apply_expr(callee)` so the diagnostic primary span lands on the receiver. Conservative: when receiver isn't a plain Ident (chained method calls on temporaries), or the method isn't resolvable, skips — sound (false-positive-free).
  - **Tests added** (3 e2e for drop-flag elision + 2 e2e for Phase-6 exit criterion): `never_moved_drop_binding_elides_flag` (asserts `%x.drop_flag` doesn't appear in IR + direct `call void @B.drop` does), `moved_drop_binding_keeps_runtime_flag` (regression — alloca + flag-load present), `never_moved_drop_runtime_behavior_unchanged` (drop_basic still prints `1\n2\n-2\n-1\n`), `phase6_exit_iterator_invalidation_rejected`, `phase6_exit_sequential_pushes_accepted`.
  - **New sample**: [docs/examples/veci32_invalidation.cplus](docs/examples/veci32_invalidation.cplus) — Phase-6 exit demo with documented `// v.push(42);` line that triggers the rejection when uncommented.
  - **What's deferred (recorded for completeness)**: definitely-moved-on-every-path → elide drop entirely (Phase-6 §5.4 "Definitely-moved" case). This requires flow-sensitive analysis matching borrowck's state at scope-exit; the always-not-moved case in 6BC.opt is the conservative, syntactically-detectable subset and the bigger common-code win. The full flow-sensitive specialization is a polish slice when a real workload measures the cost; the runtime flag mechanism is still correct for the deferred case.
- **Phase 6 slice 6BC.codegen (`noalias` + `readonly` parameter attributes) landed:** the performance unlock that the borrow checker has been making safe. Two LLVM parameter attributes flow through to non-Copy borrow parameters:
  - `mut x: T` (non-Copy) → **`ptr noalias %i`** — the borrow checker's aliasing-XOR-mutability rule proves uniqueness across the call (no other pointer in scope aliases this one). LLVM's optimizer can now reorder loads/stores aggressively, do dead-store elimination across calls, and unroll loops that would otherwise be blocked by aliasing assumptions.
  - `x: T` (non-Copy, shared) → **`ptr readonly %i`** — the callee provably can't write through the pointer (sema rejects writes; Drop is not registered on borrowed params per slice 5BC.codegen). Enables redundant-load elimination and read-reordering across calls without the soundness hazard of `noalias` (two shared args can be the same place per §2.9 — `f(x, x)` is admitted).
  - `move x: T` stays value-passed (the value is the transfer; no LLVM attribute).
  - Copy types stay value-passed regardless of marker (no aliasing constraint).
- **Two changes to `param_passes_by_ptr`**: the `_mutable` parameter is now consumed only for the attribute prefix; the pointer-pass decision now fires on **all** non-Copy struct params (shared and exclusive). Previously only `mut`-marked non-Copy was pointer-passed (slice 5BC.codegen); shared non-Copy was value-passed because the design-note said "no caller-visible difference under current sema." Phase 6 extends pointer-pass to shared because (1) `readonly` is a real performance unlock, and (2) the byte-copy on every shared-borrow call site is wasteful when the underlying place exists already at a known address.
- **New `param_attr_prefix(move_, mutable) -> &'static str`** returns `"noalias "` for `mut`, `"readonly "` for shared, `""` for `move`. Wired into `gen_function` and `gen_method` parameter emission. The attribute string is concatenated with `ptr`, trimmed of trailing whitespace, and emitted in the function signature.
  - **Why this is sound**: the borrow checker enforces (a) at most one `mut` borrow of a place at any program point (single-source 6BC.2 + multi-source 6BC.4 + intra-call 6BC.1); (b) shared borrows can multiply but the callee can't write through them (sema's mutability check). Together these match LLVM's `noalias` and `readonly` semantics exactly. Rust hit the LLVM `noalias`-on-`&T` soundness bugs around 2013–2014 and reverted; C+ ships only the sound subset (`readonly` for shared, `noalias` for exclusive).
  - **Tests updated** (1) + **added** (3):
    - Renamed and inverted `shared_param_noncopy_struct_stays_value_passed` → `shared_param_noncopy_struct_lowers_to_ptr_readonly`. The old assertion was wrong post-6BC.codegen; new test pins the `ptr readonly` shape AND asserts `noalias` doesn't appear (would be unsound).
    - Renamed `mut_param_noncopy_struct_lowers_to_ptr` → `mut_param_noncopy_struct_lowers_to_ptr_noalias` and tightened to assert the `noalias` qualifier.
    - 3 new e2e tests: `mut_param_tagged_noalias_in_ir`, `shared_param_tagged_readonly_in_ir` (also asserts NO `noalias` on shared), `copy_struct_param_stays_by_value_no_attr` (Copy fast path).
  - **Sanity bench**: still at clang -O2 parity on all four axes (build, size, run, RSS). Sum/fib/arr remain within noise. The bench programs don't exercise the non-aliasing optimizer paths that `noalias` actually unlocks (the three workloads are primitive-typed, no aggregate parameters); a follow-up bench with aggregate-mut-param-heavy workloads would show the real performance gain.
  - **Test total**: **656** (524 library + 121 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **What's deferred to 6BC.opt**: static drop-flag specialization (§5.4 of the design note) — read the analyzer's `PlaceState` at scope-exit points to specialize the runtime drop-flag mechanism. Definitely-moved → elide the drop; definitely-not-moved → unconditional drop. The runtime flag stays as the load-bearing fallback for `MaybePartial` cases. This is genuinely opportunistic — slice timing decides whether it lands now or slips to Phase 7+.
- **Phase 6 slice 6BC.5 (explicit `borrow REGION T` annotations) landed:** the spelling chosen in the design-note cleanup pass is now real syntax. `borrow` is a new reserved keyword; `borrow REGION T` parses in any type position (parameter types, return types, struct field types, including nested forms like `borrow A [B; 4]`). The annotation composes orthogonally with parameter markers — `xs: borrow A T` is a shared borrow in region A, `mut xs: borrow A T` is an exclusive borrow, and `move x: borrow A T` is a parse error (ownership transfer doesn't borrow; the annotation is meaningless on a moved parameter). New AST variant `TypeKind::Borrowed { region: String, inner: Box<Type> }`. Sema, codegen, and resolver all treat the variant as a transparent wrapper for the inner type — the region is borrow-checker metadata, not a runtime construct or a separate type at the LLVM level. The **borrow checker now consults annotations before falling through to elision rules**: a new `detect_fn_explicit_regions` runs at the head of `detect_fn_elision_with_flavor`, building the result from the annotation table when the return type is annotated. Sources = every parameter whose annotated region matches the return's region; flavor = Exclusive iff any contributing parameter is `mut`-marked, else Shared. Single-source collapses to `Param(N)`, multi-source uses `MultiParam(indices)`. This **resolves the E0384 user trap** from 6BC.4 — the diagnostic teaches `borrow REGION T`, and now adding that annotation makes the function compile. Test total: **653** (524 library + 118 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean.
