  - **Lexer**: new `TokenKind::Borrow`. Keyword string `"borrow"` mapped at the ident-lookup site. 1 new lexer unit test pins the keyword in context (`kinds("borrow A string")`).
  - **AST**: `TypeKind::Borrowed { region: String, inner: Box<Type> }`. Threaded through five exhaustive-match sites: `borrowck.rs` (CopyOracle's `definitely_non_copy` and `is_type_copy_internal` recurse into inner), `codegen.rs` (`ty_from` forwards), `resolver.rs` (`rewrite_type` recurses so `borrow A prefix::T` resolves correctly across files), `sema.rs` (`resolve_type` resolves to inner's `Ty`).
  - **Parser**: new branch in `parse_type` consuming `borrow`-ident-type. `parse_param` rejects `move x: borrow A T` with `ParseErrorKind::Unexpected`. 5 new parser unit tests covering happy path on parameter / return / struct field, `mut`-marker composition, `move`-rejection, and array-nesting (`borrow A [B; 4]`).
  - **Borrowck**: new `detect_fn_explicit_regions` returns `Some((source, flavor))` when the return type is `borrow REGION T` AND at least one parameter shares that region. Wired into `detect_fn_elision_with_flavor` as the first check — explicit annotations take precedence over body-flow elision (E1, E1-mut, E3, E3-mut). E0384 naturally doesn't fire on annotated functions because `return_borrow.is_some()` after explicit-region detection runs. 7 new borrowck unit tests: shared single-source, shared multi-source, exclusive (any-mut), disjoint-regions (only matching params contribute), E0384 suppression, multi-source borrow at call site (E0372 fires on move of either source), and explicit-takes-precedence-over-elision (`fn merge(a: borrow A B, b: borrow A B) -> borrow A B { return a; }` classifies as MultiParam([0, 1]) Shared, not E1's Param(0)).
  - **E2E**: 5 new e2e tests covering compile-and-link, multi-source borrow tracking, exclusive-flavor read rejection, parse-rejection of `move x: borrow A T`, and the headline win — the E0384-triggering function from 6BC.4 now compiles cleanly when the user adds the annotation.
  - **What's deferred to follow-up slices**: **E0385 (mismatched annotations)** — when a function's body returns a value not actually rooted at any parameter in the declared region. Phase-6 first cut is permissive: annotations are taken as truth; the body isn't cross-checked. A function with `borrow A B` return and a fresh-value return path compiles without warning. **E0386 (struct field requires annotation)** — when a struct field has a non-Copy borrow-typed value, sema should require an explicit annotation. Today the borrow-region machinery is parsed but sema doesn't enforce its presence on borrow-typed fields. **Variance enforcement** — design note §4.3 commits invariant/covariant/contravariant rules, but the sema-level check isn't wired yet; the rules are honored implicitly by the borrow checker's place-equality but not by explicit region-substitution checks. **`'static` / 'lifetime-of-program' regions** — design note §4.4 defers to Phase 7+ when string literals motivate it. None of these block the Phase-6 exit criterion ("a `VecI32` rejects iterator invalidation"); they're polish-on-the-annotation-surface items.
- **Phase 6 slice 6BC.4 (Rule E3-mut + E0384 emission) landed:** the multi-`mut`-param body-flow analysis half of the borrow checker. New `detect_fn_e3_mut` mirrors Phase 5's `detect_fn_e3`: a function with 2+ `mut`-marked non-Copy params returning non-Copy, where every `return EXPR;` is rooted at one of the parameters, classifies as `(ReturnBorrowSource::MultiParam(indices), BorrowFlavor::Exclusive)`. The detection order in `detect_fn_elision_with_flavor` becomes E1-mut → E1 → E3-mut → E3 so `mut`-marked params don't fall through to the shared classifier. Calling an E3-mut function records the result as borrowing from *every* parameter in the result's set; moving any of them while the result is live fires E0372 with the exclusive-flavor message refined in 6BC.2. **New diagnostic E0384** — fires when a multi-non-Copy-param + non-Copy-return function fails every elision rule AND has at least one return rooted at a parameter. The "rooted at param" trigger distinguishes the ambiguous case (some-rooted-some-not, where the user clearly wants borrowing but the body-flow analysis can't pick) from the fresh-value-on-every-path case (the return is genuinely owned, no annotation would help). E0384 carries a help suggestion referencing the `borrow REGION T` annotation that slice 6BC.5's parser will admit. **New signature-level pass `collect_e0384_diagnostics`** runs in `analyze_with_diags` after SigTable collection and before the per-fn body walk. It walks every fn / method, checks the E0384 conditions, and pushes the diagnostic to the shared diag stream. Methods route through `e0384_for_method` with the impl-block target included in the diagnostic's name. **New helper `any_return_rooted_at_param`** walks blocks / statements / expressions to detect "at least one rooted return" without disqualifying on the first unrooted one — distinct from Phase 5's `body_returns_only_rooted_at` which is all-or-nothing. Test total: **635** (511 library + 113 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **Unit tests added** (9): `e3_mut_fires_on_multi_mut_param_with_param_rooted_returns` (canonical `longest_mut` case classifies as `MultiParam([0, 1])` with Exclusive flavor), `e3_mut_does_not_fire_when_some_path_returns_fresh_value` (conservative disqualification), `e3_mut_does_not_fire_with_mixed_shared_and_mut_params` (require every param `mut`), `e0384_fires_on_multi_param_with_mixed_rooting`, `e0384_does_not_fire_when_no_return_is_rooted` (fresh-value case stays silent), `e0384_does_not_fire_when_e3_matches_cleanly` (regression — E3-matching functions shouldn't trigger E0384), `e0384_carries_annotation_suggestion` (suggestion text mentions `borrow REGION T`), `e0384_fires_on_method_with_mixed_rooting` (method path), `e3_mut_multi_source_borrow_at_call_site` (E0372 fires on move of either source while the result is alive — the cross-statement consequence of E3-mut's multi-source `live_borrows` entries).
  - **E2E tests added** (4): `e3_mut_longest_pattern_compiles_cleanly` (positive: the `longest_mut(mut a, mut b) -> B` pattern admits end-to-end through `cpc build`), `e3_mut_move_of_either_source_while_borrowed_rejected` (E0372 fires with exclusive flavor), `e0384_mixed_rooting_requires_annotation` (asserts `borrow REGION T` text appears in stderr), `e0384_does_not_fire_on_fresh_value_returns` (positive: always-fresh stays clean).
  - **What's deferred to 6BC.5**: the parser side of `borrow REGION T`. E0384 today teaches the syntax in its suggestion text, but the parser doesn't yet admit annotation; users hit E0384 with no way to fix until 6BC.5 lands. The diagnostic still carries informational value — agents reading the JSON output can recognize "this function needs annotation" and route around it rather than retrying with a syntactically-invalid annotation.
  - **What's deferred to 6BC.codegen**: `noalias` tagging on the underlying pointer for non-Copy `mut x: T` parameters. The borrow checker now proves uniqueness for both single-mut (E1-mut, slice 6BC.2) and multi-mut (E3-mut, this slice); codegen can light up `ptr noalias %i` once 6BC.5 settles the lifetime-annotation surface that will affect signature-time analysis.
- **Phase 6 slice 6BC.3 (partial-place activation) landed:** the `Place::projections` machinery — plumbed since Phase 5 5BC.1 but dormant through 6BC.2 — now drives both intra-call and cross-statement conflict detection. Two structural wins: (1) **disjoint sub-places admit** — `modify_both(p.left, p.right)` compiles cleanly where pre-6BC.3 it would have been rejected at the root level. (2) **partial-overlap rejects** — `write_pair(p, p.left)` and the cross-statement `let cur = cursor(p.left); peek_pair(p);` both fire **E0374** ("partial-place conflict"), the Phase-5-reserved code that activates here. New `PlaceOverlap::{Same, Contains, Contained, Disjoint}` enum and `Place::overlap` / `Place::conflicts_with` methods implement the projection-prefix check from design note §5.2: place A covers place B iff `A.root == B.root && A.projections` is a prefix of `B.projections`. New `place_from_expr(&Expr) -> Option<Place>` walker builds places from Field/Index chains; constant `IntLit` indices become `Projection::Index(n)`, non-constant ones coarsen to `Projection::AnyIndex`. **Intra-call refactor**: the per-error scanning loops from 6BC.1 collapsed into a single `check_intra_call_conflicts` + supporting `ArgClaim` / `ClaimKind` types. Each arg's claim is computed once; pairs walk the conflict matrix from design note §3.0. Direct-place pairs (Mut+Mut, Mut+Move, Move+Mut) emit E0380 / E0382 on same-place overlap and E0374 on partial overlap. Shared-read conflicts (Mut+Shared via sibling expression-tree scan, Move+Shared same) use the new `scan_overlapping_places` walker — it finds any place inside the sibling's expression that overlaps the primary's place, emitting E0370 / E0381 on same-place and E0374 on partial overlap. **Cross-statement refactor**: `record_read` scans `state` for *any* place rooted at the read's binding name that's in `BorrowedExclusive`, firing E0383 on Same overlap and E0374 on Contains/Contained. `check_move_against_borrow` scans `live_borrows` the same way, picking the first overlapping entry (BTreeMap iteration is deterministic). A new `record_place_read(&Place, ...)` variant handles Field/Index chains as places — without this, `peek(p.right)` would recurse into `apply_expr(p)` and mis-record as a read of the root `p`, which would conflict with a borrow of `p.left`. The Field/Index branch in `apply_expr` now builds the full place and dispatches to the place-aware variant when the chain is rootable. Test total: **622** (502 library + 109 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **Unit tests added** (11): `place_overlap_same`, `place_overlap_disjoint_roots`, `place_overlap_disjoint_sub_places`, `place_overlap_parent_contains_child` (covers both directions), `place_overlap_index_const_distinct`, `place_overlap_index_any_overlaps_const` (records the conservative Disjoint rule for AnyIndex+Index — precision improvement noted in design note §9), `partial_place_admit_disjoint_subfields_in_one_call` (positive: `modify_both(p.left, p.right)` admits), `e0374_partial_overlap_parent_with_subfield_in_one_call`, `e0374_cross_statement_read_of_parent_while_subfield_borrowed`, `e0374_does_not_fire_on_disjoint_subfield_cross_statement`, `place_from_expr_walks_field_chain` (constructs `Place { root: "p", projections: [Field("left"), Field("v")] }` from `p.left.v`).
  - **E2E tests added** (4): `disjoint_subfield_borrows_accepted_in_one_call`, `e0374_parent_and_subfield_in_one_call_rejected`, `e0374_cross_statement_subfield_borrow_blocks_parent_read`, `disjoint_subfield_cross_statement_accepted`.
  - **Dead code retired**: the 6BC.1 implementation used `expr_reads_ident` / `stmt_reads_ident` for the sibling-read scan. 6BC.3's `scan_overlapping_places` is more precise (operates on places, not just binding names). Both old helpers are marked `#[allow(dead_code)]` rather than deleted — they remain as a reusable building block for future passes that need binding-name-only lookups.
  - **What's deferred to a future precision-improvement slice**: `Projection::AnyIndex` vs. `Projection::Index(n)` is currently treated as Disjoint (different projection lists). The conservatively-correct rule would treat AnyIndex as overlapping with every Index value (the runtime index could be any). This rejects more programs than necessary; admitting it requires a const-eval pass to prove index distinctness. Recorded in design note §9.1 (under "open" pre-6BC.3 — closes now as "rule shipped is the conservative Disjoint; tighten when a real workload measures the cost").
  - **What's deferred to 6BC.4**: Rule E3-mut (multi-`mut`-param body-flow analysis). 6BC.3 handles partial-place at the analyzer level; multi-mut elision is its own logic.
  - **What's deferred to 6BC.5**: explicit lifetime annotations. E0384 still doesn't fire — Phase-5 E1-mut returns None when the body-flow analysis can't prove single-source, but no "annotation required" diagnostic surfaces yet. Slice 6BC.5 lands it.
- **Phase 6 slice 6BC.2 (cross-statement exclusive-borrow tracking) landed:** the borrow checker now establishes `BorrowedExclusive(borrower)` claims when a `let`-init returns an exclusive borrow (Rule E1-mut for free fns, Rule E2-mut for `mut self` methods), tracks them through scope, and rejects any access to the source place while the borrower is alive. New `BorrowFlavor::{Shared, Exclusive}` enum carries the flavor info; `FnEntry` widens with `return_borrow_flavor: Option<BorrowFlavor>` parallel to `return_borrow`. **Rule E1-mut detection**: exactly one `mut`-marked param (and not `move`), non-Copy param type, non-Copy return type, every `return EXPR;` rooted at the parameter — same shape as Rule E1 but for the exclusive flavor. **Rule E2-mut detection**: `Receiver::Mut` (i.e. `mut self`), non-Copy target, non-Copy return, every return rooted at `self`. Both detectors reuse Phase 5's `body_returns_only_rooted_at` walk. `classify_borrow_source` widens to return `(Vec<Place>, BorrowFlavor)`; `acquire_borrows` takes the flavor and sets `BorrowedShared(N)` or `BorrowedExclusive(borrower)` accordingly. `record_read` extends to fire **E0383** on `BorrowedExclusive` reads (skipping self-reads — reading the borrower itself is admitted). `check_move_against_borrow` extends to branch its message on flavor: a move while the borrow is exclusive emits **E0372** with "exclusively borrowed" wording instead of the Phase-5 "shared-borrowed" text. **Cascading-error suppression**: a new `record_move_arg_use` variant of `record_read` checks the MaybePartial (E0371) case only, suppressing E0383 — without this split, a move-arg of an exclusively-borrowed binding would fire BOTH E0383 and E0372 for one conflict; E0372 is the precise diagnostic. Test total: **607** (491 library + 105 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **Surface area**: no language change. Same `mut x: T` / `mut self` syntax that's been parsed since Phase 3 slice 3A; the borrow checker now tracks the lifetime contract that the §2.9 model promises. Two new public test hooks (`return_borrow_source_with_flavor`, `method_return_borrow_source_with_flavor`) expose the flavor pairing for unit tests.
  - **Unit tests added** (13): `e1_mut_call_records_exclusive_borrow_in_state`, `e2_mut_method_call_records_exclusive_borrow_in_state` (state-dump assertions: `v=BorrowedExclusive(cur)` after `let cur = cursor(v);`), `e0383_fires_on_read_of_exclusively_borrowed_place`, `e0383_does_not_fire_after_exclusive_borrower_scope_exits` (releases at scope close), `e0383_does_not_fire_on_borrower_itself` (self-conflict suppression), `e0372_message_refined_when_borrow_is_exclusive` (asserts both the new wording AND that E0383 doesn't double-fire), `exclusive_borrow_does_not_fire_on_copy_param` (Copy fast path), `e1_mut_classification_with_flavor` + `e1_shared_classification_with_flavor` (flavor recorded correctly), `e1_mut_does_not_fire_on_move_marker` (`move x: T` is not a borrow), `e0383_releases_when_exclusive_borrower_is_moved` (moving the borrower releases the source). Plus the two Phase-5 tests `e1_does_not_fire_with_mut_marker` and `e2_does_not_fire_on_mut_self` had their assertions inverted (the detector now fires with `Exclusive` flavor) and renamed to `e1_mut_fires_on_mut_marker_with_exclusive_flavor` / `e2_mut_fires_on_mut_self_with_exclusive_flavor` — the rename preserves the lesson while reflecting the new behavior.
  - **E2E tests added** (5): `e0383_read_of_exclusively_borrowed_place_rejected`, `e0383_does_not_fire_when_borrower_consumed_first` (positive: moving the borrower releases the borrow, subsequent read OK), `e0372_message_refined_when_borrow_is_exclusive` (asserts E0383 doesn't appear — single-diagnostic-per-conflict), `e2_mut_method_call_establishes_exclusive_borrow` (Rule E2-mut path through `cpc build`), `reading_the_exclusive_borrower_itself_accepted` (positive: borrower self-read works).
  - **What's deferred to 6BC.3**: partial-place activation via `Place::projections` — `modify_both(mut buf.left, mut buf.right)` should succeed, `mut buf` while `mut buf.left` is live should reject. Today the analyzer treats `buf.field` as a read of `buf`, so projection-aware conflict detection isn't yet wired in. The machinery's been plumbed since Phase 5 slice 5BC.1; 6BC.3 makes it live.
  - **What's deferred to 6BC.4**: Rule E3-mut (multi-`mut`-param body-flow analysis). E1-mut covers single-param; multi-mut returning a borrow of one specific param needs the same body-walk Phase 5's 5BC.4 did for shared.
  - **What's deferred to 6BC.5**: explicit lifetime annotations (`borrow REGION T`). Phase-5's E0384 path doesn't yet activate — E1-mut-on-failure today returns `None` rather than firing the "annotation required" diagnostic. The annotation surface lands as its own slice.
- **Phase 6 slice 6BC.1 (intra-call exclusive-borrow conflicts) landed:** the borrow checker now enforces three new aliasing-XOR-mutability families at call-evaluation granularity, completing the symmetric counterpart to Phase 5's E0370. New `PlaceState::BorrowedExclusive(String)` variant pays its own way in `PlaceState::merge` (same-borrower-both-branches → still exclusive; everything else → MaybePartial) and in `fmt_state`. `FnEntry` widens with `param_muts: Vec<bool>`; `SigTable::fn_param_muts(name)` exposes it. `apply_call` grows a second scan loop after the existing E0370 detection — for each `mut`-position argument naming a non-Copy binding, the loop checks every sibling argument: a `mut`-position sibling of the same binding fires **E0380** (mut-mut), a `move`-position sibling fires **E0382** (mut-move), any other read fires **E0381** (mut-shared). Each `mut`-arg fires at most one diagnostic to keep cascading errors out of a single conflict. The E0370 loop also gains a small suppression — when a sibling at a `mut`-position names the same binding, E0382 takes the diagnostic and E0370 is silenced, so the user sees one error for one conflict rather than two. All three new codes carry machine-applicable suggestions. Copy bindings are skipped at every gate — `mut x: i32` is local-mutability per §2.9, not a borrow. **Test total: 591** (480 library + 100 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **Unit tests added** (14): `e0380_fires_on_two_mut_borrows_of_same_non_copy_binding`, `e0380_does_not_fire_on_two_mut_copy_args`, `e0380_does_not_fire_on_different_bindings`, `e0381_fires_on_mut_arg_with_sibling_read`, `e0381_does_not_fire_on_copy_binding`, `e0382_fires_on_mut_arg_with_sibling_move`, `e0382_does_not_fire_when_other_arg_does_not_name_binding`, `e0382_suppresses_e0370_for_same_pair` (the cross-code suppression — exactly one E0382 fires, zero E0370), `e0380_e0381_e0382_carry_suggestions` (every new code attaches a `MaybeIncorrect` help-text), plus 5 merge tests covering `BorrowedExclusive` against every other state (same borrower → still exclusive, different borrowers → MaybePartial, vs Owned → MaybePartial both directions, vs BorrowedShared → MaybePartial both directions, fmt_state coverage).
  - **E2E tests added** (5): `e0380_two_mut_borrows_of_same_binding_rejected`, `e0381_mut_and_shared_borrow_in_same_call_rejected`, `e0382_mut_and_move_in_same_call_rejected` (asserts E0370 does NOT appear — single-diagnostic-per-conflict), `mut_borrows_of_different_bindings_accepted` (positive: distinct places admit two `mut` args), `mut_borrows_of_copy_type_accepted` (positive: Copy types pass through).
  - **What's deferred to 6BC.2**: method-call exclusive-borrow detection (`buf.bump()` where `bump` takes `mut self` — the receiver claim isn't yet routed through `mut_flags`); cross-statement exclusive-borrow tracking (the `let cur = cursor(mut vec); cur.advance(); vec.len();` family — needs the `BorrowedExclusive` state to be *established* by a let-init and *released* on borrower scope-exit, mirroring how 5BC.3b handles shared borrows). 6BC.1's static-analysis half is complete; 6BC.2's cross-statement form is the natural next slice.
  - **No language surface change.** No new keywords, no new syntax. The `mut` parameter marker that's been parsed since Phase 3 slice 3A is now actually enforced as an exclusive borrow at call sites. The diagnostic suggestions reference `borrow REGION T` annotations (per the slice-6BC.5 spelling decision) only in places where lifetime annotations would be the fix; 6BC.1 doesn't suggest them itself.
- **Phase 6 design-note cleanup pass** (this session): six §9 items that already had concrete answers in the body but were framed as "open" have been reframed as CLOSED — §9.5 (tagged-union variant projections lands alongside 6BC.3), §9.7 (mut-self field precision via 6BC.3 partial-place), §9.8 (self-referential structs deliberately rejected in Phase 6 first cut), §9.9 (re-borrow admitted as implicit sub-borrow, no surface syntax), §9.10 (`unsafe` non-interaction recorded), §9.12 (diagnostic prioritization is naive in 6BC.1–5, polish post-Phase-6). The remaining genuinely-open items are §9.3 (Atomic[T] interaction — sibling note's job) and §9.4 (drop-flag specialization slip risk — slicing-time call). Also fixed a factual error in §7's Atomic[T] paragraph that referenced `&` (which doesn't exist in C+); the correct phrasing is that `Atomic[T]` admits mutation through a shared `x: Atomic[T]` parameter. Added a conflict-matrix table at §3.0 — rows are place states, columns are operations, cells give code or state-transition. Captures every conflict the analyzer must enforce at-a-glance; supplements (not replaces) the prose in §§3.1–3.6.
- **Phase 6 lifetime annotation spelling decided: `borrow REGION T`** (this session). Three candidates were on the table — apostrophe-prefix lifetimes ('a T, Rust-shaped), `borrow A T` named regions (this choice), and `where return borrows ...` clauses (contract-style). The chosen form attaches at the type position (`xs: borrow A string`, `buf: borrow A Buffer` for fields) and composes orthogonally with the existing `mut` / `move` parameter markers — `mut xs: borrow A T` is the exclusive form, `move xs: T` admits no region (ownership transfer doesn't borrow). New reserved keyword: `borrow`. Region names are ordinary identifiers; convention is short uppercase (A, B) inline, descriptive when clarity helps (`borrow BUF Buffer`); names are local to one signature. **No function-level region declaration list** — unlike Rust's `<'a>`, region names introduce themselves at first use within the signature, which avoids the double-mention of every region and keeps the surface a single new keyword rather than a syntactic block. **Reasoning recorded in [phase6-borrow-exclusive.md](docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md) §4.2:** §2.8c "verbosity exposes hidden rules" argues for `borrow` over `'a` (the keyword tells a reader-without-context what the annotation means; `'a` is opaque until learned); the where-clause form separates the constraint from the parameters it constrains and risks confusion with Phase-7's `[T: Ord]` generic constraints. **Closing of the §9.6 `noalias`-on-shared question alongside (this session):** shared parameters lower to `ptr readonly %i`, never `ptr noalias %i`. The aliasing-XOR-mutability rule explicitly permits `f(x, x)` for a function taking `(a: T, b: T)`, so the underlying pointers genuinely can alias; `noalias` would be unsound regardless of analysis precision. Rust hit this and reverted `noalias` on `&T` for the same reason; only `&mut T` gets it. This is one fewer open question for slice 6BC.codegen. Diagnostic E0384 ("annotation required") now points at a concrete `borrow REGION T` recipe rather than a placeholder, so slices 6BC.1–6BC.4 produce useful diagnostics even before slice 6BC.5 lands the parser side. Phase-6 status stays 🟡 planning; one design decision moves from open to closed.
- **Phase 6 borrow-exclusive design note landed:** [docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md](docs/design/phase6-borrow-exclusive.md). Extends the Phase-5 borrow checker with the exclusive half: `mut x: T` / `mut self` on non-`Copy` types now establish a `BorrowedExclusive(name)` state that conflicts with *everything* (reads, writes, moves, shared borrows, additional exclusive borrows). Six conflict families specified — three intra-call (E0380 mut-mut, E0381 mut-shared, E0382 mut-move) plus E0383 (access-while-exclusively-borrowed across statements), plus tightening of the existing E0370–E0372 to consider exclusive claims. Rule E1-mut / E2-mut / E3-mut mirror Phase 5's E1/E2/E3 for `mut`-marked sources. **Three load-bearing extensions over Phase 5:** (1) the partial-place machinery (`Place::projections`) finally activates — `modify_both(mut buf.left, mut buf.right)` succeeds where `modify_both(mut buf, mut buf)` fails; the projection-prefix check resolves the "two borrows of different sub-places are independent" case. (2) Explicit lifetime annotations land for the cases inference can't solve (return borrow with ambiguous source, struct fields holding non-Copy borrows, cross-function threading). **Spelling decision deferred to slice 6BC.5** after the analysis surface is prototyped — three candidates enumerated in §4.2: Candidate A (apostrophe-named regions, Rust-shaped), Candidate B (`borrow A` keyword), Candidate C (`where return borrows xs, ys` clauses). (3) `noalias` parameter attribute on the underlying LLVM pointer for every proved-unique `mut x: T` — the performance unlock that lets borrow-checked C+ outperform equivalent C, where compilers can't assume non-aliasing without `restrict`. Codegen change is one line per call site; the borrow checker's signature analysis is the real work. Diagnostic surface adds E0380–E0386 (E0374 is the Phase-5-reserved partial-place code that activates here). Slicing: 6BC.1 (BorrowedExclusive state + intra-call detection) → 6BC.2 (cross-statement exclusive tracking E0383) → 6BC.3 (partial-place activation) → 6BC.4 (multi-mut-param elision Rule E3-mut + E0384 annotation-required diagnostic) → 6BC.5 (explicit annotation spelling + E0385/E0386) → 6BC.codegen (`noalias` tagging) → 6BC.opt (static drop-flag specialization, opportunistic). 12 open questions recorded — biggest is the spelling decision; others cover iterator-invalidation prototyping (verify a `Vec[T]` rejects the canonical pattern *before* 6BC.5 lands), self-referential lifetime structs (Phase-6 first cut rejects, lift later), re-borrow within mut borrow (admitted as a sub-borrow — Rust's reborrow pattern, implicit in C+ syntax), Phase-6 shared parameters and `noalias` (default: don't tag; revisit if a workload measures the cost), and `unsafe`-block placement (still reserved for Phase 10 C-interop — historically "Phase 8" before strings and identity-exploration phases were inserted). Implementation blocked on Phase 5 being done (✅ as of this session) and on the lifetime-spelling prototype (slice 6BC.5).
- **Phase 5 ✅ done.** All settled features land:
  - Design notes: phase5-borrow-shared (5BC), phase5-attributes (5ATTR), phase5-doctests (5DOC).
  - Borrow checker: 5BC.1 (place-state machinery) · 5BC.2a (Copy oracle + E0370 pipeline wiring) · 5BC.2b (flow-sensitive branch merging + E0371) · 5BC.3a (Rule-E1/E2 elision detection) · 5BC.3b (call-site borrow tracking + E0372) · 5BC.4 (Rule-E3 multi-parameter elision; `fn longest(...)` accepts under elided lifetimes) · 5BC.codegen (§2.9 mut-borrow pointer ABI for non-Copy `mut x: T`).
  - Attributes + `cpc test`: 5ATTR.1 (parser + AST + validation E0354–E0357) · 5ATTR.2 (sema E0358/E0359 + `attrs::discover_tests`) · 5ATTR.3 (`assert EXPR;` statement) · 5ATTR.4 (`cpc test [--json]` subcommand + synthesized driver `main`).
  - Doctests: 5DOC (pre-parser source-level `///` fence extraction; synthesized `#[test] fn __doctest_<item>_<idx>` functions; design-note `DOC_TEST::<qualified>::<idx>` display name via `attrs::discover_tests`).
  - Exit met (per design note §1 and Phase 5 §3 last paragraph): (a) `fn longest(xs: B, ys: B) -> B` accepts under elided lifetimes; (b) using a moved value while a shared borrow of the same place is alive is a compile error (E0372); (c) `cpc test --json` runs the test suite for any in-tree program (single-file *and* project-mode); (d) §2.9 mut-borrow pointer ABI lands so non-Copy `mut x: T` writes propagate back to the caller. Test total at Phase-5 close: **572** (466 library + 95 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **Carried to Phase 6+** (not blocking the Phase-5 exit criteria): 5BC.5 partial-place tracking + E0374 — surface syntax for partial moves doesn't exist in Phase 5 (sema's E0337 rejects `move x.field` before borrowck sees it), so the `Place::projections` machinery is plumbed but unused. Lifts naturally when Phase 6's mut-borrow exclusivity rules motivate finer-grained tracking, *or* when a future surface change admits partial moves; 5BC.6 borrow-checker diagnostic polish — current diagnostics already carry machine-applicable suggestions plus primary spans; deferring an additional sweep to whenever a real user-facing case demands sharper messaging; LSP polish (completions / hover / find-references / rename / inlay hints, filesystem watcher, pull diagnostics, cross-file `WorkspaceEdit`); editors beyond VS Code; multi-binding `guard let`; 4D.2 formatter reformatting heuristics; `?*T` / slices (need raw pointers, which still wait on motivating use cases). Source-line attribution for failing asserts (design note §6.3 q3): the test-runner output reports which *test* failed, not which *line* of the test — wiring span data through assert lowering is straightforward but cosmetic.
- **Phase 5 slice 5DOC (doctest extraction) landed:** new module [cplus-core/src/doctest.rs](cplus-core/src/doctest.rs); pre-parser source-level pass that scans `///` doc-comment blocks for triple-backtick fences and appends one synthesized `#[test] fn __doctest_<item>_<idx>() { <body> }` per fence. The synthesized fns flow through the regular lex/parse/lower/sema/borrowck/codegen pipeline, exactly like hand-written `#[test]` fns; `attrs::discover_tests` recognizes the `__doctest_` leaf prefix and reformats the display name to the design-note's `DOC_TEST::<qualified>::<item>::<idx>` form for human + JSON output. Single-file and project-mode both wire extraction in (single-file via `cpc/src/main.rs:build_ir`/`build_program`; project-mode via `cplus-core/src/resolver.rs` before tokenize). 16 new doctest unit tests + 6 new e2e tests covering extraction, name synthesis, multiple fences per block, doctest failure surfacing through the runner, doc-comments-without-fences staying inert, and `cpc build` still working on files with fences. Test total at slice close: **572** (466 library + 95 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored.
  - **Design-note deviations recorded for honesty.** (1) The design note specifies the synthesized function name as `DOC_TEST::<item>::<idx>` — that contains `::`, which is path syntax, not identifier characters. Source-level rewriting needs a valid C+ identifier, so the synthesized name is `__doctest_<item>_<idx>` and only the *display* name (in human/JSON test output) uses the `DOC_TEST::` form. The user never types the underscored form; it's an internal symbol. (2) The design note's §3.4 span-attribution promise — diagnostics into a doctest fence point at the user's `///` line — is **not** delivered. Source-text rewriting appends the synthesized fn at the end of the file, so diagnostics into the synthesized region point at the appended position, not the original doc-comment line. The design note itself flags this attribution as a follow-up and accepts it for the first cut. (3) The design note explores both a token-rewrite hook and an AST-rewrite hook (§6); source-text rewrite was picked because it minimizes the surface area (one new module, no lexer/parser changes) at the cost of the span fidelity above. Either alternative is achievable when span attribution becomes important.
  - **What's deferred:** span-stable extraction (token- or AST-level rewriting per design note §6); `ignore` / `no_run` / `compile_fail` fence tags (note §5 open question 1); auto-`import` of the documenting file under a prefix (note §5 q2); `assert`-source-line attribution (note §5 q3); empty-fence treatment (note §5 q4 — currently produces a vacuous always-pass test); the hidden-imports `#`-prefix convention (note §5 q6).
- **Phase 5 slice 5ATTR.4 (`cpc test` subcommand + driver synthesis) landed:** new subcommand `cpc test [FILE] [--json]` (single-file when FILE is given; project-mode when reading `./Cplus.toml`). Pipeline: load + sema + borrowck the program (same as `cpc build`), call `attrs::discover_tests`, hand the test list to a new codegen entry `generate_test_binary(program, mode, tests, json)` that emits the project IR *and* a synthesized `main`. The synthesized `main` zeroes a per-test failure flag (`@cpc_test_failed`), calls each test in source order, OR-s the i32 return (for `fn() -> i32` tests) into the flag check, prints one pass/fail line per test (human or JSON per `--json`), tracks pass/fail counts in stack-allocated counters, prints a summary, and returns the fail count as the process exit code (clamped into u8). Two key changes feed into this:
  - **`assert` becomes mode-dependent in codegen.** `FnState` gains a `test_mode: bool`; `gen_assert` branches on it. In non-test builds (the slice 5ATTR.3 path) assert still emits `br i1 cond, ok, trap; trap: call @llvm.trap(); unreachable`. In test builds the false-path block writes `store i32 1, ptr @cpc_test_failed` then falls through to the ok label — Phase 5 has no raw pointers, so continuing past a failed assertion can't segfault, and a flag write is cheaper than synthesizing a default-typed `ret` per function. The driver `main` reads the flag *after* each test call to decide pass/fail.
  - **User's `main` is suppressed in test mode.** `generate_inner` skips emitting any `fn main` from the user's program; the synthesized test-driver `main` is the linker's only `@main`. A user's `main` returning 42 doesn't leak into the test binary's exit code.
  - 7 new e2e tests: `cpc_test_runs_passing_tests`, `cpc_test_reports_failing_test`, `cpc_test_json_output` (validates per-test + summary JSON shape), `cpc_test_no_tests_zero_exit`, `cpc_test_i32_return_form`, `cpc_test_calls_helper_functions` (non-test helpers still emitted), `cpc_test_skips_user_main`. Existing 543 tests stay green.
  - **What's deferred to 5DOC / Phase 6+:** doctest-as-discovered-tests (the next slice); `--json` per-test `duration_ms` and `reason` fields (design-note §4.4 enumerates the full shape; the Phase-5 first cut emits only `name` + `result` + summary `passed`/`failed`); `assert`-source-line attribution into the JSON (a separate `cpc_runtime_assert_failed` intrinsic that records span data; design note §6.3 q3); parallel test execution (single-process serial run is acceptable for Phase 5; parallel matters when test suites get large); test-discovery directory conventions (`tests/` subdir) for projects that grow many tests.

- §1.1 ABI-only via `extern fn`; bindgen as separate future tool
- §1.2 Rust as the compiler implementation language
- §1.2 No comptime
- §1.2 Full borrow checker, phased across Phases 3/5/6
- §1.2 Wrap on release overflow, trap on debug
- §1.2 C11 memory model + borrow checker prevents data races; volatile via functions
- §2.7 Comma operator removed (operator only); separator stays in arg lists, struct literals, and `for` headers
- Language name: **C+**
- Source file extension: `.cplus`
- `for` loop: both C-style `for (init; cond; update)` (parens required) and range/iterator `for x in 0..n` / `for x in coll`
- Statement terminator: semicolons
- Function keyword: `fn`
- Variable declaration: `let` (immutable by default), `let mut` for mutable
- Range syntax: `..` exclusive, `..=` inclusive
- Block expressions: blocks evaluate to their last expression (Rust-style)
- Phase 1 grammar drafted: see [docs/design/phase1-grammar.md](docs/design/phase1-grammar.md)
- §2.8 No function overloading
- §2.8 No operator overloading (skipped entirely; named methods for arithmetic-like types)
- §2.8 No `any`-type / dynamic escape hatch
- §2.8 No glob imports as default
- §2.8 No inheritance
- §2.4 / §2.8 / §2.8b — **No `try`, no `!T` error type.** Errors are plain tagged unions; users write `match` explicitly. Driven by FFI honesty (no surface syntax that implies machinery the ABI doesn't carry) — the same reason C++ exceptions can't cross FFI cleanly.
- §2.8b FFI honesty principle: no surface syntax that implies machinery the ABI doesn't carry. Gates future feature additions.
- §2.8c Verbosity is acceptable: C+ is optimized for LLM-as-primary-writer, so explicit + locally-complete beats short-but-magic. Already informs §2.4, §2.8a, §2.8.
- §5.1 Compiler-as-library: cplus-core (library) + cpc (binary) + cpc-lsp (binary), all sharing the same library
- §5.2 Structured diagnostics from Phase 1 (JSON output, machine-applicable suggestions)
- §5.3 Determinism guaranteed (BTreeMap, sorted iteration, no timestamps in artifacts)
- §5.4 Built-in subcommands: `build`, `check`, `parse`, `fmt`, `test`, `lsp`
- §5.6 Doctests in scope (Phase 5; design note required)
- §5.7 Editions: deferred until we need a second one; intent recorded
- Library/binary split landed: cplus-core + cpc separate crates
- Phase 1 lexer landed: 14 unit tests, all green
- Phase 1 parser landed: 13 unit tests, all green
- Phase 1 diagnostics infrastructure landed: see [docs/design/diagnostics.md](docs/design/diagnostics.md), 8 unit tests + structured `--diagnostics=json|short|human` flag
- Phase 1 sema landed: 14 error codes E0300–E0313, 29 unit tests
- Phase 1 codegen landed: 19 unit tests; alloca+mem2reg strategy; all four samples emit IR; debug-mode overflow trapping (`llvm.{sadd,ssub,smul}.with.overflow.i32` + `llvm.trap`); always-on divide-by-zero trap; `BuildMode::Debug` (default) vs `BuildMode::Release`
- Phase 1 driver landed: `cpc FILE [-o OUT]` runs full pipeline; `cpc --release` / `--debug` mode flags; 13 e2e tests including 4 sample programs, runtime overflow trap verification, runtime div-zero trap verification, and release-mode wrap behavior
- **Phase 1 complete: 102 tests, 0 warnings, all 4 sample programs compile + run; overflow traps in debug, wraps in release; div-zero always traps.**
- Phase 2 slice 1 (types + casts) landed: full primitive type set; 17 new sema tests; 17 new codegen tests; 3 new sample programs (mixed_ints, float_arith, unsigned); E0315 invalid cast, E0316 float modulo. Test total: **143** (127 library + 16 e2e), 0 warnings.
- Phase 2 slice 2A (plain enums + paths) landed: `enum Name { V1, V2, ... }`; two-segment path expressions `Name::Variant`; `Ty::Enum(EnumId)`; cross-enum types distinct; equality but no ordering; `enum as i32` cast; design note [docs/design/phase2-enums.md](docs/design/phase2-enums.md); 13 new sema tests; 4 new codegen tests; 1 new sample program (direction); E0317 unknown variant, E0318 duplicate variant. Test total: **162** (145 library + 17 e2e), 0 warnings.
- Phase 2 slice 2B (structs, no methods) landed: `struct Name { f: T, ... }`; struct literals `Name { f: e }`; field read `p.x`; field assignment with mutable-root walk (`l.to.x = 5` works when `l` is `let mut`); struct-literal-vs-block disambiguation (no struct literals in `if`/`while`/`for-in` heads without parens); pass-by-value as fn params and returns; forward references between structs; design note [docs/design/phase2-structs.md](docs/design/phase2-structs.md); 19 new sema tests; 7 new codegen tests; 3 new sample programs (point, mutable_struct, nested); E0319 duplicate field, E0320 unknown field, E0321 missing field, E0322 extra field, E0323 non-struct field access. Test total: **193** (173 library + 20 e2e), 0 warnings.
- Phase 2 slice 2C (methods + `impl`) landed: Rust-style `impl Type { fn method(...) }`; three receiver forms (`self`, `&self`, `&mut self`); name mangling `Type::method` → `@Type.method`; `value.method()` and `Type::method()` call dispatch in both sema and codegen; resolved §11 open question on method syntax. Design note [docs/design/phase2-methods.md](docs/design/phase2-methods.md); 15 new sema tests; 7 new codegen tests; 1 new sample program (methods); E0324 no method, E0325 impl on non-struct, E0326 duplicate method, E0327 wrong call form, E0328 `&mut self` on non-mut place. Test total: **217** (196 library + 21 e2e), 0 warnings.
- Phase 2 slice 2D (fixed-size arrays) landed: `[T; N]` types; `[e1, e2, ...]` literals; bounds-checked `a[i]` indexing via `icmp uge` + `llvm.trap`; indexed assignment via place-walk extension; arrays as fn params, returns, struct fields; `Ty: Copy → Clone` refactor (~50 small clones); 2 new sample programs (array_sum, array_struct); E0329–E0332 error codes; deferred slices+raw pointers to Phase 3/5. Test total: **236** (212 library + 24 e2e), 0 warnings.
- **Phase 2 ✅ done.** All four slices landed; slice 2E (slices + raw pointers) deferred to Phase 3/5 where the borrow-checker brings in references.
- **Style migration (post-Phase 2)** landed: §2.8a style rules now enforced. Function bodies use explicit `return` (E0333 rejects implicit tail). Method receivers use `self`/`mut self` syntax — `&` removed from the language. All 14 sample programs rewritten. `Point::magnitude` renamed to `Point::magnitude_squared` (precise naming rule). Receiver enum collapsed: `Receiver::Value/Ref/RefMut` → `Receiver::Read/Mut`; codegen now always pointer-passes for receivers. Test count after migration: **234** (210 library + 24 e2e), 0 warnings.
- **Phase 3 slice 3A (ownership surface syntax + move tracking) landed:** `move` keyword; parameter markers `x: T` / `mut x: T` / `move x: T`; receiver `move self`; `Ty::is_copy()` (primitives + enums); move tracking with E0335 use-of-moved and E0337 move-from-non-binding; design note [docs/design/phase3-ownership.md](docs/design/phase3-ownership.md); 1 new sample (ownership.cplus); 17 new sema tests + 10 new parser tests + 3 new e2e tests. Codegen pointer-pass for non-Copy params deferred to Phase 6 alongside `noalias` (§7a). Test total: **263** (236 library + 27 e2e), 0 warnings.
- **Phase 3 slice 3B (wrapping operators `+% -% *%`) landed:** integer-only wrapping arithmetic; emits plain `add/sub/mul` regardless of build mode; sema rejects wrapping ops on floats (E0302); 1 new sample (wrap_arith.cplus); 3 new sema tests + 2 new codegen tests + 2 new e2e tests. Test total: **269** (240 library + 29 e2e), 0 warnings.
- **Phase 3 slice 3C (Copy auto-derive) landed:** structural rule — aggregate `Copy` iff every component is `Copy`. `Ty::is_copy()` → `SemaCx::is_copy(&Ty)` with `is_copy` flag cached per `StructDef`; fixpoint computation pass between fields and methods. Move tracking gates correctly on the new rule. Design note [docs/design/phase3-copy-derivation.md](docs/design/phase3-copy-derivation.md); 1 new sample (copy_struct.cplus); 5 new sema tests + 1 new e2e test. 6 slice-3A move tests + 2 e2e tests moved to `#[ignore]` until a non-Copy aggregate type exists (predicted in design note §6.3). Test total: **267** (239 library + 28 e2e), 6 ignored, 0 warnings.
- **Bench sanity check landed:** `cpc --release` was passing IR to clang without `-O`, producing 100×+ slower binaries than necessary. Fixed (now passes `-O2` in release / `-O0` in debug). Three micro-benchmarks (sum, fib, arr) confirm parity with `clang -O2`. Numbers and code in [bench.md](bench.md). The "C+ beats C on aliasing" story still rests on Phase-6 `noalias`.
- **Phase 3 slice 3D (literal-suffix codegen fix) landed:** codegen's `gen_expr` was returning `Ty::I32` for every integer literal regardless of suffix, producing invalid IR for array literals like `[10u8, ...]` (wrong element type) and arithmetic on suffixed literals like `1u64 +% 2u64` (computed in i32, stored as i64). Fixed; 2 regression codegen tests. Test total: **269** (241 library + 28 e2e), 6 ignored, 0 warnings.
- **Phase 3 slice 3E (Drop design note) landed:** [docs/design/phase3-drop.md](docs/design/phase3-drop.md) — magic `fn drop(mut self)` method; reverse-order scope-exit; drop flags suppress dropping of moved-out bindings; Drop forces non-Copy; `defer` and drop share a single LIFO stack.
- **Phase 3 slice 3F (Drop implementation) landed:** `is_drop` flag on `StructDef`/`StructInfo`; codegen scope-frame Drop list; per-binding `i1` drop flag; conditional drop at scope exit + on `return`; move events flip flags; destructor bodies opt out of self-drop; 2 new samples (`drop_basic.cplus`, `drop_move.cplus`); 5 sema tests + 2 e2e tests for Drop; **8 dormant slice-3A tests revived** (empty `fn drop(mut self) {}` is the non-Copy idiom). New error code: E0338 (wrong drop signature). Bench parity preserved. Test total: **284** (252 library + 32 e2e), 0 ignored, 0 warnings.
- **Phase 3 slice 3G (`defer`) landed:** lexical `defer EXPR;` statement; unifies with Drop in a single LIFO scope-exit stack (codegen's `drop_scopes` became `scope_exits` with `Drop` / `Defer` variants); 2 new samples (`defer_basic.cplus`, `defer_drop.cplus`); 3 sema tests + 2 e2e tests. Test total: **289** (255 library + 34 e2e), 0 warnings.
- **Phase 3 slice 3H (tagged unions design note) landed:** [docs/design/phase3-tagged-unions.md](docs/design/phase3-tagged-unions.md). Extends `enum` with positional payloads; `match` expression with exhaustiveness; tagged-union LLVM layout (`{ i32 tag, [N x i8] payload }`); Copy auto-derive extends structurally to variant payloads; Drop on payloads forbidden in Phase 3 (E0344) until heap types motivate it. Implementation deferred to slice 3I.
- **`!T` / `try` rejected (post slice-3H discussion):** errors are plain tagged unions; users write `match`. FFI honesty (§2.8b) + LLM-as-primary-writer (§2.8c) are the two locked-in principles driving this. Verbosity acceptable; no language-level error machinery. The tagged-unions slice (3H/3I) is also the error-handling surface — no separate slice needed.
- **Phase 3 slice 3I (tagged unions + `match` implementation) landed:** extends `enum` with positional payloads; `match` expression with variant/wildcard/binding patterns; exhaustiveness checking; LLVM lowering as `{ i32 tag, [N x i64] payload }` (plain enums stay bare-`i32`); 2 new samples (`maybe.cplus`, `shape.cplus`); 11 new sema tests + 3 new e2e tests. Error codes E0340–E0344 now active. Test total: **303** (266 library + 37 e2e), 0 warnings.
- **Phase 3 slice 3J (definite assignment) landed:** `let x: T;` now legal; sema's flow-sensitive analysis verifies every read is preceded by an assignment on every control-flow path. New `assigned: bool` flag on `LocalInfo`; snapshot/restore/intersect helpers do flow merging at `if`/`else` and `match` arms; loops are conservative. First write into an unassigned binding is allowed without `mut` (the initialization site); subsequent writes need `mut`. New error codes: E0345 (use of possibly-unassigned binding), E0346 (uninit `let` needs type annotation). 1 new sample (`uninit_init.cplus`); 8 new sema tests + 2 new e2e tests. Test total: **313** (274 library + 39 e2e), 0 warnings.
- **Phase 3 ✅ done.** Settled features: 3A (ownership syntax + move tracking), 3B (wrapping ops), 3C (Copy auto-derive), 3D (literal-suffix codegen fix), 3E/3F (Drop), 3G (`defer`), 3H/3I (tagged unions + `match`), 3J (definite assignment). Deferred to Phase 5/6: `?*T` and slices (need raw pointers / borrow checker).
- **Phase 4 modules design note landed:** [docs/design/phase4-modules.md](docs/design/phase4-modules.md). Filesystem-driven (`src/foo.cplus` = module `foo`; `src/foo/bar.cplus` = `foo::bar`); `use foo::Item` imports with no globs allowed; `pub` keyword with default-private for items, fields, and methods; `Cplus.toml` manifest minimum is `[package]` + `[[bin]]`; whole-program compilation in Phase-4 minimum (separate compilation is later polish); `impl` block must live in the same module as its type. Sliced 4A (manifest + multi-file driver) → 4B (`use` + visibility) → 4C (cycle detection + E0401–E0410 diagnostics). Implementation slices not yet started.
- **Phase 5 sequencing + attributes principle locked in (Phase-5 kickoff):** three decisions, written to §3 Phase 5 and §2.8d.
  - **Sequencing**: design notes first (borrow-shared, attributes, doctests), then borrow checker, then attributes + `cpc test`, then doctests, then LSP polish. Rationale: risk concentration — the borrow checker is the only Phase-5+ work whose design might retroactively invalidate earlier slices. Doing it first means every later slice gets to assume stable borrow semantics. Earlier "tooling-first" lean retracted: the test loop helps borrow-checker *users*, not its construction; negative tests (programs that must fail with E0xxx) drive BC development, and the Phase 1–4 infrastructure already handles those.
  - **Lifetime elision** designed from C+'s actual surface, not ported from Rust. Rust's elision exists because `&T` everywhere is unreadable; C+ has no `&T` so the elision motivation differs. Bias: elide less rather than more in Phase 5 — conservative-now-relax-later is a one-way door; permissive-now-tighten-later is a migration.
  - **Attributes as a general extension point** (§2.8d), declarative-only. `#[test]` is the first instantiation; the `test fn` vs `#[test]` open question resolves in favor of `#[test]`. Hard rule: attributes carry no expression-level compile-time computation. `#[derive(Eq)]`-style code-synthesis attributes rejected; structural auto-derive (as we already do for `Copy`) is the alternative when interfaces land in Phase 7.
- **Phase 4 ✅ done.** All settled features land:
  - Slice 4A (manifest + multi-file driver) · Slice 4A.5 (`if let` / `guard let`) · Slice 4B (`pub` visibility) · Slice 4C (field-pub + parser polish + per-file source threading + E0401–E0410 polish) · Slice 4D (`cpc fmt` preserving formatter) · Slice 4E.1 (LSP skeleton + diagnostics) · Slice 4E.2 (LSP formatting + code-actions) · Slice 4E.3 (LSP goto-definition) · Slice 4-end (break/continue/loop/while-let + cross-file variant patterns + 5-file `calc` sample).
  - Exit met: 5-file project builds, fmt round-trips every sample, LSP serves diagnostics + formatting + jump in VS Code. Test total at Phase-4 close: **414** (335 library + 68 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored.
  - Carried to Phase 5+: 4D.2 formatter reformatting heuristics; 4F `cpc test --json` (design-blocked on `#[test]`); multi-binding `guard let`; LSP polish (filesystem watcher, pull diagnostics, cross-file `WorkspaceEdit`, completions / hover / find-refs / rename / inlay hints); editors beyond VS Code.
- **Phase 5 slice 5ATTR.3 (`assert EXPR;` statement + lowering) landed:** new `assert` keyword + statement form runs end-to-end through the pipeline; sema rejects non-bool conditions (E0302), codegen branches on the value and traps on the false path. Phase-5 trap-only behavior; slice 5ATTR.4 will swap the trap for a per-test failure-flag write inside synthesized test-driver builds. Test total: **543** (450 library + 82 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **Lexer**: new `TokenKind::Assert` (`assert` keyword). 1 new lexer unit test.
  - **AST**: new `StmtKind::Assert(Expr)`. Threaded through every stmt-walking site: parser, sema, lower, resolver, borrowck (four sites), codegen.
  - **Parser**: new `parse_assert_stmt` — `assert EXPR ;`. Dispatched from the statement-loop alongside `defer` / `break` / `continue`. 2 new parser unit tests (positive shape + missing-`;` rejection).
  - **Sema**: in `check_stmt`, an `Assert(e)` calls `check_expr(e, Some(Ty::Bool))` and emits **E0302** ("`assert` condition must be `bool`, got `…`") if the actual type isn't `Bool` or `Error`. Reuses the general type-mismatch code so the diagnostic shape matches every other type-error position. 3 new sema unit tests (bool clean, i32 condition rejected, float condition rejected).
  - **Codegen** ([cplus-core/src/codegen.rs](cplus-core/src/codegen.rs)): new `gen_assert(cond)` emits `br i1 %v, label %ok, label %trap` + a trap block (`call void @llvm.trap()` + `unreachable`) + the ok continuation. 2 new codegen unit tests (the IR shape + assert in a `#[test]` fn).
  - **Multi-pass plumbing**: borrowck (E3 returns walk, single-root returns walk, `apply_stmt`, `stmt_reads_ident`), lower (`lower_stmt`), and resolver (`rewrite_stmt`) all gained an `Assert(e)` arm that recurses into the expression. No behavioral change in those passes — `assert` is a leaf statement that wraps a single expression.
  - **E2E**: 3 new e2e tests drive `cpc build`:
    - `assert_true_runs_to_completion` — `assert 1 == 1; assert 2 + 2 == 4; println(42);` exits 0 with stdout `42\n`.
    - `assert_false_traps_at_runtime` — `assert 1 == 2; println(999);` exits non-zero and stdout never contains `999` (the trap fires before the print).
    - `assert_non_bool_rejected_e0302` — `assert 42;` fails sema with E0302 in stderr.
  - **What's deferred to 5ATTR.4**: the test-driver-aware lowering. Today `assert` always traps; under `cpc test` the synthesized driver needs `assert` to set a per-test failure flag and return early so the runner can report which test failed and keep running the rest. The codegen helper `gen_assert` is the only site that needs to switch on the test-build mode — design note §4.5 spells out the per-test failure-flag approach (set a global `i32`, return from the function, runner reads the flag after the call). Source-line attribution for the failing assert is also future work (§6.3 open question 3).
- **Phase 5 slice 5ATTR.2 (sema-level `#[test]` validation + discovery) landed:** sema now rejects test fns with wrong signatures (E0358) or `pub` markers (E0359); a new `attrs::discover_tests` pass walks the merged Program after sema to produce the `Vec<TestFn>` the upcoming `cpc test` driver (5ATTR.4) will consume. Test total: **530** (442 library + 79 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean.
  - **Sema validation** (`check_test_attribute_rules` in [cplus-core/src/sema.rs](cplus-core/src/sema.rs)): runs at the top of `check_function`, gated on `f.attributes` containing a `#[test]`. Both diagnostics carry the *attribute* span as primary so error highlighting points at the `#[test]` line, not the surrounding fn signature.
    - **E0358** — signature shape. Required: empty params + return type ∈ `{Ty::Unit, Ty::I32}`. Anything else (params present, return type bool/struct/enum/etc.) fires. Sema uses the already-resolved `FnSig` so type-name mistakes route through earlier sema errors first.
    - **E0359** — `pub` rejection. `#[test] pub fn t() { ... }` fires; non-test `pub fn` is unaffected (the rule is gated on the `#[test]` attribute, not on `pub` itself).
    - **E0360 (sema-level `impl` placement) deliberately not emitted** — the attrs pass (5ATTR.1) already rejects `#[test]` on methods via E0356, so a sema-level check would be unreachable defense-in-depth. Code reserved by the design note for future use; this slice's docstring records the choice.
  - **`attrs::discover_tests(prog: &Program) -> Vec<TestFn>`** ([cplus-core/src/attrs.rs](cplus-core/src/attrs.rs)): pure-data pass, no diagnostics — callers expected to have run `attrs::check` and `sema::check` first. Returns `TestFn { qualified_name, display_name, origin_file, returns_i32, span }` in source order:
    - `qualified_name` is the resolver's `.`-flavored form (e.g. `src.math.adds_one`) — the same backbone codegen uses for mangling.
    - `display_name` converts `.` → `::` for human + JSON output (`src::math::adds_one`); resolves design-note §6 open question 1 in favor of the `::` form users see in source.
    - `returns_i32` distinguishes the two accepted signatures so the driver knows whether to capture an exit code vs. just call-and-return.
  - **Tests added** (8 sema unit + 6 attrs unit + 2 e2e = 16):
    - Sema: `test_fn_with_no_return_clean`, `test_fn_with_i32_return_clean` (both accepted shapes), `test_fn_with_param_rejected_e0358`, `test_fn_with_wrong_return_type_rejected_e0358` (bool return), `test_fn_pub_rejected_e0359`, `test_fn_pub_and_wrong_signature_emits_both` (independent rules fire together), `non_test_fn_with_pub_is_clean`, `non_test_fn_with_param_is_clean` (gate is the attribute — non-test fns are unaffected).
    - Discovery: `discover_tests_finds_single_test`, `discover_tests_ignores_unmarked`, `discover_tests_preserves_source_order`, `discover_tests_captures_return_type_kind`, `discover_tests_display_name_uses_double_colon` (mutates the parsed AST to simulate the resolver's `.`-qualified form and pins the `::` conversion), `discover_tests_empty_when_no_tests`.
    - E2E: `test_attribute_bad_signature_rejected_e0358`, `test_attribute_pub_rejected_e0359` — both drive full `cpc build` and assert the code appears in stderr.
  - **What's deferred to 5ATTR.3 / 5ATTR.4**: `assert EXPR;` statement form, lowering, and `cpc_runtime_assert_failed` intrinsic (5ATTR.3); `cpc test` subcommand + driver synthesis that consumes `TestFn` + `--json` output (5ATTR.4).
- **Phase 5 slice 5ATTR.1 (attribute parser + AST + validation) landed:** the `#[NAME]` / `#[NAME(args)]` surface lands across lexer, parser, AST, and a new validation pass; `cpc build` / `cpc check` / `cpc-lsp` all now reject unknown or misplaced attributes with structured diagnostics before lower / sema run. Phase 5 ships exactly one known attribute (`#[test]`); other names are E0354 with a did-you-mean. Test total: **516** (428 library + 77 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean; sanity bench at clang -O2 parity on all four axes (build, size, run, RSS).
  - **Lexer:** new `TokenKind::Pound` for `#`. Two new lexer unit tests pin the token and the `#[test]` sequence shape.
  - **AST:** new `Attribute { path: Ident, args: Vec<AttrArg>, span }` + `AttrArg::{Ident, Str, KeyValue}` + `AttrValue::{Ident, Str}`. Item-bearing nodes (`Function`, `StructDecl`, `EnumDecl`, `StructField`, `EnumVariant`, `Method`) each gain `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` — empty when none precede the declaration. `ImplBlock` deliberately does not carry attributes (per design note §6 open question 6); the parser rejects `#[...]` immediately before `impl`.
  - **Parser:** new `parse_attributes()` consumes zero or more `#[...]` blocks at item-start position; called from `parse_item`, `parse_method`, and inline before each struct field / enum variant. Attributes appear before `pub` in source order (the canonical form per the design note's examples). `parse_attr_arg` admits all three Phase-5 shapes (bare ident, string literal, `key = value`); only `#[test]` (no-arg) is actually used today, but the grammar is forward-compatible. 9 new parser unit tests cover each shape + each placement + the impl-block rejection.
  - **Validation pass** ([cplus-core/src/attrs.rs](cplus-core/src/attrs.rs)): single-file `check` + multi-file `check_multi` entry points mirroring sema's interface. Table-driven via `KNOWN_ATTRS: &[AttrSpec]` — each entry declares name, arg shape, target bitmask, allow-duplicate flag. Phase 5 has one row (`test`); adding `#[inline]` / `#[ignore]` later is a one-row patch + design note. Rules enforced:
    - **E0354 (unknown attribute)** — fires on any name not in `KNOWN_ATTRS`. Did-you-mean suggestion via a small inline Levenshtein (distance ≤ 2; cap kept consistent with the resolver's E0401 cutoff). `#[tset]` → "did you mean `#[test]`?" (`MaybeIncorrect`).
    - **E0355 (wrong arg shape)** — `#[test(slow)]` → "attribute `#[test]` takes no arguments."
    - **E0356 (wrong target)** — placement off the spec's bitmask. `#[test]` is FN-only; struct / enum / method / field / variant placements each fire E0356 with the legal-targets list in the message.
    - **E0357 (duplicate)** — `#[test] #[test]` → fires once on the second occurrence (per-attribute `seen` map). Spec's `allow_duplicate` gate keeps the rule extensible (future `#[link(...)]`-style attrs that stack will set it true).
  - **Pipeline wiring:** both `cpc/src/main.rs` invocation sites (project-mode `cpc build` + single-file mode) and both `cpc-lsp/src/main.rs` sites (manifest project mode + open-file single-file mode) now call `attrs::check` / `attrs::check_multi` between parse and lower. Failure is hard-stop on `Severity::Error`; diagnostics render via the same `--diagnostics=json|short|human` pipeline as sema and borrowck.
  - **Tests added** (13 attrs unit + 9 parser unit + 2 lexer unit + 3 e2e = 27): attrs unit covers happy path + each negative for E0354/E0355/E0356/E0357 + did-you-mean fires + did-you-mean doesn't over-fire on distant names + multi-attribute independent validation + struct-field / enum-variant placements + primary-span pin. Parser unit covers each AttrArg shape + each placement + `pub`-ordering + impl-block rejection. Lexer unit pins `#` alone and the `#[test]` sequence. E2E drives full `cpc build`: `unknown_attribute_rejected_e0354`, `test_attribute_on_struct_rejected_e0356`, `test_attribute_clean_compile` (positive — `#[test]` parses through end-to-end, no consumer yet so the binary just runs `main`).
  - **What's deferred to 5ATTR.2 / 5ATTR.3 / 5ATTR.4**: sema validation of the `#[test]` function signature (E0358 `fn() -> i32` or `fn()`), `pub` rejection on test fns (E0359), `impl`-placement rejection at the sema layer (E0360 — currently fires from attrs as E0356, but the design note reserves E0360 for the sema-level check); test discovery pass walking the merged Program; `assert EXPR;` statement + lowering; `cpc test` subcommand + driver synthesis + JSON output. Those are the next three slices in order.
- **Phase 5 slice 5BC.codegen (§2.9 mut-borrow pointer ABI) landed:** non-Copy `mut x: T` parameters now lower to a `ptr` LLVM parameter, bound directly to the SSA argument (no alloca, no initial store, no callee drop registration). Call sites take the source's address via `gen_place(arg)`. Caller now observes the callee's writes — the §2.9 exclusive-borrow contract holds at runtime. Test total: **488** (403 library + 74 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. 28 sample programs still compile and run clean; sanity bench at clang -O2 parity on all four axes (build, size, run, RSS).
  - **Scope kept narrow**: only `mut x: T` non-Copy struct params change. Three cases stay value-passed:
    - `x: T` non-Copy shared borrow — under current sema the callee cannot mutate, so the value-copy is observationally equivalent to a pointer borrow. Deferred to Phase 6 where pointer-passing pairs with `noalias` on `mut` and the design note's `noalias`-on-shared question resolves.
    - `move x: T` — ownership transfer; the by-value copy is the transfer, caller's drop-flag flip suppresses the caller-side drop, callee registers its own scope-exit drop. Unchanged.
    - Copy `mut p: P` — §2.9 says "mut on Copy is local mutability, not a borrow." The value-copy with local mutations is exactly the spec. New negative e2e test pins this.
  - **Implementation surface**:
    - `TypeTable::struct_defs[..].is_copy` and `TypeTable::enum_defs[..].is_copy` added; mirrors sema's Copy fixpoint via `compute_copy_flags` (new, runs at the end of `collect_types`). Free helper `is_copy_ty(ty, types)` walks arrays and consults the per-id flags. Codegen no longer asks sema this question — sema is still the source of truth for diagnostics; codegen now answers ABI questions on its own.
    - `FnSig::params` and `MethodInfo::params` tuples widened from `(Ty, bool)` to `(Ty, bool, bool)` — third field is `mutable`. Wired through `collect_sigs` and the method-table builder. Existing tuple-destructure sites in `gen_function`, `gen_method`, `gen_named_call`, `gen_method_call`, `gen_assoc_call` updated.
    - New predicate `param_passes_by_ptr(ty, move_, mutable, types) = mutable && !move_ && matches!(ty, Struct(_)) && !is_copy_ty(ty, types)`. Fires only on `Ty::Struct` — arrays of non-Copy elements deliberately excluded for this slice (no current sample exercises them; the symmetric fix lands when the first one shows up).
    - Param-emission and call-site loops branch on the predicate. Ptr branch: header writes `ptr %i`, callee binds directly to `%i`, no drop registration; call site takes `gen_place(arg)` and emits `ptr <addr>`. Value branch: unchanged from before.
  - **Retraction of 5BC.3b's "latent double-drop" claim.** Below in that slice's entry the codegen caveat states that today's by-value pass for non-Copy non-move params causes both caller and callee to drop the same logical value, with empty `fn drop` bodies masking the breakage. **That claim was wrong.** Empirical test (`/tmp/drop_param_test.cplus` with a Drop body that prints `-id`) showed exactly one drop, because `register_drop` is already gated on `*move_flag`. The real user-visible bug was different: `mut x: T` on a non-Copy struct couldn't propagate field writes back to the caller (callee mutated a byte-copy). The previous entry's framing led to a wider planned scope than the actual bug required — this slice ships only the narrower fix and leaves shared-borrow pointer-pass to Phase 6. The 5BC.3b entry stays as written so the wrong premise is preserved as a lesson record.
  - **Tests added** (7 unit + 3 e2e):
    - Unit: `mut_param_noncopy_struct_lowers_to_ptr` (signature shape), `shared_param_noncopy_struct_stays_value_passed`, `move_param_noncopy_struct_stays_value_passed`, `mut_param_copy_struct_stays_value_passed`, `mut_param_noncopy_struct_no_alloca_in_callee` (no stray re-alloca in the body), `mut_param_noncopy_struct_no_double_drop` (no `@Tag.drop` inside callee), `mut_param_noncopy_struct_via_method_call` (non-receiver method param hits the same ABI).
    - E2E: `mut_param_noncopy_struct_mutation_propagates` (runtime regression: prints 11, not 10 — the runtime witness for §2.9 exclusive-borrow), `mut_param_copy_struct_does_not_propagate` (negative: Copy semantics preserve caller's value), `mut_param_noncopy_struct_no_double_drop_at_runtime` (drop body prints `-id` exactly once across the call boundary — was the supposed "double-drop" bug 5BC.3b claimed).
  - **What's still deferred**: shared non-Copy pointer-pass + `noalias` on `mut` (Phase 6); non-Copy *arrays* as mut params (will fix when needed); the borrow-checker flow merging of `live_borrows` across branches (5BC.5/5BC.6 polish).
- **Phase 5 slice 5BC.4 (Rule E3 multi-parameter elision) landed:** delivers the design note's Phase-5 exit criterion — `fn longest(xs: B, ys: B) -> B { ... }` accepts under elided lifetimes, and moving either input while the return-binding is alive fires E0372.
  - **New variant `ReturnBorrowSource::MultiParam(Vec<u32>)`** records the union of parameter indices each return path roots at. `ReturnBorrowSource` is no longer `Copy` (it carries a Vec); call sites updated to `.clone()` / pattern-match by ref where needed.
  - **`detect_fn_e3`** runs after `detect_fn_e1`. Qualifies a function iff: ≥ 2 parameters, every param non-Copy shared-borrow (no `mut`, no `move`), non-Copy return type, every `return EXPR;` rooted at *some* parameter (paths may differ on which one). The roots-set is the union of those parameter indices. Returns of fresh-constructed values on any path disqualify (conservative per design note §4.1: "elide less rather than more"). Also classifies single-root multi-param functions (e.g. `fn pick(a, b) -> B { return a; }` → `MultiParam([0])`) — the design note doesn't distinguish "all paths return same param" from "different paths return different params" once you're past the two-param threshold.
  - **`check_block_returns_e3` / `check_stmt_returns_e3` / `check_expr_returns_e3`** walk every block / statement / expression, identifying each `return EXPR;` and inserting the rooted param's index into the running set. Recursive over all C+ control-flow constructs (`if`, `match`, `while`, `for`, `loop`). Mirrors the E1 body-walk shape.
  - **`expr_root_ident`** new helper: given a chain of field/index projections, returns the root binding name (or None for non-place expressions). Used by E3 detection and `place_from_arg`.
  - **Multi-source borrow tracking** — `binding_borrows_from` changed from `HashMap<String, Place>` to `HashMap<String, Vec<Place>>`. `acquire_borrow` → `acquire_borrows(places: Vec<Place>, ...)` deduplicates and inserts the borrower into every source's `live_borrows` set. `drop_borrower` releases from every recorded place. E0372 still fires the moment ANY source is moved.
  - **`classify_borrow_source` returns `Vec<Place>` instead of `Option<Place>`** — empty for non-borrow calls, single-element for Rule E1 / E2, multi-element for Rule E3. The `apply_stmt::Let` path checks `!borrow_sources.is_empty()` before calling `acquire_borrows`.
  - **Tests**: 7 new unit tests + 1 new e2e + 1 updated. New: `e3_fires_on_longest_pattern` (the canonical case), `e3_call_records_borrows_from_every_source` (state dump shows both `a` and `b` BorrowedShared(1)), `e3_fires_e0372_on_move_of_any_source` + `e3_fires_e0372_on_move_of_other_source` (symmetric move-while-borrowed), `e3_does_not_fire_when_some_path_returns_fresh_value`, `e3_does_not_fire_with_copy_param`, `e3_does_not_fire_with_move_param`, `e3_borrow_released_after_borrower_scope_exits`. Updated: `e1_does_not_fire_with_multiple_params` was asserting `None` — now correctly asserts E3 fires with `MultiParam([0])` for `fn pick(a, b) -> B { return a; }`. E2E: `longest_move_either_input_while_borrowed_rejected` in [cpc/tests/e2e.rs](cpc/tests/e2e.rs) — the design-note exit criterion compiled end-to-end through `cpc build`. **Test total: 478** (396 library + 71 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. All 24 sample programs still compile clean.
  - **Phase 5 exit met for borrow checking** (the static analysis half): `fn longest(...) -> ...` accepts; using a moved value while a shared borrow of it is alive is a compile error. The full Phase-5 exit also requires `cpc test --json` (deferred to the post-BC tooling slices) and the codegen fix surfaced in 5BC.3b's caveat (separate slice).
  - **What's deferred to 5BC.5 / 5BC.6 / 5BC.codegen**: partial-place tracking through field / index projections (E0374); diagnostic polish (the 5BC.6 sweep); flow merging of borrow state across branches (a borrow established in one branch and not the other isn't currently snapshotted through `merge_branches` — needs `live_borrows` to participate in the merge); codegen fix for non-Copy non-move param passing (still passes by value, latent double-drop on Drop structs).
- **Phase 5 slice 5BC.3b (call-site borrow tracking + E0372) landed:** consumes 5BC.3a's elision detection to record per-call borrows and fire the first lifetime-aware diagnostic. **Also retracts the sema-interaction blocker claim from the 5BC.3a entry** — empirical check shows sema's `check_arg_with_move` only marks bindings moved when `expected.move_ && !is_copy(ty)`. Non-move non-Copy params don't trigger sema's move tracker; `let y = passthrough(x); return x.x;` compiles cleanly under sema today. The blocker described in 5BC.3a's history entry was incorrect; that paragraph stands as a record of the wrong premise so the lesson sticks.
  - **New analyzer state**: `live_borrows: BTreeMap<Place, BTreeSet<String>>` (per-place set of currently-live borrower names) + `binding_borrows_from: HashMap<String, Place>` (back-pointer for scope-exit cleanup). When `let r = f(x);` and `f` is Rule-E1, `r` joins `live_borrows[x]` and `x`'s state becomes `BorrowedShared(N)`. Method calls (`let r = b.method();`) use the same machinery with Rule-E2's `SelfReceiver` source.
  - **`classify_borrow_source(expr)`** inspects a `let`-init expression. For Rule E1: plain `Ident` callee whose `SigTable` entry has `return_borrow == Some(Param(i))` → returns the place rooted at arg-i (when that arg is a plain `Ident`). For Rule E2: `Field { receiver: Ident, name: method }` where the receiver's recorded binding-type names a struct/enum whose `Type.method` SigTable entry has `return_borrow == Some(SelfReceiver)` → returns the receiver's place.
  - **Scope-exit cleanup**: `walk_block_in_scope` now releases borrows held by branch-local bindings before the `state.retain` step. Each dropped binding's borrow (if any) is removed from `live_borrows`; the source place's `BorrowedShared(N)` decrements (or restores to `Owned` when N hits 0).
  - **Move-arg path also releases**: when a non-Copy binding is moved out via a `move`-marked arg, any borrow it was holding gets released; any borrowers of *it* get their `live_borrows` entry cleared (E0372 already fired for them, and the moved binding is no longer a valid source).
  - **E0372 — move while shared-borrow live**: `check_move_against_borrow` looks up `live_borrows[Place::root(name)]` in the move-arg path before transitioning to `Moved`. If non-empty, emits E0372 naming the lexicographically-first borrower (stable via `BTreeSet`). Each E0372 carries a `MaybeIncorrect` suggestion describing the two fixes ("drop the borrower before moving, or clone").
  - **Tests**: 6 new unit tests + 1 new e2e. Unit: `e1_call_records_borrow_in_state` (state dump shows `x=BorrowedShared(1)` after `let y = passthrough(x);`), `e2_method_call_records_borrow_in_state` (same for `let r = b.pass();`), `e0372_fires_on_move_while_e1_borrow_live` (the canonical pattern), `e0372_does_not_fire_after_borrower_scope_exits` (scope-cleanup correctness), `e0372_does_not_fire_on_copy_param` (Copy fast path), `moving_borrower_releases_borrow` (moving the borrower allows subsequent moves of the source). E2E: `move_while_return_borrow_live_rejected` in [cpc/tests/e2e.rs](cpc/tests/e2e.rs) drives the full pipeline through `cpc build` and asserts E0372 in stderr. **Test total: 469** (388 library + 70 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored. All 24 sample programs still compile clean.
  - **Codegen caveat surfaced (not blocking 5BC.3b's analysis, recorded for awareness):** the test program in `e1_call_records_borrow_in_state` exposes a latent codegen issue with non-Copy non-move parameter passing. Today codegen passes non-Copy aggregates by value, which means the function copies the struct bytes and the caller's binding is bit-identical to the callee's. For Drop structs this means both caller and callee end up dropping the same logical value; the Phase-3 empty-`drop`-body samples mask the breakage. The §2.9 model says non-Copy `x: T` is a shared borrow — codegen should pass it by pointer, not by value, when borrowck has classified it as a borrow flow. This codegen fix is a separate slice (call it 5BC.codegen) and is independent of the static analysis 5BC.3b just landed.
  - **What's deferred to 5BC.3c / 5BC.4 / 5BC.5**: E0373 (return of borrow from moved-in param — design note says `fn f(move x: T) -> Bytes { return x.field; }`, but sema's E0337 already rejects partial moves so this trigger is already covered by an earlier error). Rule E3 multi-parameter elision (the `longest(a, b)` case) — 5BC.4. Partial-place tracking through field / index projections — 5BC.5. Flow merging of borrow state across branches (currently `acquire_borrow` doesn't snapshot/restore through `merge_branches` — a borrow established in one branch and not the other isn't currently flow-merged; needs the same machinery `live_borrows` shares with the state map). The codegen fix above.
- **Phase 5 slice 5BC.3a (Rule E1 + Rule E2 elision detection) landed:** signature analysis only — no new diagnostics, no call-site state changes, pure analysis-surface growth. Builds the inference machinery that 5BC.3b will consume.
  - **New `ReturnBorrowSource` enum**: `Param(u32)` or `SelfReceiver`. Records which input a non-Copy return semantically borrows from under the design note's elision rules.
  - **`SigTable` restructured**: replaced the bare `HashMap<String, Vec<bool>>` with `FnEntry { param_moves, return_borrow }`. Methods now have a parallel `BTreeMap` keyed `Type.method`.
  - **`SigTable::collect(prog, &CopyOracle)`** runs the elision detection during collection.
  - **Rule E1 (`detect_fn_e1`)** matches iff: (1) exactly one param, (2) shared-borrow form (no `mut`, no `move`), (3) param type is provably non-Copy via `CopyOracle::definitely_non_copy`, (4) return type is non-Copy, (5) every `return EXPR;` in the body has EXPR being a path rooted at the parameter's binding (recursive `expr_is_path_rooted_at` walks field / index projections back to the root `Ident`). Returns of fresh-constructed values (`return B { x: 0 };`) disqualify — the conservative rule per design note §4.1.
  - **Rule E2 (`detect_method_e2`)** matches the same shape but for methods: `Receiver::Read` (not `mut`, not `move`), non-Copy impl-target type, non-Copy return, every `return EXPR;` rooted at `self`.
  - **Body-walk helpers** (`body_returns_only_rooted_at` / `check_*_returns`) traverse blocks, statements, and expressions — including `if`/`match`/`while`/`for`/`loop` — and require every `return EXPR;` to satisfy the root predicate. At least one return must exist (no all-divergent / infinite-recursion fns qualify).
  - **Public test hooks** `return_borrow_source(prog, fn_name)` and `method_return_borrow_source(prog, target, method)` expose the analyzer result so unit tests pin detection without observable behavior change.
  - **Tests**: 14 new unit tests. Positive: E1 on `fn passthrough(b: B) -> B { return b; }`, E1 on `fn pull(o: Outer) -> Inner { return o.inner; }` (field access rooted at param), E2 on `fn pass(self) -> B { return self; }`, E2 on `fn payload(self) -> Inner { return self.inner; }`. Negative: E1 rejects fresh-value return, Copy param, `move` marker, `mut` marker, multi-param, no-return-type, mixed-root returns; E2 rejects `mut self`, `move self`, Copy target. Plus `detection_does_not_emit_diagnostics_in_isolation` — the pipeline `check()` entry emits nothing on E1/E2 candidates today. **Test total: 462** (382 library + 69 e2e + 11 LSP), 0 warnings, 0 ignored.
  - **What's deferred to 5BC.3b**: (1) call-site borrow tracking — when `let r = f(x);` and `f` has `return_borrow = Some(Param(0))`, record `r` as borrowing from `x`; introduce `BorrowedShared` state for `x`; track live-borrow scope. (2) **E0372 (move-while-shared-borrow-live)** — fires when `x` is moved while `r` is live. (3) **E0373 (return-of-borrow-from-moved-in-param)** — function-body check rejecting `fn f(move x: T) -> Bytes { return x.field; }` (borrow would dangle past the function frame). (4) Method-call borrow tracking (`b.payload()` returning a borrow of `b`).
  - **Sema-interaction blocker (recorded for 5BC.3b/5BC.3c, not blocking 5BC.3a):** sema today treats `f(b: B)` as moving `b` for non-Copy `B`, even when `f` takes `b` as a shared borrow per §2.9. This is sema's pre-Phase-5 conservatism — it predates the borrow checker. Until sema either (a) defers to borrowck for non-Copy parameter passing or (b) is taught the §2.9 shared-borrow rule, the pipeline rejects programs like `let r = passthrough(x); use(x);` with sema's E0335 before borrowck's E0372 can fire. Resolving this is its own slice. 5BC.3a's signature analysis is unblocked and lands cleanly; the call-site machinery in 5BC.3b will need this sema work either as a prerequisite or as a co-landing change.
